Eid Prayer: Wajib on Those Obliged for Jumu'ah
Ruling statement with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer and identify the conditions under which it becomes wajib.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib for the same individuals who must perform Jumu'ah — free Muslim men who are residents.

This lesson examines the ruling of Eid prayers ('Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha) in the Hanafi school. The text establishes that the obligation of Eid prayer is tied to the conditions of Jumu'ah: only those for whom Jumu'ah is wajib are required to pray Eid. The passage also provides two Quranic proofs to support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the legal status of Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school as presented in the text: it is wajib (obligatory, not fard) in the most sound opinion.
Note the phrase 'fi al-asahh' indicates a preferred view within the school.
2
Determine the qualifying condition
Identify who is obligated: the text says Eid prayer is wajib on those upon whom Jumu'ah is wajib. Recall the conditions for Jumu'ah: free male, resident (muqim), healthy, not excused.
Thus women, travelers, and those excused from Jumu'ah are not obliged to pray Eid.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
Locate the two verses: Surah al-Baqarah 2:185 (takbir after completing fast) and Surah al-Kawthar 108:2 (pray and sacrifice). Understand how tafsir links them to Eid prayers.
The command to glorify Allah (takbir) is interpreted as the takbir of Eid al-Fitr; the command to pray is interpreted as Eid al-Adha prayer.
4
Note the madhhab debate
Acknowledge that some Hanafi authorities (e.g., Imam Muhammad) considered Eid prayer sunnah, but the text declares the majority opinion as wajib.
Other schools like Shafi'i classify it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
5
Apply the conditions
Confirm that the conditions for Jumu'ah (free male resident, healthy) apply equally to Eid prayer, excluding women, travelers, and the sick from obligation.
These are the same conditions mentioned in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العيدين (۸۱۴) صلوة العيد واجبة فى الاصح على من تجب عليه الجمعة
ضروری نوٹ: عید کی نماز واجب ہے۔ زمانہ جاہلیت میں لوگ عید مناتے تھے۔ بعد میں اسلام میں بھی اس کو برقرار رکھا۔ (۱) اس کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے۔ ولتكملوا العدة ولتكبروا الله على ما هداكم ولعلكم تشكرون (آیت ۱۸۵ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) تفسیر طبری میں ہے کہ اس آیت میں عید الفطر میں تکبیر کہنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اسی آیت کے شروع میں روزے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ جس سے عید الفطر کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔ (۲) اور فصل لربك وانحر. ( آیت ۲ ،سورۃ الکوثر ۱۰۸) اس آیت میں تذکرہ ہے کہ پہلے عید الاضحی کی نماز پڑھو پھر جانور کی قربانی کرو۔ اس لئے دونوں آیتوں سے عید الفطر اور عیدالاضحی کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۸۱۴) جس پر جمعہ واجب ہے اس پر عید کی نماز واجب ہے، اصبح روایت میں ۔ تشریح : جن لوگوں پر جمعہ کی نماز واجب ہے انہیں لوگوں پر عید کی نماز بھی واجب ہے، کیونکہ دونوں کی شرائط ایک ہی ہیں، مثلا مرد پر جمعہ واجب ہے تو عید بھی واجب ہے، اور عورت پر جمعہ نہیں ہے تو عید بھی نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the Two 'Eids. (814) The 'Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) in the most sound opinion on those upon whom Jumu'ah is wajib. Necessary note: 'Eid prayer is wajib. In the time of Jahiliyyah, people used to celebrate 'Eid. Later, in Islam, it was retained. (1) Its proof is from this verse: 'And that you complete the period and glorify Allah for that [to] which He has guided you; and perhaps you will be thankful.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185). Tafsir al-Tabari mentions that this verse mentions the takbir on 'Eid al-Fitr because at the beginning of the verse fasting is mentioned, which indicates 'Eid al-Fitr. (2) And 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice [to Him alone].' (Surah al-Kawthar 108:2). This verse mentions that first pray the 'Eid al-Adha prayer, then sacrifice the animal. So from both verses, proof of 'Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha is established. Translation: (814) 'Eid prayer is wajib on those upon whom Jumu'ah is wajib, in the most sound opinion. Explanation: The people on whom Jumu'ah is wajib, 'Eid prayer is also wajib on them, because the conditions of both are the same. For example, Jumu'ah is wajib on men, so 'Eid is also wajib on them; Jumu'ah is not wajib on women, so 'Eid is also not wajib on them.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with Quranic evidence. The ruling: 'Eid prayer (both 'Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha) is wajib on those individuals for whom Jumu'ah is wajib. In the Hanafi school, the conditions for Jumu'ah being wajib are: being a free male, resident (muqim), and healthy (not excused). Therefore, women, travelers, and the excused are not obliged to perform 'Eid prayer. The text then provides two Quranic proofs: Surah al-Baqarah 2:185, which mentions completing the fast and then glorifying Allah, indicating 'Eid al-Fitr; and Surah al-Kawthar 108:2, which orders prayer and sacrifice, indicating 'Eid al-Adha. The phrase 'in the most sound opinion' (fi al-asahh) indicates that there is some debate within the Hanafi school, but this is the relied-upon position. The commentator stresses that the conditions for obligation are identical for both prayers.

Key Terms
العيد (al-'Eid): The two Islamic festivals: 'Eid al-Fitr (after Ramadan) and 'Eid al-Adha (during Hajj).
واجب (wajib): Obligatory but less than fard; established with zanni dalil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on whom is 'Eid prayer wajib?
A) All Muslims, male and female
B) Those on whom Jumu'ah is wajib
C) Only men
D) Only women

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib on every free, healthy, resident Muslim man – exactly those who are obligated for Jumu'ah.

Sadaqat al-Fitr Before Eid Prayer
Ruling and proof for paying sadaqat al-fitr before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of sadaqat al-fitr and explain the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-fitr is wajib; giving before Eid prayer is preferred, but delay does not drop the obligation.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the Hanafi ruling on sadaqat al-fitr, focusing on its timing relative to the Eid prayer. It affirms the obligation is permanent—even if one misses the preferred time, the duty remains and must be fulfilled later. The proof is the well-known hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet commanded giving before the people go out to prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification. The passage explicitly calls it 'wajib'.
The text says 'if it is wajib'—Hanafis consider it wajib, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The author quotes the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah made zakat al-fitr obligatory... and commanded that it be given before the people go out to the prayer.'
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith supports the ruling. The word 'farada' indicates obligation; the command 'an tu'adda' indicates the preferred timing.
The command for timing is understood as recommendation (mandub), not obligation, because the text itself distinguishes between the duty (farada) and the time (amara).
4
Apply the ruling
What does the ruling mean in practice? One should give before Eid prayer if possible; if not, the obligation remains and must be given later.
The text says: 'if he could not, the wajib is not dropped; rather he must give it later.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۱۸) [۲] صدقۃ الفطر ادا کرے اگر واجب ہو۔
رض
صلى الله
تشریح عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے صدقہ فطر ادا کرے تو بہتر ہے، اور اگر نہ کر سکا تو واجب ساقط نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بعد میں بھی ادا کرنا ہوگا وجه : عن ابن عمر قال : فرض رسول الله لا لا لا لا زكاة الفطر صاعا من تمر أو صاعا من شعير على العبد و الحر و الذكر و الانثى و الصغير و الكبير من المسلمين ، و أمر بها أن تؤدى قبل خروج الناس الى الصلاة
Translation of (818): [2] He gives sadaqat al-fitr if it is wajib. Explanation: It is better to give sadaqat al-fitr before going to the Eid prayer ground. If he could not, the wajib is not dropped; rather he must give it later. Reasoning: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made zakat al-fitr obligatory, a sa' of dates or a sa' of barley upon the slave and free, male and female, young and old among the Muslims, and he commanded that it be given before the people go out to the prayer.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of sadaqat al-fitr in relation to Eid prayer. The text states that it is wajib (obligatory) and that it should preferably be given before proceeding to the Eid prayer ground. If one fails to do so, the obligation does not drop; it must be fulfilled later. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed zakat al-fitr and commanded it to be given before people go out for the Eid prayer. The Hanafi school holds that sadaqat al-fitr is wajib upon every free Muslim who possesses nisab, and it is recommended to give it before the Eid prayer to fulfill the sunnah timing.

Key Terms
صدقۃ الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan
واجب (wajib): Obligatory, less than fard in the Hanafi classification

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred time for giving sadaqat al-fitr according to this passage?
A) After Eid prayer
B) Before going to the Eid prayer ground
C) At any time during Ramadan
D) Only on the day of Eid after prayer

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-fitr is wajib, and the preferred time is before the Eid prayer; if delayed, the obligation remains.

Giving Charity on Eid: The Recommendation and Its Proof
Ruling and proof for increasing charity on Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving charity on Eid and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Giving sadaqah on Eid is mustahab, not wajib; the proof is the Prophet's encouragement of generous giving.

Eid is a day of joy and gratitude. The Hanafi school teaches that increasing voluntary charity on Eid is a recommended act, drawing on the example of the Prophet who inspired women to give generously after the Eid prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text instructs 'giving charity according to capacity' on Eid. Determine the legal category (fard, wajib, mustahab, etc.) based on the language used.
The text uses 'ziyada sadqa karna' (increase charity) without a command implying obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Bukhari. Identify the key elements: the Prophet's action and the women's response.
Understanding the chain and context helps assess the strength of the evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Show how the hadith indicates desirability: the Prophet specifically addressed women, and they responded by donating jewelry, indicating enthusiastic compliance.
The hadith is zanni in both thubut and dalala, supporting a non-obligatory ruling.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules it mustahab. Check the pre-populated hanafi_position_box for details.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf reported; the mufta bihi is mustahab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۲۰)[۸] اپنی طاقت کے اعتبار سے زیادہ صدقہ کرنا۔
وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورتوں نے زیادہ سے زیادہ صدقہ کیا۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال سمعته يقول قام يوم الفطر فصلى فبدأ بالصلاة ثم خطب فلما فرغ نزل فأتى النساء فذكر هن و هو يتوكأ على يد بلال و بلال باسط ثوبه يلقى فيه النساء الصدقة قلت لعطاء زكاة يوم الفطر ؟ قال لا و لكن صدقة يتصدقن حينئذ تلقى فتخها و یلقین ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب موعظة الامام النساء یوم العید ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۹۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورتیں صدقہ کرتیں تھیں۔
Translation of (820): [8] Giving charity according to one's capacity. Reasoning: (1) In this hadith, women gave a lot of charity. From Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: He (the Prophet) stood on the day of Fitr and prayed, starting with the prayer then the khutbah. When he finished, he descended and went to the women, and he reminded them while leaning on Bilal's hand, and Bilal spread his cloth, and the women threw charity into it. I said to Ata: Is it zakat al-Fitr? He said: No, but it is charity they give at that time; some threw their rings, others threw (things). (Bukhari, chapter on the Imam advising women on Eid, p. 157, no. 978). In this hadith, women used to give charity.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage instructs that one should give charity on Eid according to their capacity. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet, after the Eid prayer, went to the women and exhorted them to give charity, and they gave generously, including jewelry. The text clarifies that this charity is not sadaqat al-fitr but general sadaqah. The Hanafi school considers giving sadaqah on Eid a recommended act (mustahab), especially to the poor and needy, as a way of spreading joy and fulfilling community needs.

Key Terms
صدقہ (sadaqah): Voluntary charity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the women give as charity during the Prophet's khutbah on Eid al-Fitr?
A) Only food items
B) Their jewelry and other items
C) Money only
D) Nothing, they were listening

Key Takeaway
Giving sadaqah on Eid is mustahab; the proof is the Prophet's encouragement, not a command.

Zakat: Definition and Seven Conditions of Obligation
Defining zakat and listing its seven conditions of obligation with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for zakat to be obligatory and explain the proof for each condition.

Core Idea
Zakat is fard on every free, adult, sane Muslim who fully owns nisab for one lunar year.

This passage opens the Book of Zakat by defining it both linguistically and legally, then lays out the seven conditions that must be met for zakat to be obligatory. Each condition is supported by textual evidence from the Quran, hadith, or athar. Understanding these conditions is the foundation for correctly applying the obligation of zakat.

Guided Path
1
Define zakat legally
Identify the legal definition: making a specific person (poor/needy) own specific wealth (nisab) with intention.
The linguistic meaning is purity or growth.
2
List the seven conditions
From the Hidayah: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, ownership of nisab, complete ownership, passing of one year.
Conditions 1-4 relate to the person; 5-7 relate to the wealth.
3
Examine the proof for freedom
Hadith from Jabir shows no zakat on a mukatab until free; a slave does not own wealth.
4
Examine the proof for sanity and adulthood
The hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' exempts children and the insane; athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibrahim confirm no zakat on orphan's wealth until puberty.
The same proof covers both conditions.
5
Examine the proof for Islam and nisab
Quranic verses (27:3, 9:71) link zakat to faith; a disbeliever's payment is tax. For nisab, hadith from Abu Sa'id sets thresholds for livestock and silver/gold.
Nisab thresholds differ by asset type.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢

كتاب الزكوة

ضروری نوٹ: زکوۃ کے معنی پاکی ہیں اور چونکہ زکوۃ دینے سے مال پاک ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو زکوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ یا زکوۃ کے معنی بڑھنا ہیں اور چونکہ زکوۃ دینے سے مال بڑھتا ہے اس لئے اس کو زکوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت بہت سی آیتوں میں ہے۔ مثلا يقيمون الصلوة ويؤتون الزكوة ويطيعون الله ورسوله (آیت اے سوره تو به ۹) اسی آیت سے زکوۃ دینا فرض ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
ترجمه : (١١٥٠) مخصوص شخص کو مخصوص مال کا مالک بنانا ( زکوۃ کہلاتا) ہے۔ تشریح : زکوۃ کا مال مخصوص مال ہے، اور جو زکاۃ کا مصرف ہے، یعنی غریب اور مسکین و مخصوص شخص ہیں۔ تو گویا کہ زکوۃ کے مال کوزکوۃ کی نیت سے غرباء ومساکین کو دینے کا نام زکوۃ ہے۔ یہاں مصنف نے زکوۃ کی تعریف کی ہے۔
ترجمه : (١١٥١) زکوۃ ہر آزاد مسلمان مکلف پر فرض ہے جو نقد نصاب کا مالک ہو۔
تشریح : زکوۃ عبادت مالیہ ہے۔ اس لئے کا فر پ زکوۃ واجب نہیں اس سے جو کچھ لیا جائے گا وہ ٹیکس لیا جائے گا۔ چنانچہ ھدایہ کے متن میں زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے سات [۷] شرطیں بیان فرمارہے ہیں ۔ [1] آزاد ہو۔ [۲] عاقل ہو۔ [۳] بالغ ہو ۔ [۴] مسلمان ہو [۵] نصاب کا مالک ہو ۔ [۶] نصاب پر مکمل ملک ہو [۷] نصاب پر سال گزر چکا ہو۔۔ ہر ایک کی تفصیل اور دلائل یہ ہیں [1]ا آزاد ہو، اس لئے غلام اور مکاتب پر زکاۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مال اس کے مولی کا ہے۔ غلام کا نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ حدیث میں ہے (۱) عن جابر قال قال رسول الله ليس فى مال المكاتب زكوة حتى يعتق (دار قطنی ۱۰، باب ليس في مال المكاتب زکوة حتى يعتق ج خانی ص ۹۳ نمبر ۱۹۴۱ سفن للبیھقی ، باب من قال ليس في مال العبد زکوۃ ، ج رابع ص ۱۸۲ نمبر ۷۳۴۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکاتب کے مال میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ آزاد نہیں ہے، (۲) دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ مال کا پورا مالک بننا ضروری ہے اور غلام کا مال نہیں ہے اس کے ہاتھ میں جو کچھ ہے وہ اس کے مولی کا مال ہے۔ [۲] دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ عاقل ہو ، اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو بالغ ہو چکا ہے لیکن مجنون ہے اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ بچے اور مجنون پر زکوۃ نہ ہونے کی دلیل ایک ہی ہے کہ دونوں کو عقل نہیں ہے اس لئے دونوں کے دلائل بچے پر زکوۃ واجب نہ ہونے کے تحت میں آرہے ہیں۔
[۳] تیسری شرط بالغ ہونا ہے۔ چنانچہ بچے کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے(۱)۔عن علی عن النبی

كتاب الزكوة
مکلّف مالک لنصاب من نقد
صلى الله
قال رفع القلم عن عن ثلثة عن النائم - حتى يستيقظ وعن الصبى حتى يحتلم وعن المجنون حتى يعقل . (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی المجنون يسرق او یصیب حداج ثانی ص ۲۵۶ کتاب الحدود، نمبر ۴۴۰۳ / ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب طلاق المعتوه والصغير والنائم ، کتاب الطلاق ص۲۹۲، نمبر ۲۰۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے ، اور مجنون کے اوپر کوئی ذمہ داری نہیں ہے تو زکوۃ بھی اس کے مال میں واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : لا يجب على مال الصغير زكاة حتى تـجـب عليه الصلاة ـ ( دارقطنی ، باب استقراض الوصی من مال الیتیم ، ج ثانی، ص ۹۷ نمبر ۱۹۶۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے کے مال پر زکاۃ نہیں ہے۔ (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال لیس فی مال الیتیم زكوة حتى يحتلم. (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۴۳ من قال لیس فی مال الیتیم زکوۃ حتی یبلغ ج ثانی ص ۱۳۷۹ نمبر ۱۰۱۲۶) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بچے کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ (۴) عن ابن مسعود أنه كان يقول أحص ما يجب فى مال اليتيم من الزكوة ، فاذا بلغ و أؤنس منه رشدا فادفعه اليه ، فان شاء زكاه و ان شاء تركه (مصنف ابن ابی هیپه ۴۳ ، من قال ليس في مال الیتیم زکوة حتی یبلغ ج ثانی، ص ۳۷۹، نمبر ۱۰۱۲۵؎ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ یتیم چاہے تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد بچپنے کی زکوۃ ادا کرے اور چاہے تو ادانہ کرے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے ۔
[۴] چوتھی شرط مسلمان ہونا ہے۔(۱) زکوۃ عبادت مالیہ ہے اور فرض ہے، اور فرض مسلمان پر ہی ہوتا ہے، ورنہ کافر سے جو کچھ لیا جاتا ہے وہ عبادت کے طور پر نہیں بلکہ ٹیکس کے طور پر، اس میں کا فر کو آخرت میں کوئی ثواب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس پر تو اسکو یقین ہی نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس آیت میں زکوۃ دینے کے لئے مسلمان کی شرط ہے۔ الذین یقیمون الصلوة ويؤتون الزكوة و هم بالآخرة هم يوقنون (آیت ۳،سورۃ النمل (۲۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ وہ آخرت پر یقین رکھتا ہو یعنی مسلمان ہوتب زکوۃ فرض ہو گی (۳) و المؤمنون والمؤمنات بعضهم أولياء بعض يأمرون بالمعروف وينهون عن المنكرو يقيمون الصلوة و يؤتون الزكوة و يطيعون الله ورسوله أولئك سيرحمهم الله ان الله عزیز حکیم (آیت اے سورہ تو بہ 9 ) اس آیت میں بھی زکوۃ دینے کے لئے مسلمان ہونے کی شرط ہے۔ [۵] پانچویں شرط ہے کہ نصاب کا مکمل مالک ہو۔ (۱) کیونکہ تھوڑے سے مال کا مالک ہوگا اور اس میں زکوۃ دے گا تو آج زکوۃ دے گا اور کل لوگوں سے زکوۃ مانگے گا۔ اس لئے شرط لگائی کہ نصاب کا مالک ہو۔ اور نصاب یہ ہے کہ سال بھر کھا پی کر دو سو درہم بچے، یا نہیں مثقال سونا بچے تو اس میں چالیسواں حصہ زکوۃ ہے یعنی چالیس درہم میں ایک درہم لازم ہوگا۔ اور اونٹ ،گائے ، بکری اور کاشتکاروں کا نصاب الگ الگ ہے جس کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔ (۲) دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت ابا سعید الخدری قال: قال رسول الله له ليس فيما دون خمس ذود صدقة من الابل وليس فيمادون خمس اواق صدقة،وليس
Fruit of Success Volume 2
254
Book of Zakat
Book of Zakat
(1150) It is making a specific person own specific wealth. (1151) It is obligated upon a free Muslim.
Book of Zakat
Necessary note: Zakat means purity, and because giving zakat makes wealth pure, it is called zakat. Or zakat means increase, and because giving zakat increases wealth, it is called zakat. Its proof is in many verses. For example: 'They establish prayer and give zakat and obey Allah and His Messenger' (verse 9 of Surah at-Tawbah). From this verse, giving zakat is established as obligatory.
Translation: (1150) Making a specific person own specific wealth (is called zakat). Explanation: The wealth of zakat is specific wealth, and the one who receives zakat, i.e., the poor and needy, are specific persons. So, giving the wealth of zakat with the intention of zakat to the poor and needy is called zakat. Here the author has defined zakat.
Translation: (1151) Zakat is obligatory upon every free, Muslim, accountable person who owns the nisab of cash.
Explanation: Zakat is a financial worship. Therefore, zakat is not obligatory upon a disbeliever; whatever is taken from him will be taken as tax. Accordingly, the text of Hidayah states seven [7] conditions for zakat to be obligatory: [1] Free. [2] Sane. [3] Adult. [4] Muslim. [5] Owner of nisab. [6] Complete ownership of nisab. [7] One year has passed over the nisab. Their details and proofs are: [1] Free: therefore, zakat is not obligatory upon a slave or a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission), because this wealth belongs to his master, not the slave. As in the hadith: 'From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: There is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab until he is freed' (al-Daraqutni, chapter 'There is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab until he is freed', volume 2, page 93, number 1941; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter 'Who said there is no zakat on the wealth of a slave', volume 4, page 182, number 7348). From this hadith, it is known that there is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab because he is not free. (2) The second point is that complete ownership of wealth is necessary, and a slave does not own wealth; whatever is in his hand is his master's wealth. [2] Second condition: that he be sane. This means that if someone has reached adulthood but is insane, zakat is not obligatory upon him. The proof that zakat is not upon a child or an insane person is one: both lack intellect. Therefore, their proofs are coming under the section of zakat not being obligatory upon a child. [3] Third condition: being adult. Thus, zakat is not obligatory upon a child's wealth. Its proof is this hadith: 'From Ali, from the Prophet (peace be upon him): He said: The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the insane stealing or committing a hadd punishment, volume 2, page 256, book of Hudud, number 4403; Ibn Majah, chapter on divorce of the insane, the minor, and the sleeper, book of Divorce, page 292, number 2042). From this hadith, it is known that there is no responsibility upon the child and the insane, so zakat will also not be obligatory in their wealth. (2) There is an athar: 'From Ibn Abbas, he said: Zakat is not obligatory upon the wealth of a minor until prayer becomes obligatory upon him.' (al-Daraqutni, chapter on the guardian borrowing from the orphan's wealth, volume 2, page 97, number 1962). From this athar, it is known that there is no zakat upon the wealth of a child. (3) There is an athar: 'From Ibrahim, he said: There is no zakat in the wealth of an orphan until he reaches puberty.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 43, 'Who said there is no zakat in the wealth of an orphan until he reaches puberty', volume 2, page 1379, number 10126). From this athar also, it is known that zakat is not obligatory in the wealth of a child. (4) 'From Ibn Mas'ud, he used to say: Calculate what is obligatory in the orphan's wealth of zakat, then when he reaches puberty and you perceive his maturity, give it to him; if he wishes, he may give zakat, and if he wishes, he may leave it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 43, 'Who said there is no zakat in the wealth of an orphan until he reaches puberty', volume 2, page 379, number 10125). In this athar, it is that the orphan, if he wishes after reaching adulthood, may pay the zakat of his childhood, and if he wishes, he may not pay, from which it is known that zakat is not obligatory in the wealth of a child. [4] Fourth condition: being Muslim. (1) Zakat is a financial worship and is obligatory, and obligation is only upon a Muslim; otherwise, whatever is taken from a disbeliever is not as worship but as tax; there is no reward in the Hereafter for the disbeliever because he does not believe in it. (2) In this verse, being Muslim is a condition for giving zakat: 'Those who establish prayer and give zakat and of the Hereafter they are certain' (verse 3, Surah an-Naml (27)). In this verse, he believes in the Hereafter, i.e., he is Muslim, then zakat will be obligatory. (3) 'And the believing men and believing women are allies of one another. They enjoin what is right and forbid what is wrong, establish prayer, and give zakat, and obey Allah and His Messenger. Those – Allah will have mercy upon them. Indeed, Allah is Exalted in Might and Wise.' (verse 9 of Surah at-Tawbah). In this verse also, being Muslim is a condition for giving zakat. [5] Fifth condition: that he be a complete owner of the nisab. (1) Because if he owns a small amount and gives zakat on it, today he will give zakat and tomorrow he will beg from people. Therefore, the condition was made that he be the owner of the nisab. And the nisab is that after a year's sustenance, two hundred dirhams remain, or twenty mithqals of gold remain; then one-fortieth portion is zakat, i.e., one dirham becomes obligatory on forty dirhams. And the nisab for camels, cows, goats, and farmers is separate, whose details are coming later. (2) The proof is in this hadith: 'I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: There is no sadaqah on less than five dhud of camels, and there is no sadaqah on less than five uqiyyah, and there is no...'
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Zakat in Thamaratun Najah. It begins by defining zakat linguistically (purity and growth) and legally (transferring specific wealth to a specific person with intention). The author then states the core ruling: zakat is obligatory (fard) on every free Muslim who is accountable (mukallaf) and owns nisab of cash. The commentary from Hidayah lists seven conditions for the obligation: freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, ownership of nisab, complete ownership, and the passing of one lunar year. The passage then provides detailed proofs for the first four conditions. For freedom, hadiths from Jabir and others show that a slave or mukatab does not pay zakat because they lack complete ownership. For sanity and adulthood, the famous hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' exempts children and the insane, and multiple athar (companion reports) confirm no zakat on an orphan's wealth until puberty. For Islam, Quranic verses (27:3 and 9:71) link zakat to faith, and a disbeliever's payment is merely a tax, not worship. The fifth condition on nisab is introduced with the minimum thresholds for gold and silver, and a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri on livestock. The author follows the order of conditions, explaining each with textual evidence from Quran, hadith, and athar.

Key Terms
زكوة (zakāh): Linguistically: purity and growth. Legally: transferring specific wealth (nisab) to specific recipients (fuqara, masakin, etc.) with intention.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth (200 dirhams silver, 20 mithqals gold, or equivalent) required for zakat to be obligatory.
حر (ḥurr): Free person, as opposed to a slave (raqīq). Zakat is not obligatory on slaves because they do not own wealth.
مکلف (mukallaf): A person who is legally responsible: free, adult, sane, Muslim. Zakat is only obligatory on the mukallaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of zakat?
A) Being free (hurr)
B) Being male (dhakar)
C) Being Muslim
D) Ownership of nisab for one year

Key Takeaway
Zakat is obligatory only when all seven conditions are met; understanding each condition prevents errors in fulfilling this pillar.

Zakat Not Obligatory on Non-Mukallaf
Ruling with proof establishing condition of mukallaf for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zakat is not wajib on the wealth of non-mukallaf individuals and cite the primary proof (hadith raf' al-qalam).

Core Idea
Zakat is only wajib on the mukallaf; the pen is lifted from minors, the insane, and the sleeper.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh: zakat is not obligatory upon the wealth of minors, the insane, or sleeping individuals. The key proof is the hadith of the lifted pen, which removes all legal accountability from these categories. We will also explore supporting athars from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding zakat on the wealth of a minor or insane person? Determine the hukm level (wajib, not wajib, etc.).
The ruling is that zakat is not wajib on their wealth.
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
Find the primary textual proof cited in the passage. What is the hadith and where is it from?
The hadith of raf' al-qalam (the pen is lifted from three).
3
Analyse the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. What specific phrase indicates that obligations are lifted from these categories?
The phrase 'raf' al-qalam' and the explicit mention of the child until puberty, etc.
4
Examine Supporting Athars
Identify the athars from Ibn Abbas, Ibrahim, and Ibn Mas'ud. How do they reinforce the ruling?
They explicitly state that no zakat is due on the wealth of a child/orphan until they reach puberty.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Status
Is this ruling agreed upon by all schools? If not, which school differs and on what grounds?
Some schools consider zakat wajib on productive wealth of minors; Hanafi holds firm on the condition of mukallaf.

(مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۴۳ من قال لیس فی مال الیتیم زکوۃ حتی یبلغ ج ثانی ص ۱۳۷۹ نمبر ۱۰۱۲۶) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بچے کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ (۴) عن ابن مسعود أنه كان يقول أحص ما يجب فى مال اليتيم من الزكوة ، فاذا بلغ و أؤنس منه رشدا فادفعه اليه ، فان شاء زكاه و ان شاء تركه (مصنف ابن ابی هیپه ۴۳ ، من قال ليس في مال الیتیم زکوة حتی یبلغ ج ثانی، ص ۳۷۹، نمبر ۱۰۱۲۵؎ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ یتیم چاہے تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد بچپنے کی زکوۃ ادا کرے اور چاہے تو ادانہ کرے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے کے مال میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے ۔
Book of Zakat. Accountable, owner of nisab in cash. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he regains sanity. (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). From this hadith it is understood that children and the insane have no responsibility, so zakat will not be obligatory upon their wealth. (2) There is an athar from Ibn Abbas: Zakat is not obligatory upon the wealth of a child until prayer becomes obligatory upon him. (Darqutni). (3) Athar from Ibrahim: There is no zakat in the wealth of an orphan until he reaches puberty. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). (4) From Ibn Mas'ud that he used to say: I will assess what zakat is due in the wealth of an orphan, then when he reaches maturity and I see sound judgement in him, I give it to him; if he wishes he may give zakat and if he wishes he may leave it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From this athar it is understood that zakat is not obligatory upon the wealth of a child.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage establishes that one of the conditions for zakat is being mukallaf (legally accountable). The hadith of the lifted pen (raf' al-qalam) is a foundational proof in Hanafi fiqh that minors, the insane, and those asleep are not subject to religious obligations. The author then supports this with athars from the Companions and Successors. Notably, the athar from Ibn Mas'ud shows that if a guardian pays zakat on behalf of an orphan before majority, it is not considered obligatory; the orphan has a choice after reaching puberty. This reinforces that zakat is not wajib on non-mukallaf individuals. The Hanafi school adheres to this ruling consistently.

Key Terms
مکلّف (mukallaf): A legally accountable person who has reached puberty and is sane.
رفع القلم (raf' al-qalam): The lifting of the pen, meaning no accountability for actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is zakat not obligatory on a minor's wealth?
A) Because minors have no wealth
B) Because the pen is lifted from minors until puberty
C) Because zakat is only on cash crops
D) Because minors are exempt from all financial duties

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not wajib on the wealth of non-mukallaf individuals because the pen is lifted from them until they become legally accountable.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Condition of Being Muslim for Zakat
Proves condition of Islam for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that zakat is wajib only on Muslims and prove it using Quranic and rational evidence.

Core Idea
Zakat is an act of worship; only a Muslim can perform worship with reward.

Zakat is a financial worship that Allah has made obligatory upon those who believe in Him and the Hereafter. The Hanafi school emphasises that this obligation is tied to faith itself. In this lesson, we examine the fourth condition for zakat: being Muslim, and the proofs that establish it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states that being Muslim is the fourth condition for zakat. Zakat is wajib only on Muslims.
This is a condition for obligation (shart al-wujub), not for validity.
2
Understand the rational proof
Zakat is an act of worship ('ibadat maliyyah). Worship is only meaningful if the performer believes in the One worshipped. A non-Muslim's payment is therefore treated as tax, not worship, and yields no reward in the afterlife.
The rational argument links the nature of worship to faith.
3
Analyse the first Quranic proof
Surah al-Naml 27:3 describes those who give zakat as 'certain of the Hereafter'. This implies that zakat is an act of believers, thus non-Muslims are not addressed.
Verse: 'Who establish prayer and give zakat, and they are certain of the Hereafter.'
4
Analyse the second Quranic proof
Surah al-Tawbah 9:71 refers to 'believing men and believing women' who pray, give zakat, and obey Allah. Again, zakat is linked to faith.
The verse conditions zakat on being a believer (mu'min).
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
Based on these proofs, the Hanafi school holds that zakat is not wajib on non-Muslims. If a non-Muslim pays wealth, it is taken as tax (e.g., jizya or kharaj), not as zakat, and carries no spiritual reward.
This is the mufta bihi position.

[۴] چوتھی شرط مسلمان ہونا ہے۔(۱) زکوۃ عبادت مالیہ ہے اور فرض ہے، اور فرض مسلمان پر ہی ہوتا ہے، ورنہ کافر سے جو کچھ لیا جاتا ہے وہ عبادت کے طور پر نہیں بلکہ ٹیکس کے طور پر، اس میں کا فر کو آخرت میں کوئی ثواب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس پر تو اسکو یقین ہی نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس آیت میں زکوۃ دینے کے لئے مسلمان کی شرط ہے۔ الذین یقیمون الصلوة ويؤتون الزكوة و هم بالآخرة هم يوقنون (آیت ۳،سورۃ النمل (۲۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ وہ آخرت پر یقین رکھتا ہو یعنی مسلمان ہوتب زکوۃ فرض ہو گی (۳) و المؤمنون والمؤمنات بعضهم أولياء بعض يأمرون بالمعروف وينهون عن المنكرو يقيمون الصلوة و يؤتون الزكوة و يطيعون الله ورسوله أولئك سيرحمهم الله ان الله عزیز حکیم (آیت اے سورہ تو بہ 9 ) اس آیت میں بھی زکوۃ دینے کے لئے مسلمان ہونے کی شرط ہے۔
[4] The fourth condition is being Muslim. (1) Zakat is a financial worship and an obligation, and an obligation is only upon a Muslim; otherwise, what is taken from a disbeliever is not as worship but as tax, and the disbeliever gets no reward in the afterlife because he does not believe in it. (2) In this verse, being Muslim is a condition for giving zakat: 'Those who establish prayer and give zakat, and they are certain of the Hereafter' (Surah al-Naml 27:3). This verse indicates that one who believes in the Hereafter, i.e., is Muslim, zakat becomes obligatory. (3) 'And the believing men and believing women are allies of one another; they enjoin what is right and forbid what is wrong and establish prayer and give zakat and obey Allah and His Messenger. Those - Allah will have mercy upon them. Indeed, Allah is Exalted in Might and Wise.' (Surah al-Tawbah 9:71). This verse also conditions being Muslim for giving zakat.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth condition for zakat: being Muslim. The author provides two arguments: first, a rational one that zakat is an act of worship, and worship is only meaningful for those who believe in the One worshipped. A disbeliever's payment is considered a tax (jizya or kharaj), not zakat, and yields no reward. Second, two Quranic verses are cited: Surah al-Naml 27:3 and Surah al-Tawbah 9:71, both of which describe those who give zakat as believers. The Hanafi school holds that zakat is not wajib on non-Muslims, though they may be compelled to pay a tax instead.

Key Terms
مسلمان (muslim): One who believes in Allah and the Hereafter, for whom zakat is obligatory.
زکوٰۃ (zakat): Obligatory alms; a financial worship.
عبادت مالیہ (ibadat maliyyah): Financial worship — worship that involves wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of zakat for a non-Muslim?
A) It is wajib on them as well
B) It is not wajib; whatever they pay is treated as tax, not worship
C) It is wajib but they have no reward
D) It is makruh to take from them

Key Takeaway
Zakat is wajib only on Muslims; non-Muslims' payments are tax, not worship.

Condition of Full Ownership of Nisab
Defines nisab and full ownership as conditions for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds for silver, gold, and livestock, explain why zakat is not wajib on a mukatab's wealth, and apply the condition of full ownership to determine zakat obligation.

Core Idea
Zakat is wajib only when you fully own a complete nisab—partial ownership or insufficient wealth means no zakat.

In this lesson, we explore two key conditions for zakat: reaching the nisab threshold and having full ownership. The text explains the nisab amounts for different types of wealth and uses the case of a mukatab to illustrate why incomplete ownership prevents zakat. We'll examine the hadith proofs and understand how these rules apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the opening: the fifth condition is complete ownership (malikiyyah) of the nisab. Understand the rationale: to prevent hardship, one must own enough to sustain a year.
The condition is called 'tam al-milk' (full ownership).
2
Define nisab amounts
The text gives nisab for silver (200 dirhams), gold (20 mithqals), camels (5), and crops (5 wasq). Note that livestock and crop nisabs are separate, with details promised later.
One uqiya = 40 dirhams, so 5 awaq = 200 dirhams.
3
Examine the first hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) explicitly states: no sadaqah below thresholds. This establishes nisab as a necessary condition.
Hadith: 'ليس فيما دون خمس ذود صدقة من الابل...'
4
Examine the second hadith proof on full ownership
The hadith of Jabir (Darqutni, Bayhaqi) says: no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab until he is freed. The commentary explains this is because his ownership is incomplete; his master still has a claim.
A mukatab is a slave who contracted to buy freedom by installments.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Zakat is wajib only when both conditions are met: wealth reaches nisab AND ownership is complete. If either is missing, no zakat.
The Hanafi school holds this position based on these proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵] پانچویں شرط ہے کہ نصاب کا مکمل مالک ہو۔ (۱) کیونکہ تھوڑے سے مال کا مالک ہوگا اور اس میں زکوۃ دے گا تو آج زکوۃ دے گا اور کل لوگوں سے زکوۃ مانگے گا۔ اس لئے شرط لگائی کہ نصاب کا مالک ہو۔ اور نصاب یہ ہے کہ سال بھر کھا پی کر دو سو درہم بچے، یا نہیں مثقال سونا بچے تو اس میں چالیسواں حصہ زکوۃ ہے یعنی چالیس درہم میں ایک درہم لازم ہوگا۔ اور اونٹ ،گائے ، بکری اور کاشتکاروں کا نصاب الگ الگ ہے جس کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔ (۲) دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت ابا سعید الخدری قال: قال رسول الله له ليس فيما دون خمس ذود صدقة من الابل وليس فيمادون خمس اواق صدقة،وليس فيما دون خمسة اوسق صدقة (بخاری شریف، باب زکوة الورق ص ۱۹۴ کتاب الزکوۃ نمبر ۱۴۴۷ر مسلم شریف ، باب لیس فیما دون خمسته اوسق صدقته ،ص ۱۳۹۳، نمبر ۲۲۶۳/۹۷۹ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما تجب فیه الزکوۃ ص ۲۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۵۸) ایک اوقیہ چالیس درہم کا ہوتا ہے تو پانچ اوقیہ دوسو درہم ہوئے ۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو سو درہم سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب ہے ہی نہیں ۔ اسی طرح پانچ اونٹ سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اس حدیث میں بہت سی چیزوں کا نصاب بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ اور یہ بھی فرمایا کہ اس نصاب سے کم کا مالک ہو تو اس پر زکوۃ فرض ہی نہیں ۔ اور اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ پانچ وسق سے کم غلہ پیدا ہوتو زکوۃ یعنی عشر نہیں ہے۔ البتہ دوسری حدیث کی وجہ سے حنفیہ کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے جس کی تفصیل آگے آئے گی۔ [1] ۔ ملک نام کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ مکاتب چیز کا مالک ہوتا ہے لیکن اس کی ملکیت اس پر تام نہیں ہے اس لئے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔عن جابر قال قال رسول الله ليس فى مال المكاتب زكوة حتى يعتق (دارقطنی ۱۰، باب ليس في مال المكاتب زکوة حتى يعتق ج ثانی ص ۹۳ نمبر ۱۹۴۱ر سنن للبیھقی ، باب من قال ليس في مال العبد زكوة ، ج رابع ص ۱۸۲، نمبر ۷۳۴۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکاتب کے مال میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ مال کا پورا مالک نہیں ہے ، آج ہی غلامیت کی طرف لوٹ جائے گا تو اس مال کا مالک اس کا مولی ہو جائے گا۔
[5] The fifth condition is that one must be the complete owner of the nisab. (1) Because if someone owns only a little wealth and gives zakat, he would give zakat today and beg from people tomorrow. So the condition was set that one must own the nisab. The nisab is that after a year's expenses, two hundred dirhams remain, or twenty mithqals of gold remain; then one-fortieth is zakat, i.e., one dirham for every forty dirhams. The nisab for camels, cows, goats, and crops is separate, details to follow. (2) The proof is in this hadith: I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: There is no sadaqah on less than five dhoud of camels, and there is no sadaqah on less than five awaq, and there is no sadaqah on less than five wasq. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). One uqiya is forty dirhams, so five awaq is two hundred dirhams. From this hadith it is understood that zakat is not obligatory on less than two hundred dirhams. Similarly, zakat is not wajib on less than five camels. This hadith explains the nisab for many things. And it also states that if one owns less than this nisab, no zakat is obligatory. And from this hadith it is proven that if less than five wasq of grain is harvested, there is no zakat, i.e., no 'ushr. However, due to another hadith, the Hanafis have a difference of opinion on this, details to come. [1] The restriction of 'ownership' was placed because a mukatab is an owner of something but his ownership is not complete, so zakat is not wajib on him. The hadith: Jabir narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: There is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab until he is freed. (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). From this hadith it is understood that there is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab, because he is not the full owner of the wealth; if he returns to slavery, his master becomes the owner.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage covers two sub-conditions: ownership of nisab and full ownership. The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams and for gold is 20 mithqals. The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri establishes minimum thresholds for zakat on camels, silver, and grain. The author notes that for grain, the Hanafis have a different view due to another hadith, which will be discussed later. Then, the condition of full ownership is illustrated by the case of a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom). Since his ownership is not complete (his master still has a claim), zakat is not wajib on him. This shows that only complete and unrestricted ownership triggers zakat.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
ملک تام (milk tam): Full and complete ownership, free from any claims or restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because his ownership is not complete; the master retains a claim
C) Because he is poor
D) Because he is a minor

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not wajib until you fully own the nisab; partial or incomplete ownership, like that of a mukatab, exempts you.

The Condition of Hawl for Zakat
Proves hawl condition via two hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of hawl for zakat, cite the two hadith proofs, and apply the ruling to determine when zakat becomes wajib.

Core Idea
Zakat is due only after one lunar year passes on the nisab — the hawl is a binding condition.

Zakat is one of the five pillars, but it is not due immediately upon acquiring wealth. The Hanafi school requires a full lunar year to elapse while the nisab is maintained. This lesson examines the textual proofs from the Sunnah that establish this condition, and clarifies the ruling if someone pays zakat before the year ends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its ruling
Recognize that hawl is a condition (shart) for zakat to be wajib. The passage states it as the seventh condition. The ruling: zakat becomes wajib only after one year.
2
Locate the first dalil (Hadith of 'Ali)
The hadith from 'Ali (Abu Dawud) explicitly conditions zakat on the completion of a year for both silver and gold. Find the conditional phrase 'when a year passes'.
3
Locate the second dalil (Hadith of Ibn Umar)
The hadith from Ibn Umar (Darqutni) is even more explicit: 'There is no zakat on a person's wealth until a year passes over it.' This is a clear statement of conditionality.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider someone who acquires 200 dirhams. Zakat is not due immediately; it becomes wajib only after one full lunar year. If they pay before the year, the payment is valid and accepted, fulfilling the obligation.
The payment before time is considered ta'jil (advance payment) and is valid.
5
Note the scope of hawl
Hawl applies to gold, silver, cash, and trade goods. It does NOT apply to crops and fruits, which are due at harvest even if the year has not passed.
This is a Hanafi specific distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷] ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ اس مال پر سال گزرے ۔ (۱) اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علـى عن النبي الله ببعض اول الحديث قال فاذا كانت لک مائتا در هم و حال عليه الحول ففيها خمسة دراهم ولیس علیک شیء یعنی في الذهب حتى يكون لك عشرون دينارا فاذا کانت لک عشرون دينارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلک (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۵۷۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نصاب پر سال گزر جائے تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی، اس سے پہلے نہیں لیکن کوئی ادا کر دے تو ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ [۲] عـــن ابـــن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله لا زكوة في مال امرئ حتى يحول عليه الحول ( دارقطنی ، باب وجوب الزكوة بالحول ج ثانی ص ۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۷۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ مال نصاب پر سال گزرنے کے بعد واجب ہوتی ہے۔ یہ اجمالی دلائل ہوئے جو ھدایہ میں ذکر ہوئے ہیں۔ معلومات کے لئے یہاں بھی ذکر کرئے ہیں۔
[7] The seventh condition is that a year passes over that wealth. (1) Its proof is this hadith: From 'Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him) - part of the first hadith - he said: When you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes over them, then five dirhams are due, and nothing is due from you regarding gold until you have twenty dinars; when you have twenty dinars and a year passes over them, then half a dinar is due, and for whatever exceeds that, the calculation is according to that. (Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that zakat becomes wajib only when a year passes over the nisab; before that, it is not, but if someone gives it, it will be accepted. [2] From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: There is no zakat on a person's wealth until a year passes over it. (Darqutni). From this hadith it is also understood that zakat becomes wajib after a year passes over the nisab. These are summary proofs that are mentioned in the Hidayah; for information, they are also mentioned here.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage establishes the seventh condition: the passage of one lunar year (hawl) over the nisab. Two hadiths are cited: the first from 'Ali specifying the calculation of zakat for silver and gold after a year, and the second from Ibn Umar explicitly stating that no zakat is due until a year passes. The author notes that if someone voluntarily pays zakat before the year ends, it is valid (the obligation is discharged). This condition is crucial for cash and trade goods; for crops, the nisab and time differ. The Hanafi school holds that hawl is a condition for zakat on silver, gold, and trade goods, but not for crops and fruits (which are due at harvest). The author acknowledges that these proofs are summarized from al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
حول (hawl): A full lunar year that must pass over the nisab for zakat to become wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on paying zakat before the completion of one year on the nisab?
A) It is not allowed
B) It is accepted and the obligation is fulfilled
C) It is invalid and must be repeated
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Zakat on nisab-based wealth becomes wajib only after one complete lunar year, as proven by the hadiths of 'Ali and Ibn Umar, and advance payment is valid.

Zakat on Gold, Silver, Jewelry, Utensils, and Trade Goods
Ruling statement: zakat on gold/silver in all forms and trade goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for gold, silver, jewelry, utensils, and trade goods, and identify the nisab threshold.

Core Idea
Gold and silver in any form—bullion, coins, jewelry, utensils—are subject to zakat when nisab is reached.

This lesson presents a foundational ruling from the Hanafi school: zakat is wajib on gold and silver regardless of their form. Many assume that jewelry for personal use is exempt, but the Hanafi school differs from other madhahib. Understanding this ruling clarifies one's obligation accurately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the ruling applies to gold and silver in all forms: bullion, coins, jewelry, utensils, and trade goods.
The substance (ayn) triggers zakat, not the form or usage.
2
Note the condition
Zakat becomes wajib only when the nisab is reached—for gold, 7.5 tola (approx. 87.48 g); for silver, 52.5 tola (approx. 612.36 g); trade goods are valued by the silver nisab.
3
Apply to examples
Test the ruling: a gold necklace above nisab is zakatable, but a below-nisab gold coin is not.
The hawl (lunar year) is also required but not explicitly mentioned here.
4
Contrast with other schools
Note that Shafi'i and Maliki schools exempt jewelry for personal use, while Hanafi does not.
This is a key ikhtilaf that affects practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تـرجـمه : (۱۱۵۲) چاہے سونا چاندی ہو، چاہے زیور، برتن یا تجارت کے سامان کی کوئی ایسی چیز ہو جو (نصاب کی ) قیمت کے برابر ہو. تشریح : سونا اور چاندی جس شکل میں بھی ہو، چاہے سونے اور چاندی کی ڈلی ہو، چاہے روپنے کی شکل میں ہو، یاز یور ہو، یا برتن ہو ، نصاب پورا ہونے سے اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ اور تجارت کے سامان کی قیمت ساڑھے باون تولہ چاندی، یا ساڑھے سات
Translation: (1152) Whether it is gold and silver, whether jewelry, utensils, or any item of trade goods that is equivalent to the value of the nisab. Explanation: Gold and silver in whatever form, whether lumps of gold and silver, whether in the form of coins, or jewelry, or utensils, when the nisab is complete, zakat is wajib on them. And the value of trade goods is at fifty-two and a half tola of silver, or seven and a half
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is the matn (text) of the book, likely from al-Hidayah or similar. It states that zakat is wajib on gold and silver in any form—whether as bullion, coins, jewelry, or utensils—as long as the nisab is reached. The same applies to trade goods (urud al-tijarah) whose value equals the nisab. The commentary clarifies that the nisab for trade goods is measured by the value in silver (52.5 tola) or gold (7.5 tola). This ruling is based on the principle that zakat is on the substance of gold and silver, not on their form. Jewelry for personal use is also subject to zakat in the Hanafi school, unlike some other schools.

Key Terms
زیور (zaywar): Jewelry made of gold or silver, for which zakat is wajib if it reaches nisab.
عرورض تجارة (urud al-tijarah): Trade goods: merchandise intended for sale, valued at nisab for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is zakat wajib on a gold necklace that a woman wears for personal use?
A) Yes, if it reaches the nisab
B) No, because it is for personal use
C) Only if it is meant for trade
D) It is makruh to pay zakat on it

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is wajib on all gold and silver in any form, including jewelry and utensils, provided the nisab is reached.

Conditions for Zakat: Nisab, Complete Ownership, and Passage of Year
Explains obligation of zakat with conditions and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three main conditions for zakat (nisab, full ownership, passage of one year) and apply the Hanafi ruling on zakat for gold, silver, jewelry, and trade goods using the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Zakat is not obligatory until you own the nisab fully AND a lunar year passes — incomplete ownership or a broken year means no zakat.

In this passage, we learn the essential prerequisites that trigger the obligation of zakat on wealth. The text explains what kinds of assets are subject to zakat and the specific conditions that must be met, backed by hadith evidence from the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding these conditions prevents premature or incorrect payment of zakat and ensures you fulfil this pillar correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the ruling is about the obligation of zakat on various assets. The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the proofs are ahad hadith (zanni thubut).
Wajib means obligatory but of slightly lower certainty than fard in Hanafi terminology.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: for nisab, the hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud about five awsuq; for hawl, the hadith from Ali (Abu Dawud) and Ibn Umar (Darqutni).
The author also mentions hadith for trade goods (Samurah) and jewelry (Amr b. Shu'ayb) later.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith prove the conditions. The imperative phrasing and explicit conditions ('if a year passes', 'no zakat until the year passes') indicate that nisab and hawl are prerequisites for obligation.
The hadith specify exact amounts (200 dirhams, 20 dinars) establishing the nisab.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions a Hanafi internal difference regarding nisab for crops (5 wasq) which will be clarified later. No other schools are discussed here.
The difference is deferred; the student should note that not all nisab rulings are unanimously applied.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that zakat is wajib on these assets when the three conditions (nisab, full ownership, hawl) are met. The tools of trade are excluded unless they are for sale.
The mufta bihi position is consistent with the matn and commentary.

[٧] ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ اس مال پر سال گزرے ۔ (١) اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علـى عن النبي الله ببعض اول الحديث قال فاذا كانت لک مائتا در هم و حال عليه الحول ففيها خمسة دراهم ولیس علیک شیء یعنی في الذهب حتى يكون لك عشرون دينارا فاذا کانت لک عشرون دينارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلک (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ص ٢٢٨ نمبر ٥٧٣، نمبر ١٥٧٣) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نصاب پر سال گزر جائے تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی، اس سے پہلے نہیں لیکن کوئی ادا کر دے تو ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ [٢] عـــن ابـــن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله لا زكوة في مال امرئ حتى يحول عليه الحول ( دارقطنی ، باب وجوب الزكوة بالحول ج ثانی ص ٧٦ نمبر ١٨٧٠) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ مال نصاب پر سال گزرنے کے بعد واجب ہوتی ہے۔ یہ اجمالی دلائل ہوئے جو ھدایہ میں ذکر ہوئے ہیں۔ معلومات کے لئے یہاں بھی ذکر کرئے ہیں۔ تـرجـمه : (١١٥٢) چاہے سونا چاندی ہو، چاہے زیور، برتن یا تجارت کے سامان کی کوئی ایسی چیز ہو جو (نصاب کی ) قیمت کے برابر ہو.
تشریح : سونا اور چاندی جس شکل میں بھی ہو، چاہے سونے اور چاندی کی ڈلی ہو، چاہے روپنے کی شکل میں ہو، یاز یور ہو، یا برتن ہو ، نصاب پورا ہونے سے اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ اور تجارت کے سامان کی قیمت ساڑھے باون تولہ چاندی، یا ساڑھے سات تولہ سونے کے برابر ہو تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہے، مثلا تاجر کے پاس بیچنے کے لئے کتا میں ہیں، تو ان کتابوں کی قیمت نصاب کے برابر ہو اور سال گزر جائے تو ان پر زکوۃ ہے۔ لیکن آلات کسب پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے ، مثلا درزی کے پاس دس ہزار پونڈ کی سلائی مشین ہے تو اس سلائی مشین کی قیمت پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ، اس سلائی میں جو آمدنی ہوگی وہ سال بھر کھا پی کر بچ جائے اور نصاب کو پہنچ جائے تو اس پر زکوۃ ہے۔ وجه : (١) تجارت کے لئے ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ، عن سمرة بن جندب قال اما بعد فان رسول الله الا الله كان يأمرنا ان نخرج الصدقة من الذى نعد للبيع - ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب العروض اذا كانت لتجارة صل فيها زكوة ص ٢٣٠، نمبر ١٥٦٢) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تجارت کے لئے ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ (٢) اور زیور ہو تو زکوۃ واجب ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان امراة اتت رسول الله له و معها ابنة لها وفي يد ابنتهـا مسـكتـان غـلـيـظـتـان مـن ذهـب فقال لها اتعطين زكاة هذا ؟قالت لا قال أيسرك ان يسورک الـلـه بهـمـا يــوم القيامة سوارين من نار ؟ قال فخلعتهما الى النبي عل و قالت هما لله و لرسوله (ابو داؤد شریف، باب الکنز ما هو؟ وزكوة الحلی ، ص ٢٣٠، نمبر ١٥٦٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ زیور میں زکوۃ ہے.
(1152) And if it is gold, jewelry, vessels, or what equals their value from trade goods, [zakat is due] on less than five awsuq? (Hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). One uqiya is forty dirhams, so five uqiyas are two hundred dirhams. From this hadith it is known that zakat is not obligatory on less than two hundred dirhams. Similarly, zakat is not obligatory on less than five camels. This hadith explains the nisab for many things. It also states that if someone owns less than this nisab, zakat is not fard. And from this hadith it is established that if less than five wasq of grain is produced, there is no zakat (ushr). However, due to another hadith, the Hanafis have a difference regarding this, details later. [1] The condition of milk (ownership) is added because a mukatib owns the thing but his ownership is not complete, so zakat is not obligatory on him. The hadith: from Jabir, the Prophet said: 'There is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatib until he is freed.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). [7] The seventh condition is that a year passes over this wealth. Its proof is the hadith from Ali: 'If you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes, then five dirhams are due; if you have twenty dinars and a year passes, then half a dinar is due, and so on.' (Abu Dawud). From this it is known that zakat becomes wajib after a year passes; before that not, but if someone pays, it is valid. [2] From Ibn Umar: 'There is no zakat on the wealth of a person until a year passes over it.' (Darqutni). These are summary proofs from Hidayah. Translation: (1152) Whether it is gold, silver, jewelry, vessels, or anything from trade goods that equals the value (of the nisab). Explanation: Gold and silver in any form—lumps, coins, jewelry, vessels—zakat is wajib when nisab is complete. The value of trade goods must equal 52.5 tolas silver or 7.5 tolas gold. For example, a trader has books for sale; if their value reaches nisab and a year passes, zakat is due. But on tools of trade, zakat is not wajib; e.g., a tailor's sewing machine worth ten thousand pounds, no zakat on the machine itself; only the income saved after expenses and reaching nisab over a year is subject to zakat. Proofs: (1) For trade goods: Samurah b. Jundub reported that the Prophet commanded us to give sadaqah from that which we prepare for sale. (Abu Dawud). (2) For jewelry: Amr b. Shu'ayb's hadith: A woman with a daughter wearing two thick gold bangles came to the Prophet; he asked if she gave zakat for them; she said no; he warned of punishment on the Day of Judgment; so she gave them as sadaqah. (Abu Dawud).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book Thamaratun Najah, explaining the obligation of zakat on various types of wealth. The author begins by presenting the matn (core text) of issue (1152), which states that zakat is obligatory on gold, silver, jewelry, vessels, and trade goods when they reach the nisab. The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams (approx. 52.5 tolas), for gold 20 dinars (approx. 7.5 tolas), and for crops 5 wasq. The matn may seem to say 'on less than five awsuq there is sadaqah', but the author clarifies via hadith that no zakat is due on less than the nisab. The hadith of five awsuq is from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud, used to establish the general principle. Then the author explains two key conditions for zakat: (1) Complete ownership (milk): The example of a mukatib (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom) shows that incomplete ownership negates zakat, supported by a hadith from Jabir. (2) Passage of one year (hawl): Two hadith are cited—one from Ali (to Abu Dawud) specifying the calculation for silver and gold, and another from Ibn Umar (Darqutni) stating no zakat until the year passes. The author then provides the detailed commentary (tashrih), explaining that zakat is due on these assets regardless of form, and on trade goods when their value equals the nisab and a year passes. He distinguishes between trade goods (subject to zakat) and tools of trade (not subject to zakat), illustrating with a tailor's sewing machine. Two additional proofs are given: one for trade goods (hadith of Samurah) and one for jewelry (hadith of Amr b. Shu'ayb). The teacher should emphasize that the Hanafi school relies on these hadith to establish the wajib level of zakat, not fard, and that the conditions of nisab, full ownership, and year are essential.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisaab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory. For silver: 200 dirhams (approx. 52.5 tolas), for gold: 20 dinars (approx. 7.5 tolas), for crops: 5 wasq, for livestock: specified numbers.
مکاتب (mukaatib): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
حول (hawl): The passage of one lunar year over the wealth, a condition for the obligation of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a mukatib's wealth regarding zakat?
A) Zakat is wajib because he owns the wealth.
B) Zakat is not wajib because his ownership is incomplete.
C) Zakat is wajib but delayed until he is freed.
D) Zakat is wajib only if he intends to pay.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of zakat hinges on three conditions: reaching the nisab, full ownership (milk tam), and the passage of one lunar year; proofs from hadith establish these as wajib.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Zakat Conditions: Free from Debt and Basic Needs
Specifies that zakat is only due on wealth free from debt and essential needs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that zakat wealth must be free from debt and basic needs, and apply it by deducting these from nisab calculations.

Core Idea
Zakat is only due on surplus wealth — debts and essential needs are deducted first.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but not all wealth is subject to it. The Hanafi school teaches that zakat is obligatory only on wealth that exceeds immediate debts and essential living expenses. This lesson unpacks that rule using Companion statements as evidence, and shows how it applies today when people have mortgages or annual installment loans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
The matn states three conditions: free from debt (fārigḥ 'an al-dayn), free from basic needs (ḥājah aṣliyyah), and productive (nām). Focus on the first two as explained in the commentary.
The term nām (productive) is a separate condition not elaborated here.
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The text cites two qawl al-ṣaḥābī: (1) Caliph Uthman's sermon: 'This is the month of your zakat; whoever has a debt, pay it, then give zakat on what remains.' (2) Views of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar on a borrower who spends on his family and crops: he repays the debt first.
These are found in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Muwatta Imam Malik, and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalālah
Uthman's command places debt repayment before zakat, implying zakat is only on net wealth after debt settlement. The Companions' practice confirms the principle that essential needs must be covered first.
This reasoning is used to deduct current-year debts and annual living expenses.
4
Apply to modern scenarios
If someone has a bank loan payable in installments, only the portion due in the current year is deducted. Similarly, essential costs (food, clothing, housing) for the year are subtracted before computing zakat.
This is the muftā bihī (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٥٣) فارغ عن الدين وعن حاجته الاصلية نام
ترجمه : (١١٥٣)، ( یہ نصاب) قرض اور حاجت اصلیہ سے فارغ ہو۔ تشریح : یہ نصاب قرض سے بھی فارغ ہو، اور سال بھر تک کھانے پینے سے بھی بچا ہوا ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ،مثلا آدمی کے پاس دس ہزار پونڈ ہے لیکن اس پر چار ہزار پونڈ قرض ہے تو اس کو منہا کر کے صرف چھ ہزار پر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ آج کل پچپیں سال تک قرض بینک سے لیتے ہیں، اور اس کو قسط وار ادا کرتے ہیں، اس لئے علماء نے فرمایا کہ ایک سال میں جتنا قرض دینا ہے اس سال کی آمدنی سے اتنا کم کیا جائے گا، مثلا اس کے پاس دو ہزار پونڈ بچا ہوا ہے اور اس سال بینک کو پانچ سو پونڈ دیا ہے تو ڈیڑھ ہزار پونڈ پر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، کیونکہ اس سال کا قرض اتناہی ادا کرنا ہے۔ وجه : (١) قول صحابی میں ہے . سمعت عثمان يخطب و هو يقول : ان هذا شهر زكوتكم ، فمن كان عليه دين فليؤده ، ثم ليؤد زكاة ما فضل . (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب لا زکاة الا فی فضل، ج رابع ، ص ٧٤ نمبر ١٦ اے موطا امام مالک، الزکوۃ فی الدین ، ص ٢٨٤ رسنن سیھتی ، باب الدین مع الصدقة ج رابع ، ص ٢٤٩، نمبر ٧٦٠٦ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرض ادا کر کے جو باقی بچے اگر وہ نصاب تک پہنچے اور اس پر سال گزر جائے تو اس باقی ماندہ مال میں زکوۃ ہے ورنہ نہیں (٢) قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس و ابن عمر في الرجل يستقرض فينفق على ثمرته و علی اهله قال قال ابن عمر ـ بما استقرض فيقضیه و یزکی ما بقى، قال: و قال ابن عباس يقضى ما انفق على الثمرة ثم يزكي ما بقى (سنن
(1153) Free from debt and from his primary need, productive. Translation: (1153) This nisab is free from debt and basic needs. Explanation: This nisab is free from debt, and also surplus from food and drink expenses for the whole year; then zakat becomes wajib. For example, a person has ten thousand pounds but has four thousand pounds debt; subtract that, zakat is wajib on only six thousand. Today people take loans from banks for many years and pay in installments; so scholars have said: whatever debt is to be paid in that year is deducted from that year's income. For example, he has two thousand pounds saved and this year he pays the bank five hundred pounds; then zakat is wajib on one thousand five hundred pounds, because that year's debt is only that much to pay. Proof: (1) The saying of a Companion: I heard Uthman delivering a sermon saying: 'This is the month of your zakat, so whoever has a debt should pay it, then give zakat on what remains.' (Musannaf Abd ar-Razzaq, Muwatta Imam Malik, Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this athar it is known that after paying the debt, if the remainder reaches nisab and a year passes, then zakat is due on that remainder, otherwise not. (2) The saying of a Companion: From Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar regarding a person who borrows and spends on his fruit and his family: Ibn Umar said: He repays what he borrowed and gives zakat on what remains; Ibn Abbas said: He repays what was spent on the fruit, then gives zakat on what remains. (Sunan).
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling (matn) of issue (1153) which adds two more conditions for zakat: the wealth must be free from debt (fārigḥ 'an al-dayn) and free from basic needs (ḥājah aṣliyyah). The term 'nām' (productive) is also part of the matn, indicating the wealth must be of a type that grows, though the commentary focuses on the first two. The commentary explains that nisab is calculated after deducting debts and after subtracting what is needed for essential living expenses (food, drink, etc.) for the year. A contemporary example is given: if a person has a debt payable in installments, only the portion due in the current year is deducted from the current assets before computing zakat. The proofs come from the sayings of the Companions (qawl al-ṣaḥābī): Uthman's statement instructing people to pay their debts first then give zakat on the remainder, and the view of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that one should repay borrowed money spent on essential needs before calculating zakat on the surplus. This establishes that zakat is on surplus wealth only, not on wealth that is encumbered by debts or allocated for essential living costs.

Key Terms
حاجته الاصلية (haajatuhu al-asliyyah): Essential needs such as food, clothing, and shelter for oneself and dependents for the coming year.
نام (naam): Productive or growing; wealth that has the potential to increase, such as business stock or livestock. This is a condition for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for zakat wealth?
A) It must be free from all debts, past and future.
B) It must be free from debt and basic needs for the year.
C) It must be free from debt only, not basic needs.
D) It must be free from zakat already paid.

Key Takeaway
Zakat in the Hanafi school is calculated on net surplus wealth after subtracting current-year debts and essential living expenses.

Zakat on Trade Goods and Jewelry: The Growth Condition
Ruling with proof on zakat for trade goods and jewellery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for trade goods and jewelry, explain the requirement of growth (nama'), and identify the two hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Zakat is due on trade inventory and gold jewellery because they are capable of growth.

This passage lays the foundation: zakat is only due on wealth that is 'growing' (nami). The author gives examples of trade goods (zakatable) and tools of earning (exempt), then grounds the ruling in two sahih hadith: one for trade goods, one for jewellery. Let us examine how these proofs establish the condition of nama'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that zakat is obligatory on wealth that equals a tola of gold (nisab), is free from debt and essential needs, and is 'nami' (growing).
The author uses 'wajib' but the technical level is fard.
2
Parse the examples
A merchant's books for sale are subject to zakat because they are trade goods (nami). A tailor's sewing machine is a tool of earning (not nami), so exempt. However, the income from it, once saved, becomes zakatable.
Tools of earning are exempt, but profits from them are zakatable when saved.
3
Locate the first dalil
Hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub: the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) commanded charity from 'what we prepare for sale'. The imperative indicates obligation; the phrase specifies trade goods.
This hadith is in Abu Dawud (no. 1562).
4
Locate the second dalil
Hadith of the woman with gold bangles: the Prophet asked if she paid zakat; she did not; he warned her of punishment; she gave them. This shows zakat is due on gold jewellery.
This hadith is in Abu Dawud (no. 1563).
5
Conclude
Both hadith confirm that wealth is zakatable if it is nami, i.e., intended for growth (trade) or inherently growing (gold/silver). Personal tools and consumables are not.
