صلى الله
على قال زهيرا حسبه عن النبي ... وفى البقر في كل ثلاثين تبيع والاربعين مسنة وليس على العوامل شيء (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمۃ ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو جانور کھیتی کے کام آتا ہو اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے (۶) عن عمر و ابن شعیب عن ابيه عن جده عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ليس في الابل العوامل صدقة دار قطنی ، باب لیس فی العوامل صدقته ، ج ثانی ، ص ۸۸، نمبر ۱۹۲۱) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ جانور جو روزمرہ کے کام آتے
ہیں اور ضرورت کی چیز ہیں مثلا ہل جو تنا اور سواری کرنا اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
اصول: حاجت اصلیہ کی چیزوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
Book of Zakat. (1153) Free from debt and from his essential needs, growing. If it equals a tola of gold, then zakat upon it is obligatory. For example, if a merchant has books for selling, and the value of those books equals the nisab and a year passes, then zakat on them is obligatory. But on tools of earning, zakat is not obligatory. For example, a tailor has a sewing machine worth ten thousand pounds, then zakat is not obligatory on the value of that sewing machine. Whatever income comes from that sewing, if after eating and drinking for a year something remains and reaches the nisab, then zakat on it is obligatory. Reason: (1) If [wealth] is for trade, zakat becomes obligatory. For this there is this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub, he said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us to give charity from what we prepared for sale.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on goods when they are for trade, is there zakat on them? p.230, no.1562) In this hadith, it is that if [wealth] is for trade, zakat becomes obligatory. (2) And if it is jewelry, then zakat is obligatory. Its proof is this hadith: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and with her was a daughter of hers, and on the daughter's hands were two thick bangles of gold. He said to her: 'Do you give the zakat of this?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'Would it please you that Allah should adorn you with them on the Day of Resurrection as two bracelets of fire?' He said: 'So she threw them to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: They are for Allah and His Messenger.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on what is buried treasure? And zakat on jewelry, p.230, no.1563) This hadith indicates that zakat is due on jewelry. Translation of (1153): This nisab is free from debt and from essential needs. Explanation: This nisab is also free from debt, and what remains after eating and drinking for a year, then zakat becomes obligatory. For example, a person has ten thousand pounds but he has a debt of four thousand pounds, then subtracting that, zakat is obligatory only on six thousand. Nowadays, people take loans from banks for [؟] years and pay them in installments. Therefore, scholars have said that whatever debt is to be paid in one year, that amount will be deducted from that year's income. For example, he has two thousand pounds saved, and this year he pays the bank five hundred pounds, then zakat is obligatory on fifteen hundred pounds, because the debt of this year is only that much to be paid. Reasons: (1) There is a saying of a Companion: 'I heard Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) giving a sermon, and he said: This is the month of your zakat. So whoever has a debt, let him pay it, then let him pay zakat on what remains.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq, chapter: No zakat except on surplus, vol.4, p.74, no.16? and Muwatta Imam Malik, Zakat on debt, p.284 and Sunan [؟], chapter: Debt with charity, vol.4, p.249, no.7606) From this Athar, it is understood that after paying the debt, whatever remains, if it reaches the nisab and a year passes over it, then zakat is due on that remaining wealth, otherwise not. (2) There is a saying of a Companion: From Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar concerning a man who borrows and spends on his crops and his family. He said: Ibn Umar said: He pays what he borrowed, then gives zakat on what remains. He said: And Ibn Abbas said: He pays what he spent on the crops, then gives zakat on what remains. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Debt with charity, vol.4, p.249, no.7608, Book of Zakat) From this Athar, it is understood that first he will pay the debt, then what remains, if it reaches the nisab, then zakat becomes obligatory on it. And if it does not reach the nisab, for example, after paying the debt only one hundred and ninety dirhams remain, and one hundred and ninety is less than the nisab, therefore zakat will not be obligatory on him. (3) Becoming free from essential needs. Its proof is this hadith: 'Abu Hurayrah heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: The best charity is what is given from surplus wealth, and start with those you support.' (Bukhari, chapter: No charity except from surplus, p.192, no.1426) From this hadith, it is understood that after exceeding necessity, zakat becomes obligatory. (4) From Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave nor his horse.' (Bukhari, chapter: There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave, p.237, no.1464? and Muslim, chapter: No zakat upon a Muslim regarding his slave and his horse, p.316, no.2273/982) From this hadith, it is understood that there is no zakat on a slave for service and a horse for riding. And the reason is that these things are people's necessities. Using qiyas, all the above necessities are analogized to them. (5) There is a hadith from [؟] from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'And regarding cows: for every thirty a tabi', and for forty a musinnah, and there is nothing on working animals.' (Abu Dawud, chapter: Zakat on grazing livestock, p.228, no.1572) This hadith indicates that an animal used for agricultural work has no zakat on it. (6) From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on working camels.' (Dar Qutni, chapter: No sadaqah on working animals, vol.2, p.88, no.1921) From these ahadith, it is understood that animals used for daily work and which are necessities, such as plowing and riding, have no zakat on them. Principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the conditions for zakat obligation. The text establishes that zakat is only due on wealth that is free from debt and basic necessities, and is capable of growth. The author begins by stating the condition: wealth must be free from debt and essential needs, and must be growing (nami). He then gives examples: a merchant's books for sale are subject to zakat if they reach nisab and a year passes, but a tailor's sewing machine (a tool of trade) is not subject to zakat because it is an essential need. However, the income from it, if saved and reaching nisab, is zakatable. Then the author provides multiple textual proofs: (1) Hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet commanded charity from goods prepared for sale, establishing zakat on trade goods. (2) Hadith about jewelry, showing zakat is due on gold jewelry. (3) The ruling is then explained in Urdu: nisab must be surplus after debts and basic expenses. The author notes that debts reduce the zakatable amount, and scholars rule that only the debt due in the current year is deducted. (4) Proof from the practice of Uthman and the opinions of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that debts are paid first, then zakat on the remainder. (5) Hadith about surplus charity (best charity is from surplus). (6) Hadith that there is no zakat on a slave or horse, which are essential needs, and by qiyas all essential needs are excluded. (7) Hadith on working cattle and camels, again excluding assets used for daily work. The passage concludes with the principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.

Key Terms
نامی (nami): Growing or productive; wealth capable of increase, either actually (trade goods) or potentially (gold/silver kept at home).
نصاب (nisab): Minimum threshold of wealth triggering zakat: 20 mithqal gold (approx. 87.48g) or 200 dirhams silver (approx. 612g).
عروض تجارة (urud tijarah): Goods intended for trade; inventory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT subject to zakat?
A) Gold jewelry kept for personal use
B) Books held by a merchant for sale
C) A sewing machine used by a tailor for his business
D) Profit from the sewing machine saved for a year and reaching nisab

Key Takeaway
Zakat is due only on wealth that is growing (nami), such as trade goods and gold jewelry, not on tools of earning or personal essentials.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Zakat Obligation: Deducting Debts
Ruling with proof on deducting debts before calculating zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that zakat is calculated on wealth after deducting debts due in the current year, and cite the proofs from the Companions.

Core Idea
Zakat is due only on surplus wealth after paying immediate debts.

This passage clarifies an important practical aspect: zakat is not due on the full amount of wealth if the owner has debts. The author explains that only the surplus after paying debts due in the current year is subject to zakat. The proof is drawn from the practice of Caliph Uthman and the opinions of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. Let us examine how debt deduction works and what evidence supports it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling
Zakat is due on wealth that is 'free from debt'. This means debts are subtracted from total assets before calculating zakat.
Only debts due in the current year are deducted, not long-term installments.
2
Apply the example
If a person has £10,000 but owes £4,000, zakat is only on £6,000. For bank loans paid in installments, only the annual installment is deducted.
Example from the text: £2,000 saved, £500 annual payment → zakat on £1,500.
3
Examine the proof from Uthman
Uthman (رض) said: 'Whoever has a debt, let him pay it, then let him pay zakat on what remains.' This shows debt repayment takes priority.
Athar in Musannaf Abdur Razzaq.
4
Examine the proof from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar
Both agreed that a farmer who borrows for expenses should pay the debt first, then give zakat on the remainder.
Athar in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
5
Apply the principle
If after debt deduction the remainder is below nisab, no zakat. Example: 190 dirhams remain; nisab is 200 dirhams, so no zakat.

تولہ سونے کے برابر ہو تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہے، مثلا تاجر کے پاس بیچنے کے لئے کتا میں ہیں، تو ان کتابوں کی قیمت نصاب کے برابر ہو اور سال گزر جائے تو ان پر زکوۃ ہے۔ لیکن آلات کسب پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے ، مثلا درزی کے پاس دس ہزار پونڈ کی سلائی مشین ہے تو اس سلائی مشین کی قیمت پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ، اس سلائی میں جو آمدنی ہوگی وہ سال بھر کھا پی کر بچ جائے اور نصاب کو پہنچ جائے تو اس پر زکوۃ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) تجارت کے لئے ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ، عن سمرة بن جندب قال اما بعد فان رسول الله الا الله كان يأمرنا ان نخرج الصدقة من الذى نعد للبيع - ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب العروض اذا كانت لتجارة صل فيها زكوة ص ۲۳۰، نمبر ۱۵۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تجارت کے لئے ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ (۲) اور زیور ہو تو زکوۃ واجب ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان امراة اتت رسول الله له و معها ابنة لها وفي يد ابنتهـا مسـكتـان غـلـيـظـتـان مـن ذهـب فقال لها اتعطين زكاة هذا ؟قالت لا قال أيسرك ان يسورک الـلـه بهـمـا يــوم القيامة سوارين من نار ؟ قال فخلعتهما الى النبي عل و قالت هما لله و لرسوله (ابو داؤد شریف، باب الکنز ما هو؟ وزكوة الحلی ، ص ۲۳۰، نمبر ۱۵۶۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ زیور میں زکوۃ ہے۔
صلى الله
ترجمه : (۱۱۵۳)، ( یہ نصاب) قرض اور حاجت اصلیہ سے فارغ ہو۔ تشریح : یہ نصاب قرض سے بھی فارغ ہو، اور سال بھر تک کھانے پینے سے بھی بچا ہوا ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ،مثلا آدمی کے پاس دس ہزار پونڈ ہے لیکن اس پر چار ہزار پونڈ قرض ہے تو اس کو منہا کر کے صرف چھ ہزار پر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ آج کل پچپیں سال تک قرض بینک سے لیتے ہیں، اور اس کو قسط وار ادا کرتے ہیں، اس لئے علماء نے فرمایا کہ ایک سال میں جتنا قرض دینا ہے اس سال کی آمدنی سے اتنا کم کیا جائے گا، مثلا اس کے پاس دو ہزار پونڈ بچا ہوا ہے اور اس سال بینک کو پانچ سو پونڈ دیا ہے تو ڈیڑھ ہزار پونڈ پر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، کیونکہ اس سال کا قرض اتناہی ادا کرنا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) قول صحابی میں ہے . سمعت عثمان يخطب و هو يقول : ان هذا شهر زكوتكم ، فمن كان عليه دين فليؤده ، ثم ليؤد زكاة ما فضل . (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب لا زکاة الا فی فضل، ج رابع ، ص ۷۴ نمبر ۱۶ اے موطا امام مالک، الزکوۃ فی الدین ، ص ۲۸۴ رسنن سیھتی ، باب الدین مع الصدقة ج رابع ، ص ۲۴۹، نمبر ۷۶۰۶ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرض ادا کر کے جو باقی بچے اگر وہ نصاب تک پہنچے اور اس پر سال گزر جائے تو اس باقی ماندہ مال میں زکوۃ ہے ورنہ نہیں (۲) قول صحابی
يبدأ
میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس و ابن عمر في الرجل يستقرض فينفق على ثمرته و علی اهله قال قال ابن عمر ـ بما استقرض فيقضیه و یزکی ما بقى، قال: و قال ابن عباس يقضى ما انفق على الثمرة ثم يزكي ما بقى (سنن
للبيهقى
تھی ، باب الدین مع الصدقة ج رابع ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۷۶۰۸، کتاب الزکوۃ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہلے قرض ادا کرے گا پھر جو بچے گا اگر وہ نصاب تک پہنچ جائے تو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر وہ نصاب تک نہ پہنچ سکا مثلا قرض ادا کرنے کے بعد ایک سو نوے درہم ہی رہتا ہے اور ایک سونوے درہم نصاب سے کم ہے اس لئے اس پر زکوۃ فرض نہیں ہوگی ۔ (۳) حاجت اصلیہ سے فارغ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمع ابا هريرة عن النبي الله قال خير الصدقة ماكان عن ظهر غنى وابدأ بمن تعول (بخاری شریف، باب لا صدقته الا عن ظهر غنی، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۱۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت سے زیادہ ہونے کے بعد زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ (۴) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الا الله قال ليس على المسلم صدقة في عبده ولا في فرسه ( بخاری شریف، باب ليس على المسلم فی عبدہ صدقہ، ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۱۴۶۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب لا زکوۃ علی المسلم فی عبدہ وفرسه، ص ۳۱۶ نمبر ۲۲۷۳/۹۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خدمت کے غلام اور سواری کے گھوڑے میں زکوہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ چیزیں لوگوں کی ضرورت کی چیزیں ہیں۔ انہیں پر اوپر کی تمام ضروریات کی چیزوں کو قیاس کر لیں (۵) حدیث میں ہے عـــن
صلى الله
على قال زهيرا حسبه عن النبي ... وفى البقر في كل ثلاثين تبيع والاربعين مسنة وليس على العوامل شيء (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمۃ ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو جانور کھیتی کے کام آتا ہو اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے (۶) عن عمر و ابن شعیب عن ابيه عن جده عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ليس في الابل العوامل صدقة دار قطنی ، باب لیس فی العوامل صدقته ، ج ثانی ، ص ۸۸، نمبر ۱۹۲۱) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ جانور جو روزمرہ کے کام آتے
ہیں اور ضرورت کی چیز ہیں مثلا ہل جو تنا اور سواری کرنا اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
اصول: حاجت اصلیہ کی چیزوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
Book of Zakat. (1153) Free from debt and from his essential needs, growing. If it equals a tola of gold, then zakat upon it is obligatory. For example, if a merchant has books for selling, and the value of those books equals the nisab and a year passes, then zakat on them is obligatory. But on tools of earning, zakat is not obligatory. For example, a tailor has a sewing machine worth ten thousand pounds, then zakat is not obligatory on the value of that sewing machine. Whatever income comes from that sewing, if after eating and drinking for a year something remains and reaches the nisab, then zakat on it is obligatory. Reason: (1) If [wealth] is for trade, zakat becomes obligatory. For this there is this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub, he said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us to give charity from what we prepared for sale.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on goods when they are for trade, is there zakat on them? p.230, no.1562) In this hadith, it is that if [wealth] is for trade, zakat becomes obligatory. (2) And if it is jewelry, then zakat is obligatory. Its proof is this hadith: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and with her was a daughter of hers, and on the daughter's hands were two thick bangles of gold. He said to her: 'Do you give the zakat of this?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'Would it please you that Allah should adorn you with them on the Day of Resurrection as two bracelets of fire?' He said: 'So she threw them to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: They are for Allah and His Messenger.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on what is buried treasure? And zakat on jewelry, p.230, no.1563) This hadith indicates that zakat is due on jewelry. Translation of (1153): This nisab is free from debt and from essential needs. Explanation: This nisab is also free from debt, and what remains after eating and drinking for a year, then zakat becomes obligatory. For example, a person has ten thousand pounds but he has a debt of four thousand pounds, then subtracting that, zakat is obligatory only on six thousand. Nowadays, people take loans from banks for [؟] years and pay them in installments. Therefore, scholars have said that whatever debt is to be paid in one year, that amount will be deducted from that year's income. For example, he has two thousand pounds saved, and this year he pays the bank five hundred pounds, then zakat is obligatory on fifteen hundred pounds, because the debt of this year is only that much to be paid. Reasons: (1) There is a saying of a Companion: 'I heard Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) giving a sermon, and he said: This is the month of your zakat. So whoever has a debt, let him pay it, then let him pay zakat on what remains.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq, chapter: No zakat except on surplus, vol.4, p.74, no.16? and Muwatta Imam Malik, Zakat on debt, p.284 and Sunan [؟], chapter: Debt with charity, vol.4, p.249, no.7606) From this Athar, it is understood that after paying the debt, whatever remains, if it reaches the nisab and a year passes over it, then zakat is due on that remaining wealth, otherwise not. (2) There is a saying of a Companion: From Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar concerning a man who borrows and spends on his crops and his family. He said: Ibn Umar said: He pays what he borrowed, then gives zakat on what remains. He said: And Ibn Abbas said: He pays what he spent on the crops, then gives zakat on what remains. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Debt with charity, vol.4, p.249, no.7608, Book of Zakat) From this Athar, it is understood that first he will pay the debt, then what remains, if it reaches the nisab, then zakat becomes obligatory on it. And if it does not reach the nisab, for example, after paying the debt only one hundred and ninety dirhams remain, and one hundred and ninety is less than the nisab, therefore zakat will not be obligatory on him. (3) Becoming free from essential needs. Its proof is this hadith: 'Abu Hurayrah heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: The best charity is what is given from surplus wealth, and start with those you support.' (Bukhari, chapter: No charity except from surplus, p.192, no.1426) From this hadith, it is understood that after exceeding necessity, zakat becomes obligatory. (4) From Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave nor his horse.' (Bukhari, chapter: There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave, p.237, no.1464? and Muslim, chapter: No zakat upon a Muslim regarding his slave and his horse, p.316, no.2273/982) From this hadith, it is understood that there is no zakat on a slave for service and a horse for riding. And the reason is that these things are people's necessities. Using qiyas, all the above necessities are analogized to them. (5) There is a hadith from [؟] from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'And regarding cows: for every thirty a tabi', and for forty a musinnah, and there is nothing on working animals.' (Abu Dawud, chapter: Zakat on grazing livestock, p.228, no.1572) This hadith indicates that an animal used for agricultural work has no zakat on it. (6) From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on working camels.' (Dar Qutni, chapter: No sadaqah on working animals, vol.2, p.88, no.1921) From these ahadith, it is understood that animals used for daily work and which are necessities, such as plowing and riding, have no zakat on them. Principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the conditions for zakat obligation. The text establishes that zakat is only due on wealth that is free from debt and basic necessities, and is capable of growth. The author begins by stating the condition: wealth must be free from debt and essential needs, and must be growing (nami). He then gives examples: a merchant's books for sale are subject to zakat if they reach nisab and a year passes, but a tailor's sewing machine (a tool of trade) is not subject to zakat because it is an essential need. However, the income from it, if saved and reaching nisab, is zakatable. Then the author provides multiple textual proofs: (1) Hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet commanded charity from goods prepared for sale, establishing zakat on trade goods. (2) Hadith about jewelry, showing zakat is due on gold jewelry. (3) The ruling is then explained in Urdu: nisab must be surplus after debts and basic expenses. The author notes that debts reduce the zakatable amount, and scholars rule that only the debt due in the current year is deducted. (4) Proof from the practice of Uthman and the opinions of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that debts are paid first, then zakat on the remainder. (5) Hadith about surplus charity (best charity is from surplus). (6) Hadith that there is no zakat on a slave or horse, which are essential needs, and by qiyas all essential needs are excluded. (7) Hadith on working cattle and camels, again excluding assets used for daily work. The passage concludes with the principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.

Key Terms
قرض (qard): Debt; a financial obligation owed by the person.
فضل (fadl): Surplus; wealth remaining after deducting debts and essential needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for deducting debts before calculating zakat?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) The practice of the Companions Uthman, Ibn Abbas, and Ibn Umar
C) A consensus of all four schools
D) An analogy to charity

Key Takeaway
Zakat is calculated on net wealth after subtracting debts due in the current year, as established by the practice of the Companions.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner

Zakat Obligation: Exempting Essential Needs (Hajat Asliyyah)
Ruling with proof on exempting essential needs from zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define essential needs (hajat asliyyah) in Hanafi fiqh, identify which assets are exempt from zakat based on this principle, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due on assets that are essential for a person's daily living and livelihood.

This passage explains the second condition: wealth must be free from essential needs (hajat asliyyah). The author provides hadith proofs showing that items like slaves for service, horses for riding, and working animals are free from zakat. By qiyas, all essential needs — including food, clothing, shelter, tools of trade — are exempt. Let us examine the textual evidence and the scope of this exemption.

Guided Path
1
Comprehend the principle
Essential needs (hajat asliyyah) are items without which a person cannot live or maintain their livelihood. They are exempt from zakat.
Examples: food, clothing, shelter, tools of trade, animals for transport/farming.
2
Analyze the first hadith (surplus charity)
The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) said: 'The best charity is what is given from surplus wealth.' This implies that charity is only from surplus, and essential needs are not surplus.
Hadith from Bukhari (no. 1426).
3
Analyze the second hadith (slave and horse)
The Prophet said: 'There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave nor his horse.' These are essential for service and transport, hence exempt.
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze the third hadith (working animals)
The Prophet said: 'Nothing on working animals' (cows, camels used for agriculture). This extends the exemption to all tools of livelihood.
Hadith from Abu Dawud and Dar Qutni.
5
Apply qiyas
All essential needs are analogized to these exempted items. The principle is: anything that is a basic necessity for living or earning a livelihood is not subject to zakat.
The passage concludes: 'Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.'

(مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب لا زکاة الا فی فضل، ج رابع ، ص ۷۴ نمبر ۱۶ اے موطا امام مالک، الزکوۃ فی الدین ، ص ۲۸۴ رسنن سیھتی ، باب الدین مع الصدقة ج رابع ، ص ۲۴۹، نمبر ۷۶۰۶ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرض ادا کر کے جو باقی بچے اگر وہ نصاب تک پہنچے اور اس پر سال گزر جائے تو اس باقی ماندہ مال میں زکوۃ ہے ورنہ نہیں (۲) قول صحابی

تھی ، باب الدین مع الصدقة ج رابع ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۷۶۰۸، کتاب الزکوۃ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہلے قرض ادا کرے گا پھر جو بچے گا اگر وہ نصاب تک پہنچ جائے تو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر وہ نصاب تک نہ پہنچ سکا مثلا قرض ادا کرنے کے بعد ایک سو نوے درہم ہی رہتا ہے اور ایک سونوے درہم نصاب سے کم ہے اس لئے اس پر زکوۃ فرض نہیں ہوگی ۔ (۳) حاجت اصلیہ سے فارغ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمع ابا هريرة عن النبي الله قال خير الصدقة ماكان عن ظهر غنى وابدأ بمن تعول (بخاری شریف، باب لا صدقته الا عن ظهر غنی، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۱۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت سے زیادہ ہونے کے بعد زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ (۴) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الا الله قال ليس على المسلم صدقة في عبده ولا في فرسه ( بخاری شریف، باب ليس على المسلم فی عبدہ صدقہ، ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۱۴۶۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب لا زکوۃ علی المسلم فی عبدہ وفرسه، ص ۳۱۶ نمبر ۲۲۷۳/۹۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خدمت کے غلام اور سواری کے گھوڑے میں زکوہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ چیزیں لوگوں کی ضرورت کی چیزیں ہیں۔ انہیں پر اوپر کی تمام ضروریات کی چیزوں کو قیاس کر لیں (۵) حدیث میں ہے عـــن
صلى الله
على قال زهيرا حسبه عن النبي ... وفى البقر في كل ثلاثين تبيع والاربعين مسنة وليس على العوامل شيء (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمۃ ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو جانور کھیتی کے کام آتا ہو اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے (۶) عن عمر و ابن شعیب عن ابيه عن جده عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ليس في الابل العوامل صدقة دار قطنی ، باب لیس فی العوامل صدقته ، ج ثانی ، ص ۸۸، نمبر ۱۹۲۱) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ جانور جو روزمرہ کے کام آتے
ہیں اور ضرورت کی چیز ہیں مثلا ہل جو تنا اور سواری کرنا اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
اصول: حاجت اصلیہ کی چیزوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
Book of Zakat. (1153) Free from debt and from his essential needs, growing. If it equals a tola of gold, then zakat upon it is obligatory. For example, if a merchant has books for selling, and the value of those books equals the nisab and a year passes, then zakat on them is obligatory. But on tools of earning, zakat is not obligatory. For example, a tailor has a sewing machine worth ten thousand pounds, then zakat is not obligatory on the value of that sewing machine. Whatever income comes from that sewing, if after eating and drinking for a year something remains and reaches the nisab, then zakat on it is obligatory. Reason: (1) If [wealth] is for trade, zakat becomes obligatory. For this there is this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub, he said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us to give charity from what we prepared for sale.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on goods when they are for trade, is there zakat on them? p.230, no.1562) In this hadith, it is that if [wealth] is for trade, zakat becomes obligatory. (2) And if it is jewelry, then zakat is obligatory. Its proof is this hadith: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and with her was a daughter of hers, and on the daughter's hands were two thick bangles of gold. He said to her: 'Do you give the zakat of this?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'Would it please you that Allah should adorn you with them on the Day of Resurrection as two bracelets of fire?' He said: 'So she threw them to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: They are for Allah and His Messenger.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on what is buried treasure? And zakat on jewelry, p.230, no.1563) This hadith indicates that zakat is due on jewelry. Translation of (1153): This nisab is free from debt and from essential needs. Explanation: This nisab is also free from debt, and what remains after eating and drinking for a year, then zakat becomes obligatory. For example, a person has ten thousand pounds but he has a debt of four thousand pounds, then subtracting that, zakat is obligatory only on six thousand. Nowadays, people take loans from banks for [؟] years and pay them in installments. Therefore, scholars have said that whatever debt is to be paid in one year, that amount will be deducted from that year's income. For example, he has two thousand pounds saved, and this year he pays the bank five hundred pounds, then zakat is obligatory on fifteen hundred pounds, because the debt of this year is only that much to be paid. Reasons: (1) There is a saying of a Companion: 'I heard Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) giving a sermon, and he said: This is the month of your zakat. So whoever has a debt, let him pay it, then let him pay zakat on what remains.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq, chapter: No zakat except on surplus, vol.4, p.74, no.16? and Muwatta Imam Malik, Zakat on debt, p.284 and Sunan [؟], chapter: Debt with charity, vol.4, p.249, no.7606) From this Athar, it is understood that after paying the debt, whatever remains, if it reaches the nisab and a year passes over it, then zakat is due on that remaining wealth, otherwise not. (2) There is a saying of a Companion: From Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar concerning a man who borrows and spends on his crops and his family. He said: Ibn Umar said: He pays what he borrowed, then gives zakat on what remains. He said: And Ibn Abbas said: He pays what he spent on the crops, then gives zakat on what remains. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Debt with charity, vol.4, p.249, no.7608, Book of Zakat) From this Athar, it is understood that first he will pay the debt, then what remains, if it reaches the nisab, then zakat becomes obligatory on it. And if it does not reach the nisab, for example, after paying the debt only one hundred and ninety dirhams remain, and one hundred and ninety is less than the nisab, therefore zakat will not be obligatory on him. (3) Becoming free from essential needs. Its proof is this hadith: 'Abu Hurayrah heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: The best charity is what is given from surplus wealth, and start with those you support.' (Bukhari, chapter: No charity except from surplus, p.192, no.1426) From this hadith, it is understood that after exceeding necessity, zakat becomes obligatory. (4) From Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave nor his horse.' (Bukhari, chapter: There is no charity upon a Muslim regarding his slave, p.237, no.1464? and Muslim, chapter: No zakat upon a Muslim regarding his slave and his horse, p.316, no.2273/982) From this hadith, it is understood that there is no zakat on a slave for service and a horse for riding. And the reason is that these things are people's necessities. Using qiyas, all the above necessities are analogized to them. (5) There is a hadith from [؟] from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'And regarding cows: for every thirty a tabi', and for forty a musinnah, and there is nothing on working animals.' (Abu Dawud, chapter: Zakat on grazing livestock, p.228, no.1572) This hadith indicates that an animal used for agricultural work has no zakat on it. (6) From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on working camels.' (Dar Qutni, chapter: No sadaqah on working animals, vol.2, p.88, no.1921) From these ahadith, it is understood that animals used for daily work and which are necessities, such as plowing and riding, have no zakat on them. Principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the conditions for zakat obligation. The text establishes that zakat is only due on wealth that is free from debt and basic necessities, and is capable of growth. The author begins by stating the condition: wealth must be free from debt and essential needs, and must be growing (nami). He then gives examples: a merchant's books for sale are subject to zakat if they reach nisab and a year passes, but a tailor's sewing machine (a tool of trade) is not subject to zakat because it is an essential need. However, the income from it, if saved and reaching nisab, is zakatable. Then the author provides multiple textual proofs: (1) Hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet commanded charity from goods prepared for sale, establishing zakat on trade goods. (2) Hadith about jewelry, showing zakat is due on gold jewelry. (3) The ruling is then explained in Urdu: nisab must be surplus after debts and basic expenses. The author notes that debts reduce the zakatable amount, and scholars rule that only the debt due in the current year is deducted. (4) Proof from the practice of Uthman and the opinions of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that debts are paid first, then zakat on the remainder. (5) Hadith about surplus charity (best charity is from surplus). (6) Hadith that there is no zakat on a slave or horse, which are essential needs, and by qiyas all essential needs are excluded. (7) Hadith on working cattle and camels, again excluding assets used for daily work. The passage concludes with the principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of essential need.

Key Terms
حاجت اصلیہ (hajat asliyyah): Basic essential needs such as food, clothing, shelter, tools of trade, and animals for transportation or farming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith specifically exempts animals used for agricultural work from zakat?
A) The hadith of surplus charity
B) The hadith of the slave and horse
C) The hadith on working cattle (ليس على العوامل شيء)
D) The hadith on gold jewelry

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not due on essential needs, including tools of trade and animals for livelihood, as proven by multiple hadith and qiyas.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat Requires Growth Even Potentially
Explains the condition of nama' for zakat with forms of growth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that wealth must be nami (growing) for zakat, and apply it to distinguish zakatable assets from non-zakatable assets.

Core Idea
For zakat, wealth must be growing — even if only potentially, like gold saved at home.

Zakat is not due on just any wealth; it must be wealth that is capable of increase. This lesson explains the Hanafi concept of nama' (growth), including both actual growth and potential growth (taqdiran). Understanding this condition helps you correctly determine which assets are zakatable and which are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text states that zakat is only required on wealth that is 'nami' (growing). Note that this includes both actual growth (like livestock reproducing) and potential growth (like gold that could be traded).
The phrase 'wa law taqdiran' means even if the growth is only estimable/potential.
2
Distinguish forms of growth
List the four categories of growth mentioned: (1) grazing livestock, (2) trade goods, (3) gold/silver used in trade, (4) gold/silver kept at home or as jewelry. The first two are actual; the last two are potential.
Potential growth is recognized by legal consideration (taqdir), not physical increase.
3
Apply the condition to excluded wealth
Wealth that is not even potentially growing is not zakatable. The example given is an animal fed at home: it does not grow by itself, so no zakat.
This is based on the hadith mentioning 'sa'imah' (grazing) as a condition.
4
Examine the proof
The author cites the hadith: 'For every grazing camel, for forty, a bint labun.' The word 'sa'imah' indicates that only naturally growing livestock are zakatable, supporting the condition of nama'.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud (no.1575) and is used to derive the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۱۵۴)، نامی ہوا گر چہ تقدیراً۔
تشريح : نامی کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ مال بڑھنے والا ہو ۔ بڑھنے کی تین شکلیں ہیں [1] اونٹ وغیرہ چر کر بڑھنے والا ہے۔[۲] تجارت کا مال تجارت کی وجہ سے بڑھنے والا ہے۔ [۳] اور سونا چاندی تجارت میں لگائے تو بڑھے گا [۴] اور برتن یا زیور کی شکل میں ہو یا درہم اور دنا نیر گھر میں رکھا ہو تب بھی اس کو بڑھنے والا مان لیا گیا ہے، اس لئے یہ تقدیری طور پر بڑھنے والا ہے، اس لئے تقدیری طور پر بڑھنے والا ہو تب بھی اس پر زکوۃ واجب ہے، لیکن اگر تقدیری طور پر بھی بڑھنے والا نہ ہو تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے،مثلا جو جانور گھر پر کھا کر بڑا ہورہا ہے وہ تقدیری طور پر بھی بڑھنے والا نہیں ہے کیونکہ گھر کا کھا کر بڑھ رہا ہے اس لئے اس میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے وجه : عن بهز بن حكيم عن ابيه عن جده ان رسول الله الله قال في كل سائمة ابل في اربعين بنت لبون ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۵) اس حدیث میں سائمہ [ چرنے والا] سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ مال نامی ہو
Translation of (1154): Growing even if estimably. Explanation: 'Nami' means that wealth is growing. There are three forms of growth: [1] Camels etc. grow by grazing; [2] Trade goods grow by trading; [3] Gold and silver, if used in trade, will grow; [4] And if it is in the form of vessels or jewelry, or dirhams and dinars kept at home, even then it is considered growing, so estimably it is growing. Therefore, if it is growing estimably, zakat on it is obligatory. But if it is not growing even estimably, then zakat on it is not obligatory. For example, an animal that is growing by eating at home is not growing even estimably because it is growing by eating at home, therefore there is no zakat on it. Reason: From Bahz ibn Hakim from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'For every grazing camel, for forty, a bint labun.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on zakat of grazing livestock, p.233, no.1575) In this hadith, 'sa'imah' (grazing) indicates that wealth must be growing.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the condition that wealth must be 'nami' (growing) for zakat to be obligatory. The author translates the phrase 'wa law taqdiran' (even if estimably). He explains that 'nami' means wealth that increases or is capable of increase. Growth can be actual or potential. Actual growth: (1) grazing livestock increase by natural reproduction; (2) trade goods increase through profit. Potential growth: (3) gold and silver, even if not invested, are considered potentially growing because they can be used in trade; similarly (4) vessels, jewelry, or cash kept at home are considered growing by estimable potential (taqdiran). If wealth is not even potentially growing, such as a domestic animal fed at home, it is not subject to zakat. The proof is the hadith about zakat on grazing camels, where the term 'sa'imah' (grazing) indicates that only wealth which grows by itself (e.g., by grazing) is zakatable. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that zakat is linked to growth.

Key Terms
نامی (nami): Wealth that increases or is capable of increase, whether actually (like breeding livestock or trade goods) or potentially (like gold or silver kept at home).
تقدیراً (taqdīran): Estimably; by legal consideration, not actual physical increase. Gold and silver are considered growing because they can be used for trade.
سائمہ (sā'imah): Grazing livestock that feed themselves in pastures, as opposed to animals fed at home. Such animals are considered growing naturally and thus zakatable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following assets is considered 'nami' (growing) in the Hanafi school according to this passage?
A) A cow fed at home for dairy
B) Silver coins kept in a safe
C) A horse used for riding
D) Books in a home library

Key Takeaway
Zakat is due on any wealth that is actually or potentially growing; idle gold and silver are considered potentially growing.

The Hawl Condition for Zakat and the Rule of Mustafad
Establishes hawl condition and mustafad rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of hawl for zakat and apply the Hanafi rule that mustafad wealth does not require a separate year.

Core Idea
Zakat becomes wajib only after a full year over the nisab; mustafad shares the original year.

This passage establishes one of the key conditions for zakat: the passage of a full lunar year (hawl) over the original nisab. It also clarifies how wealth acquired during the year (mustafad) is treated — a point of frequent misunderstanding. Understanding the distinction between original nisab and mustafad is essential for correctly calculating zakat deadlines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its ruling
Note that the passage states: 'liwujub ada'iha hawl al-hawl 'ala al-nisab al-asli'. This means the obligation to pay zakat is conditional upon the passage of a full year over the original nisab. The ruling level is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is ahad.
The condition applies only to the original nisab, not to mustafad.
2
Distinguish between original nisab and mustafad
Original nisab (nisab asli) is the wealth at the start of the year. Mustafad is any additional wealth acquired during the year. The passage gives the example: Zayd had less than 200 dirhams, then in Shawwal he acquires 200 dirhams — that is his original nisab. If in Muharram he earns another 100 dirhams, that is mustafad.
Mustafad does not start its own year; it is added to the original nisab's year.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage cites two hadith: one from 'Ali (mawquf) and one from Ibn 'Umar. The key phrase 'hāla 'alayhi al-hawl' (a year has passed over it) directly proves the condition. The Hanafi school uses these ahadith as zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
The hadith from 'Ali is considered mawquf but accepted as proof in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Take Zayd's case: Original nisab of 200 dirhams on 1 Shawwal. He acquires 100 dirhams on 1 Muharram. The year for the original nisab ends on next 1 Shawwal. The 100 dirhams does not require its own year; zakat on the total 300 dirhams is due on that next 1 Shawwal.
If the original nisab is lost before the year ends, no zakat is due.
5
Note the practical consequence
If someone mistakenly believes mustafad requires a separate year, they may delay zakat on that portion. The correct Hanafi position is that mustafad follows the year of the original nisab, ensuring simultaneous payment.
This ruling is unanimous (muttafaq alayh) among the Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۵۵) وشرط وجوب ادائها حولان الحول على النصاب الاصلى 

ترجمه : (۱۱۵۵) اور زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کے وجوب کے لئے اصلی نصاب پر سال گذر نا شرط ہے۔

تشریح : ایک نصاب ہے اصلی، اور دوسرا نصاب ہوتا ہے مستفاد ۔ [1] نصاب اصلی ۔ مثلا زید کے پاس پہلے دوسو درہم سے کم تھا شوال میں دو سو درہم ہوا، تو یہ نصاب اصلی ہے اس پر سال گزرے تو اگلے سال شوال میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی [۲] آگئے محرم میں ایک سودرہم اور کمایا تو اس کو مال مستفاد، کہتے ہیں ، اس مال مستفاد پر سال گزرنا ضروری نہیں ہے ، شوال میں اصلی نصاب کے ساتھ اس کی زکوۃ بھی واجب ہوگی۔

وجه : (۱) سال گزرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عـن عـلـى عن النبى الله بعض اول الحديث قال فاذا كانت لک مائتا در هم و حال عليه الحول ففيها خمسة دراهم ولیس علیک شیء يعني في الذهب حتى يكون لک عشرون دينارا فاذا كانت لک عشرون دينارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلک (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ، ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نصاب پر سال گزر جائے تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ [۲] عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا زكوة في مال امرئ حتى يحول عليه الحول ( دار قطنی ، باب وجوب الزکوۃ بالحول ، ج ثانی، ص ۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۷۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ مال نصاب پر سال گزرنے کے بعد واجب ہوتی ہے۔
(1155) And the condition for its (zakat) payment is the passage of a full year over the original nisab. 

Translation: (1155) And for the obligation of paying zakat, the passing of a year over the original nisab is a condition.

Explanation: There is an original nisab, and a second nisab called mustafad. [1] Original nisab: e.g., Zayd had less than two hundred dirhams, then in Shawwal he got two hundred dirhams. This is the original nisab. If a year passes over this, then next Shawwal zakat becomes wajib. [2] If in Muharram he earns another hundred dirhams, this is called mustafad wealth. For this mustafad wealth, it is not necessary that a year passes; with the original nisab in Shawwal, its zakat will also become wajib.

Proof: (1) The evidence for the passing of a year is this hadith: From 'Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him), part of the hadith: 'When you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes over them, then in them is five dirhams. And nothing upon you - meaning regarding gold - until you have twenty dinars. When you have twenty dinars and a year passes over them, then in them is half a dinar. For whatever increases, the calculation is accordingly.' (Abu Dawud, Book of Zakat on Sa'imah, p. 233, no. 1573) This hadith shows that when a year passes over the nisab, zakat becomes wajib. [2] From Ibn 'Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'No zakat on the wealth of a person until a year passes over it.' (Dar Qutni, Book of Obligation of Zakat by Hawl, vol. 2, p. 76, no. 1870) This hadith also shows that zakat on wealth becomes wajib after a full year passes over the nisab.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage clarifies the condition of hawl (one lunar year) for zakat. The author distinguishes between the original nisab (the initial wealth from which the year is counted) and mustafad (wealth acquired during the year). The original nisab must be possessed for a full year; newly acquired wealth is added to the original nisab and its zakat is due at the end of the original year without requiring its own separate year. Two hadith are cited: the first from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) specifying the half-dinar zakat on twenty dinars after a year, and the second from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) stating that no zakat is due until a year passes. Note: The hadith from Ali is considered mawquf (from a companion) but is taken as a proof in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
نصاب اصلی (nisāb aṣlī): The original wealth upon which the year is counted.
مستفاد (mustafād): Wealth acquired during the current zakat year.
حول (ḥawl): A full lunar year commencing from the moment the nisab is possessed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zayd acquires 200 dirhams on 1 Shawwal. On 1 Muharram he acquires another 100 dirhams. When is zakat due on the total?
A) On 1 Shawwal of the next year, on the entire 300 dirhams.
B) On 1 Shawwal of the next year, only on the 200 dirhams.
C) On 1 Muharram of the next year, on the additional 100 dirhams.
D) Immediately, because nisab is reached.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is wajib only after a full lunar year passes over the original nisab; mustafad wealth is added to the original year and does not require a separate year.

Zakat on Mustafad Wealth: Merging with Original Nisab
Ruling on mustafad wealth: added to similar assets and zakat paid at end of original year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mustafad wealth, apply it to examples, and distinguish the condition of homogeneity (jins).

Core Idea
Wealth acquired during the zakat year merges with the original nisab; zakat is due at the end of the original year, not a separate year.

This lesson addresses a common practical question: when is zakat due on wealth you receive during the year—whether by trade, inheritance, or gift? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: such mustafad wealth is merged with existing holdings of the same type, and the zakat year remains the original one. This avoids the complexity of tracking multiple years for each acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage rules on mustafād (wealth acquired during the year). Determine the act (receiving wealth) and its ruling (zakat is obligatory at the end of the original year).
The ruling applies only if the wealth is of the same type (jins) as the existing nisab.
2
Understand the Merging Principle (Damm)
The author states that mustafad is 'added to its like' (yuḍammu ilā mujānasih). This means it is merged with the original nisab for calculating the threshold and the haul.
The key condition is mujānasah (homogeneity). Gold and silver are different types, so they are not merged.
3
Analyze the Examples
The passage gives examples: dirhams with dirhams, camels with camels. Work through each to see how the total is calculated and the year endpoint remains the original one.
The same applies regardless of whether the acquisition is from trade, inheritance, or other means.
4
Examine the Proof
The cited proof is a statement of the Tabiʿī al-Zuhrī. In Hanafi usul, a qawl of a Tabiʿī is accepted as evidence in certain cases, especially when there is no contradictory text.
The full chain is not given here; the passage cuts off. The proof indicates that if a person intends to spend the acquired wealth before the year ends, it suggests that if not spent, it is included in the zakat calculation.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Shafiʿī school generally requires mustafad to have its own year if it constitutes a new nisab, especially for inheritance or gifts. Contrast this to appreciate the Hanafi position.
This difference has practical consequences: under Hanafi, zakat is often due sooner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۵۶) واما المستفاد في اثنـاء الحـول فيضم الى مجانسه ویزگی بتمام الحول الاصلي سواء استفيد بتجارة او ميراث او تب

ترجمه : (۱۱۵۶) اور جو مال سال کے درمیان میں حاصل ہوا ہوا سے اس کے ہم جنس ( نصاب ) میں ملا دیا جائے گا ، اور اصلی سال کے ختم پر تمام مال کی زکوۃ دی جائے گی، چاہے وہ مال تجارت، یا میراث ، یاکسی اور صورت سے حاصل ہوا ہو۔

تشریح : مثلا دو سو درہم شوال سے اس کے پاس تھا محرم میں ایک سو درہم تجارت سے یا وراثت سے یا کسی صورت سے آیا تو اصل نصاب کے ساتھ شوال میں اس ایک سو درہم کی بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ یا مثلا شوال میں ہیں اونٹ تھے ، اور محرم میں دس اونٹ اور ہوئے، اونٹنی کا بچہ ہو یا تجارت سے آیا یا وراثت میں ملا تو شوال میں ان دس اونٹوں کی بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، حاصل یہ ہے کہ مال مستفاد کسی بھی طرح سے آئے اس کی جنس کے ساتھ ملا کر اصل نصاب پر سال گزرتے ہی سب کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔

وجه (۱) قول تابعی میں ہے ۔ عن الزهرى انه كان يقول اذا استفاد الرجل ما لا فاراد ان ينفقه قبل مجيء الحول
(1156) And as for wealth acquired during the year, it is added to its like (similar category) and zakat is given at the completion of the original year, whether it was acquired by trade, inheritance, or [other means].

Translation: (1156) And wealth that is acquired during the year will be merged with its homogenous (nisab), and the zakat of all the wealth will be given at the end of the original year, whether that wealth was acquired by trade, inheritance, or any other form.

Explanation: For example, if someone had two hundred dirhams from Shawwal, and in Muharram he got one hundred dirhams from trade or inheritance or any form, then with the original nisab in Shawwal, zakat on that one hundred dirhams also becomes wajib. Or for example, if in Shawwal he had five camels, and in Muharram he got ten more camels, whether the offspring of a she-camel or from trade or inheritance, then in Shawwal zakat on those ten camels also becomes wajib. The conclusion is that however mustafad wealth comes, it is merged with its type, and when the year passes over the original nisab, zakat on all becomes wajib.

Proof: (1) The saying of a Tabi'i: From al-Zuhri that he used to say: 'If a person acquires wealth and intends to spend it before the coming of the [year]...'
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage details the treatment of mustafad (wealth acquired during the zakat year). The author rules that such wealth is added to the existing nisab of the same type (e.g., cash to cash, camels to camels) and its zakat is due at the end of the original year, regardless of how it was obtained. The commentary gives examples: with dirhams and camels. The proof cited is a statement of Imam al-Zuhri (a Tabi'i), which is a non-marfu' evidence but accepted in Hanafi fiqh as a support. The passage ends mid-sentence due to page break, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
مستفاد (mustafād): Wealth acquired after the start of the zakat year.
مجانسه (mujānashih): Homogeneous or of the same type (jins).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) After 6 months from inheritance.
B) At the end of the original year on the total 300 dirhams.
C) Immediately, because it is a gift.
D) Only when the original nisab changes.

Key Takeaway
Mustafad wealth is merged with the original nisab of the same type, and zakat is due at the end of the original year, not a separate year.

The Condition of the Passage of a Year for Zakat on the Original Nisab
States the condition of one year for zakat on original nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of hawlan al-hawl for zakat on the original nisab and cite the hadith evidence that establishes it.

Core Idea
Zakat is not due immediately upon reaching nisab; a full lunar year must pass over the original nisab.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational condition for zakat: the passage of one complete lunar year over the original nisab. Understanding this condition is essential because it determines when the obligation of zakat actually becomes due. The source text presents the rule and supports it with two hadith from the Prophet ﷺ, which are the primary evidence for this requirement in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
What is the act being ruled upon? The text states that a condition for the obligation (wujub) of paying zakat is the passing of a year (hawlan al-hawl) on the original nisab. The ruling is that this condition is a shart (prerequisite) for wujub, not a rukn or sunnah.
Note the distinction: the condition relates to obligation, not to the act of paying itself.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The text cites two hadith. The first is from Ali (r) in Abu Dawud: 'When you have two hundred dirhams and a year has passed over them, then five dirhams are due...'. The second is from Ibn Umar in Dar Qutni: 'No zakat is due from a person's wealth until a year passes over it.' Identify both as ahad hadith.
Both hadith are from Sunan works, considered authentic (hasan/sahih) by muhaddithun.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal indication)
The crucial phrase in the first hadith is 'wa hala 'alayhi al-hawl' (and a year passes over it). This explicitly conditions zakat on the year passing. Without this phrase, the obligation does not arise. In the second hadith, 'la zakat hatta yahula 'alayhi al-hawl' (no zakat until a year passes) is equally explicit.
The Hanafi usul principle: a condition expressed with 'hatta' or 'fa' indicates a necessary precondition.
4
Understand the original nisab (nasab asli)
The text distinguishes between original nisab (the initial wealth reaching the threshold) and acquired wealth (mustafad). The year is counted from the moment the original nisab is first attained. For example, if Zaid had less than 200 dirhams, then in Shawwal he had 200 dirhams, the year starts from that Shawwal.
This distinction is important for calculating zakat on fluctuating wealth.
5
Verify the absence of ikhtilaf
The text indicates that this condition is agreed upon among the Hanafi imams and is cross-madhhab consensus (muttafaq alayh). There is no significant dispute about the necessity of the year passing for the original nisab.
Most scholars require a year for zakat, but the start and accounting may differ – e.g., when income is irregular.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وجه : (۱) سال گزرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عـن عـلـى عن النبى الله بعض اول الحديث قال فاذا كانت لک مائتا در هم و حال عليه الحول ففيها خمسة دراهم ولیس علیک شیء يعني في الذهب حتى يكون لک عشرون دينارا فاذا كانت لک عشرون دینارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلک (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ، ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نصاب پر سال گزر جائے تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ [۲] عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا زكوة في مال امرئ حتى يحول عليه الحول ( دار قطنی ، باب وجوب الزکوۃ بالحول ، ج ثانی، ص ۷۶، نمبر ۱۸۷۰) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ مال نصاب پر سال گزرنے کے بعد واجب ہوتی ہے۔
(1155) And a condition for the obligation of its payment is the passing of a year on the original nisab. Translation: (1155) And for the obligation of paying zakat, the passing of a year on the original nisab is a condition. Explanation: There is an original nisab and an acquired nisab. [1] Original nisab: For example, Zaid had less than two hundred dirhams, then in Shawwal he had two hundred dirhams. This is the original nisab. When a year passes, zakat becomes obligatory in the next Shawwal. Proof: (1) The evidence for the passing of a year is this hadith: From Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him) part of the beginning of the hadith: 'When you have two hundred dirhams and a year has passed over them, then five dirhams are due, and nothing is due from you [in gold] until you have twenty dinars. When you have twenty dinars and a year passes over them, then half a dinar is due, and for what exceeds, according to that calculation.' (Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Zakat, hadith 1573). This hadith indicates that zakat becomes obligatory when a year passes over the nisab. [2] From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'No zakat is due from a person's wealth until a year passes over it.' (Dar Qutni, Bab Wujub al-Zakat bil-Hawl, vol. 2, p. 76, hadith 1870). This hadith also indicates that zakat becomes obligatory after a year passes over the nisab.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the hadith. The condition of the passing of a full lunar year (hawlan al-hawl) on the nisab is a consensus-based obligation for zakat on most types of wealth. The text distinguishes between original nisab (the initial wealth that reaches the nisab threshold) and acquired wealth (mustafad) during the year. For the original nisab, the year begins when the nisab is first reached. The two hadith cited are both authentic and explicitly require the year to pass before zakat is due. In the Hanafi madhhab, this condition applies to cash, gold, silver, and trade goods. Livestock also generally requires a year, but the specific calculation for each animal type follows its own rules.

Key Terms
نصاب اصلی (nisab asli): The original wealth that first reaches the nisab threshold, from which the year starts.
حولان الحول (hawlan al-hawl): The passing of one complete lunar year over the nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when does zakat become obligatory on the original nisab?
A) Immediately upon reaching the nisab
B) After one complete lunar year has passed over the nisab
C) After six months
D) Only at the end of Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Zakat on the original nisab becomes obligatory only after the completion of one lunar year.

Zakat on Wealth Acquired During the Year: Inclusion vs. Separate Year
Explains adding acquired wealth to original nisab for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mustafad, identify the proofs (athar of al-Zuhri and hadith of Ibn Umar), and explain how the Hanafi school reconciles them.

Core Idea
Acquired wealth of the same type is included with the original nisab; zakat is due at the original year's end.

Imagine you already have 200 dirhams and in the middle of the year you receive another 100 from inheritance. Do you pay zakat on that extra 100 at the end of the year, or do you wait a full year from when you got it? The Hanafi school has a well-supported position that resolves this practical question using early practice and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is wealth (mustafad) acquired during the zakat year. The ruling is that it is added (yudamm) to its mujanas (same type) and zakat is due at the completion of the original year.
The key condition: same type as existing nisab.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is an athar (saying) of the tabi'i al-Zuhri, who said: if a man acquires wealth and does not intend to spend it, he should pay zakat on it along with his existing wealth. This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
The imperative 'falyuzakkihi' indicates obligation, and 'ma'a malih' indicates combination.
3
Understand the opposing proof
There is a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever acquires wealth, there is no zakat on him until a year passes over it.' This appears to contradict the Hanafi view.
This hadith is used by other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) to require a separate year for mustafad.
4
Apply the Hanafi reconciliation
The Hanafi school reconciles by applying the hadith to wealth that is not added to an existing nisab. When there is already a complete nisab, the athar of al-Zuhri provides a specific ruling based on early practice. This is a case of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding general qiyas.
Thus, the two proofs are not contradictory; they cover different situations.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the Hanafi view allows zakat to be paid earlier on mustafad (beneficial for the poor), while the opposing view delays zakat on mustafad until its own year passes.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the inclusion method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۱۱۵۶) اور جو مال سال کے درمیان میں حاصل ہوا ہوا سے اس کے ہم جنس ( نصاب ) میں ملا دیا جائے گا ، اور اصلی سال کے ختم پر تمام مال کی زکوۃ دی جائے گی، چاہے وہ مال تجارت، یا میراث ، یاکسی اور صورت سے حاصل ہوا ہو۔
تشریح : مثلا دو سو درہم شوال سے اس کے پاس تھا محرم میں ایک سو درہم تجارت سے یا وراثت سے یا کسی صورت سے آیا تو اصل نصاب کے ساتھ شوال میں اس ایک سو درہم کی بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ یا مثلا شوال میں ہیں اونٹ تھے ، اور محرم میں دس اونٹ اور ہوئے، اونٹنی کا بچہ ہو یا تجارت سے آیا یا وراثت میں ملا تو شوال میں ان دس اونٹوں کی بھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، حاصل یہ ہے کہ مال مستفاد کسی بھی طرح سے آئے اس کی جنس کے ساتھ ملا کر اصل نصاب پر سال گزرتے ہی سب کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔
وجه (۱) قول تابعی میں ہے ۔ عن الزهرى انه كان يقول اذا استفاد الرجل ما لا فاراد ان ينفقه قبل مجيء غير  ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ ۲۶۰ كتاب الزكوة غيره (۱۱۵۷) ولو عجل ذو نصاب لسنين صح .
ثم لینفقه وان کان لا یرید ان ینفق فلیزکه مع ماله (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۴۹ من قال یزکیه اذا استفاده ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۸۷ نمبر ۱۰۲۲۷ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وجوب الصدقۃ فی الحول، ج رابع ، ص ۳۲ نمبر ۶۸۷۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال مستفاد میں مال نصاب کے ساتھ زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ (۲) دوسری حدیث بھی موجود ہے کہ مال مستفاد پر جب تک سال نہ گزرے زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی ، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله من استفاد مالا فلا زكوة عليه حتى يحول عليه الحول ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء لا زکوۃ علی المال المستفاد حتی حال علیه الحول ص ۱۳۷ نمبر ۶۳۱ ردار قطنی ، باب وجوب الزكوة بالحول ج ثانی ص ۷ے سے نمبر ۱۸۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک خود مال مستفاد پر سال نہ گزر جائے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
(1156) And as for wealth acquired during the year, it is added to its similar type, and zakat is paid at the completion of the original year, whether it was acquired through trade, inheritance, or any other means.
Translation: (1156) And wealth that is obtained during the middle of the year will be added to its similar type (nisab), and zakat will be given for all the wealth at the end of the original year, whether that wealth was obtained through trade, inheritance, or any other form.
Explanation: For example, if Zaid had two hundred dirhams from Shawwal, and in Muharram he obtained another hundred dirhams from trade or inheritance or some other means, then along with the original nisab, zakat will be obligatory on that hundred dirhams in Shawwal. Similarly, if he had ten camels in Shawwal, and in Muharram he got ten more camels (whether by birth or trade or inheritance), then zakat will be obligatory on those ten camels in Shawwal. The conclusion is that no matter how acquired wealth is obtained, it is added to its type, and when a year passes over the original nisab, zakat becomes obligatory on all.
Proof: (1) From al-Zuhri that he used to say: 'When a man acquires wealth and intends to spend it before the coming of another [year]', then let him spend it, and if he does not intend to spend, let him add it to his wealth and pay zakat on it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab man qala yuzakkihi idha istifada, vol. 2, p. 1387, hadith 10227; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab wujub al-sadaqah fi al-hawl, vol. 4, p. 32, hadith 6873). This athar indicates that zakat is obligatory on acquired wealth along with the nisab. (2) There is another hadith that zakat is not obligatory on acquired wealth until a year passes over it: From Ibn Umar, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever acquires wealth, there is no zakat on him until a year passes over it.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a la zakata 'ala al-mal al-mustafad hatta yahula 'alayhi al-hawl, p. 137, hadith 631; Dar Qutni, Bab wujub al-zakat bil-hawl, vol. 2, p. 76, hadith 1877). This hadith indicates that zakat is not obligatory on its own until a year passes over it.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that addresses acquired wealth (mustafad) during the zakat year. The Hanafi position is that mustafad is added to the same type of wealth (e.g., cash to cash, camels to camels) and zakat is due at the end of the original year, regardless of when the acquisition occurred. The text provides an example: if someone has 200 dirhams in Shawwal and acquires another 100 dirhams in Muharram, all 300 dirhams are zakatable the following Shawwal. The proof includes a statement from al-Zuhri (a tabi'i) supporting this practice. However, there is a conflicting hadith from Ibn Umar that would require a separate year for mustafad. The Hanafi school gives preference to the practice of the Companions and the fatwa of the early scholars, thus adopting the inclusion method. This is an example of istihsan overriding a general qiyas (analogy) that would require a new year for each acquisition.

Key Terms
المستفاد (al-mustafad): Wealth acquired after the original nisab has been established and before the year ends.
مجانسه (mujanasihi): Similar type or species; mustafad is added to wealth of the same category (e.g., cash to cash, livestock to livestock).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on wealth acquired during the zakat year?
A) It must wait for a full year from the date of acquisition
B) It is added to the original nisab and zakat is due at the end of the original year
C) It is not subject to zakat at all
D) Only trade profits are included, not inheritance

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, mustafad of the same type as the original nisab is added, and zakat is due at the end of the original year, supported by the athar of al-Zuhri and the principle of istihsan.

Advancing Zakat for Multiple Years: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling that advancing zakat for multiple years is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on advancing zakat for multiple years, cite the hadith proof, and explain the underlying rationale.

Core Idea
Advancing zakat before the year ends is permitted because the nisab itself is the cause.

Zakat is normally due after one lunar year passes over the nisab. But what if someone wants to pay early, even for several years? The Hanafi school, based on a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ, permits this. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, the proof from the Sunnah, and the rationale provided by our scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage states that if the owner of nisab advances zakat for years, it is valid (sahih). Determine the hukm level: mubah (permissible) because it's allowed but not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: al-Abbas asked the Prophet ﷺ about advancing zakat before it became due, and he allowed it. This is a hadith ahad from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit permission (rukhas) to pay before the year ends demonstrates that the time condition can be waived. The phrase 'before it became due' directly supports advancing payment.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not allow advancing zakat before the year completes, considering the year a condition for obligation. The Hanafi school holds the nisab as the primary cause, so early payment is valid.
5
Understand the rationale
The text gives a second proof: the nisab wealth is the original cause (sabab) for zakat. Once the cause exists, the obligation can be fulfilled early. This is a qiyas-based argument supporting the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۵۷) ولو عجل ذو نصاب لسنين صح .
ترجمه : (۱۱۵۷) اگر صاحب نصاب چند سالوں کی زکوۃ پہلے ہی سے دینا چاہے تو جائز ہے۔ تشریح : ایک آدمی نصاب کا مالک ہے اور ایک سال گزرا ہے اور تین سالوں کا دینا چاہتا ہے تو جائز ہے۔ یا اس نصاب پر سال نہیں گزرا ہے اور وہ ابھی زکوۃ ادا کر دینا چاہتا ہے تو جائز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) مال نصاب اصل سبب ہے اور وہ پایا گیا تو گویا کہ سبب پایا گیا اس لئے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائینگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن علی ان العباس سأل النبي عل في تعجيل الصدقة قبل ان تحل فرخص له في ذلك قال مرة فاذن له فی ذالک . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی تعجیل الزکوۃ، ص ۲۴۱، نمبر ۶۲۴ ارترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تجمیل الزکوۃ ص۱۷۳، نمبر ۶۷۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سال گزرنے سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ حضرت عباس گو اس کی اجازت دی تھی۔
(1157) And if the owner of nisab advances [zakat] for years, it is valid.
Translation: (1157) If the owner of nisab wishes to give zakat for several years in advance, it is permissible. Explanation: If a person owns nisab and one year has passed, and he wants to give for three years, it is permissible. Or if a year has not passed over this nisab, and he wants to pay zakat immediately, it is permissible.
Proof: (1) The nisab wealth is the original cause, and when it exists, it is as if the cause exists, so the payment of zakat is valid. (2) In a hadith: From Ali that al-Abbas asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about advancing the zakat before it became due, and he allowed him to do so. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Ta'jil al-Zakat, p. 241, hadith 1624; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi Ta'jil al-Zakat, p. 173, hadith 678). This hadith indicates that zakat can be paid before the year passes, because the Prophet permitted al-Abbas to do so.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on advancing zakat (ta'jil). The Hanafi madhhab permits paying zakat for one or more years in advance, provided the person already owns the nisab. The rationale given is that the existence of the nisab is the underlying cause (sabab) for zakat, so once the cause exists, the obligation can be fulfilled early. The hadith of al-Abbas (the Prophet's uncle) is cited as explicit permission. Note: This permissibility applies only if the nisab remains intact; if the wealth decreases later, the advance payment is still valid as a voluntary charity (sadaqah) but does not fulfill the future obligation. However, the text does not discuss the case of subsequent loss.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jil): Paying zakat before it becomes obligatory, i.e., before the year passes.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat.
سبب (sabab): Cause; the underlying factor that makes an obligation due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling on advancing zakat?
A) Quranic verse
B) Hadith of al-Abbas
C) Ijma of the Companions
D) Qiyas on sadaqat al-fitr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab permits advancing zakat for multiple years because the nisab is the underlying cause, supported by the hadith of al-Abbas.

Condition of Intention for Zakat
States that intention is required and must coincide with payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of intention for zakat, identify the four valid times for making intention, and apply the general principle that acts of worship require intention.

Core Idea
Zakat requires intention at or before payment; without it, the payment is not zakat.

Zakat is an act of worship ('ibadah), and like prayer or fasting, it requires a specific intention (niyyah) to distinguish it from ordinary charity. Without intention, even if you give money to a poor person, it does not count as zakat. This lesson explains when and how that intention must be made.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying zakat. The ruling is that intention is a condition (shart) for its validity. Without intention, the payment is not valid as zakat.
Condition means the act is not considered performed without it.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a general principle: all primary acts of worship require intention. The passage also references a hadith from Umar (though incomplete).
The dalil is 'aqli (rational) based on the nature of 'ibadat.
3
Identify the forms of valid intention
The text lists four valid times: (1) when giving to the poor, (2) when giving to one's agent, (3) when setting aside the zakat amount, (4) after giving but before the poor person spends the money.
The intention must be concurrent with the payment or setting aside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۵۸) وشرط صحة ادائها نية مقارنة لادائها شهر زکوته فليز كه ثم لينفقه وان كان لايريد ان ينفق فليز كه مع ماله 
ترجمه : (۱۱۵۸) اور نیت زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط ہے۔ اور یہ نیت ۔ متصل ہونی چاہئے فقیر کو دیتے وقت، یا وکیل کو دیتے وقت ، یا واجب مقدار کی علاحدگی کے وقت ۔ تشریح : زکوۃ ادا ہونے کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ ادا کرتے وقت زکوۃ دینے کی نیت ہو، اب نیت کرنے کی چار صورتیں ہیں [1] فقیر کو دیتے وقت نیت ہو ۔ (۲) یا اپنے وکیل کو رقم حوالہ کرتے وقت نیت ہو۔ [۳] جس وقت زکوۃ کا مال اپنے مال سے الگ کر رہا تھا اس وقت نیت ہو ۔ [۴] یا ان متینوں وقتوں میں نیت نہ کر سکا اور مال دے دیا تو جب تک یہ مال فقیر کے ہاتھ میں ہے ابھی اس کو خرچ نہیں کیا ہے اس وقت تک زکوۃ کی نیت کر لے تب بھی اس نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا ، اور زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ عبادت اصلیہ اس وقت ادا ہو گی جب عبادت کی نیت کی ہو۔ اور زکوۃ عبادت ہے اس لئے اس کی ادا ئیگی کے وقت بھی نیت ہونی چاہئے (۲) حدیث میں ہے. سمعت عمر بن الخطاب على المنبر قال : سمعت
(1158) And a condition for the validity of its payment is intention concurrent with its payment.
Translation: (1158) And intention is a condition for the correctness of paying zakat. And this intention must be concurrent: at the time of giving to the poor, or at the time of giving to the agent, or at the time of separating the obligatory amount. Explanation: For zakat to be valid, it is a condition that at the time of payment, the intention to give zakat is present. There are four forms of making intention: [1] At the time of giving to the poor. [2] Or at the time of handing over money to one's agent. [3] Or at the time of setting aside the zakat money from one's own wealth. [4] Or if he could not make intention at these times and gave the money, then as long as the money is in the hand of the poor and has not been spent, if he makes the intention at that time, that intention is valid and zakat is considered paid.
Proof: (1) It has passed earlier that a primary act of worship is only valid when the intention of worship is made. Zakat is an act of worship, so intention is required at the time of payment. (2) In a hadith: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit say: I heard...
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the condition of niyyah (intention) for zakat. In Hanafi fiqh, zakat is an act of worship ('ibadah), and like all acts of worship, it requires specific intention to distinguish it from ordinary charity. The intention must be made at the time of payment or at the time of setting aside the zakat amount. The text lists four valid times: when giving to the poor, when giving to one's agent, when segregating the zakat funds, or even after giving as long as the recipient still possesses the money and has not used it. The proof is based on the general principle that acts of worship require intention, and the hadith from Umar (though incomplete here) likely supports the necessity of intention.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The mental resolve to perform zakat as an act of worship, distinguishing it from regular charity.
شرط (shart): Condition; something whose absence makes the act invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At the time of giving to the poor
B) At the time of setting aside the zakat amount
C) After the poor person has spent the money
D) At the time of giving to one's agent

Key Takeaway
Intention for zakat must be present at or before the time of payment, with flexibility to make it later if the recipient has not spent the money.
