Advance Payment of Zakat (Ta'jil al-Zakat)
Ruling with proof: advance payment of zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on advance payment of zakat and explain the evidence from the hadith of Abbas and the reasoning by cause (sabab).

Core Idea
Advanced zakat is valid because the cause (nisab) exists and the Prophet permitted it.

Zakat is normally due after a lunar year of possessing nisab. However, the Hanafi school permits paying zakat before the year completes. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and the underlying reasoning that allows this flexibility.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (paying zakat before year's end) and the hukm level (valid/permissible). The text says 'لو عجل ذو نصاب لسنين صح' (if an owner of nisab pays in advance for years, it is valid).
The key term is 'sah' (valid), indicating permissibility not obligation.
2
Identify the proof from hadith
Locate the dalil: the Prophet permitted al-Abbas to give zakat before it was due. The hadith is cited from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi.
The hadith is ahad (singular), so it is zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the evidence (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's permission (farakhhasa) indicates permissibility (ibaha), not obligation. The word 'tarkhis' (permission) shows the act is allowed.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub but here it is permission, so hukm is mubah.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school does not allow advance payment because obligation is only established after a full year. The Hanafi school counters with the hadith and the principle that the cause (nisab) is present.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in timing of payment.
5
Apply the mufta-bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that advance payment is permissible, whether for one year or multiple years, even if no year has passed.
This is based on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غيره (١١٥٧) ولو عجل ذو نصاب لسنين صح . لغة: اثناء: درميان، جنس: ايك هي نسل كي چيز، ثمين: قيمتي. ترجمه: اگر صاحب نصاب چند سالوں کی زکوۃ پہلے ہی سے دینا چاہے تو جائز ہے۔ تشریح: ایک آدمی نصاب کا مالک ہے اور ایک سال گزرا ہے اور تین سالوں کا دینا چاہتا ہے تو جائز ہے۔ یا اس نصاب پر سال نہیں گزرا ہے اور وہ ابھی زکوۃ ادا کر دینا چاہتا ہے تو جائز ہے۔ وجه: (۱) مال نصاب اصل سبب ہے اور وہ پایا گیا تو گویا کہ سبب پایا گیا اس لئے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائیں گی (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن علی ان العباس سأل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في تعجيل الصدقة قبل ان تحل فرخص له في ذلك قال مرة فاذن له في ذلك. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی تعجیل الزکوۃ، ص ٢٤١، نمبر ٦٢٤، ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تجمیل الزکوۃ ص١٧٣، نمبر ٦٧٨) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سال گزرنے سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ حضرت عباس کو اس کی اجازت دی تھی۔
Other: (1157) And if an owner of nisab pays in advance for years, it is valid. Vocabulary: اثناء: between, جنس: same type, ثمين: valuable. Translation: If a person who owns nisab wishes to give zakat for several years in advance, it is permissible. Explanation: A person owns nisab and one year has passed, and he wants to give for three years, it is permissible. Or if a year has not passed on this nisab and he wants to give zakat now, it is permissible. Proof: (1) The wealth of nisab is the original cause, and it is found, so as if the cause is found, therefore the payment of zakat occurs. (2) There is a hadith: From Ali that al-Abbas asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about paying zakat before it was due, and he permitted him for that. He said once: he permitted him for that. (Abu Dawood, chapter on advance payment of zakat, p.241 no.624; Tirmidhi, chapter on advance payment of zakat, p.173 no.678) From this hadith it is understood that one can pay zakat before the year passes, because permission was given to al-Abbas.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on advance payment of zakat. It begins with a clear ruling that if a person who possesses nisab (the minimum threshold of wealth) pays zakat in advance for multiple years, it is valid. The commentator expands by giving an example: if a person has had nisab for one year and wishes to pay for three years, or if no year has passed yet and he pays now, it is permissible. The proof from reason is that the nisab wealth is the underlying cause (sabab) for zakat, and once the cause exists, payment is valid. Then a hadith is cited: the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted al-Abbas to give zakat before it was due. This establishes the permissibility of advance payment, even though the obligation is normally after a year according to the dominant position. The Hanafi school relies on this to allow ta'jil (advance payment) of zakat.

Key Terms
تعجيل الزكاة (ta'jil al-zakat): Paying zakat before the completion of one lunar year (hawl) since acquiring the nisab.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory, e.g., 85 grams of gold or 595 grams of silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on paying zakat before the year passes, according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is not valid; one must wait for the year to pass.
B) It is valid only if one has had nisab for a full year.
C) It is valid, whether the year has passed or not.
D) It is valid only for one year in advance.

Key Takeaway
Advance payment of zakat is valid in the Hanafi school based on the hadith of Abbas and the principle that the cause (nisab) suffices.

Condition of Intention for Zakat
Stating that intention is a condition for valid zakat payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four valid timings for intention in zakat and explain why intention is a condition based on the hadith.

Core Idea
Intention for zakat must be concurrent with payment, but if missed, can be made while the wealth is still in the poor's hands.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah establishes that intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of zakat payment. It provides specific moments when the intention is considered valid, including a generous exception for retrospective intention. The proof is drawn from the well-known hadith 'Actions are by intentions', which applies to all primary acts of worship including zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Pinpoint that the passage declares intention as a condition (shart) for the validity of zakat. Without it, the payment is invalid.
The ruling is that intention is wajib (obligatory) for zakat according to the Hanafi school.
2
List the four valid timings
Extract from the text the four moments when intention can be made: (1) at the time of giving to the poor, (2) at the time of giving to one's agent, (3) at the time of setting aside the zakat amount, and (4) after giving but while the wealth is still in the poor's possession (unspent).
The fourth timing is a relaxation allowing retroactive intention.
3
Understand the proof
The passage cites the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi-nniyyat' (actions are by intentions) as the primary evidence. This hadith is mutawatir in meaning and applies generally to all acts of worship.
The proof demonstrates that zakat, as an act of worship, requires intention like any other ibadah.
4
Connect the proof to the ruling
Explain the wajh al-dalalah: the hadith establishes that the validity of an act depends on the intention behind it. For zakat, which is an act of worship, intention is therefore essential.
This is a general principle: primary acts of worship require niyyah.
5
Note the practical relaxation
Observe the fourth scenario: if intention was not made at the time of payment, it can still be made later as long as the recipient has not spent the money. This shows leniency in the Hanafi school.
This exception is based on the idea that the wealth is still traceable and the act of giving can be associated with the intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٥٨) وشرط صحة ادائها نية مقارنة لادائها للفقير او وكيله او لعزل ما وجب . لغة: مقارنة: ملي هوئي، عزل: الگ كرنا. ترجمه: اور نيت زكوۃ كي ادائيگي كے صحيح ہونے كے لئے شرط ہے. اور يہ نيت متصل ہونی چاہئے فقير كو ديتے وقت، يا وكيل كو ديتے وقت، يا واجب مقدار كي علاحدگي كے وقت. تشریح: زکوۃ ادا ہونے کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ ادا کرتے وقت زکوۃ دینے کی نیت ہو، اب نیت کرنے کی چار صورتیں ہیں (1) فقیر کو دیتے وقت نیت ہو۔ (2) یا اپنے وکیل کو رقم حوالہ کرتے وقت نیت ہو۔ (3) جس وقت زکوۃ کا مال اپنے مال سے الگ کر رہا تھا اس وقت نیت ہو۔ (4) یا ان متینوں وقتوں میں نیت نہ کر سکا اور مال دے دیا تو جب تک یہ مال فقیر کے ہاتھ میں ہے ابھی اس کو خرچ نہیں کیا ہے اس وقت تک زکوۃ کی نیت کر لے تب بھی اس نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا، اور زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ وجه: (1) پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ عبادت اصلیہ اس وقت ادا ہو گی جب عبادت کی نیت کی ہو۔ اور زکوۃ عبادت ہے اس لئے اس کی ادائیگی کے وقت بھی نیت ہونی چاہئے (2) حدیث میں ہے. سمعت عمر بن الخطاب على المنبر قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: انما الاعمال بالنيات الخ (بخاری شریف، باب کیف کان بدء الوحی، ص۲ نمبر1) اس حدیث کی وجہ سے تمام عبادات اصلیہ کی ادائیگی کے لئے عبادت کے ساتھ ہی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے۔
(1158) And a condition for the validity of its payment is intention concurrent with its payment to the poor person, or his agent, or the setting aside of what is obligatory. Vocabulary: مقارنة: connected, عزل: separation. Translation: And intention is a condition for the validity of the payment of zakat. And this intention must be connected at the time of giving to the poor, or at the time of giving to his agent, or at the time of setting aside the obligatory amount. Explanation: For zakat to be paid, this condition is that at the time of payment, one must have the intention to give zakat. Now there are four forms of intention: (1) At the time of giving to the poor, intention is made. (2) Or at the time of handing over the amount to one's agent, intention is made. (3) At the time of separating the zakat wealth from one's own wealth, intention is made. (4) Or if he could not make intention at these specific times and he gave the wealth, then as long as this wealth is in the hand of the poor and he has not spent it yet, he can make the intention of zakat, then this intention will be considered and the payment of zakat will be valid. Proof: (1) It has passed before that a primary act of worship is only fulfilled when intention is made for worship. And zakat is worship, therefore at the time of its payment, intention must be present. (2) There is a hadith: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Actions are by intentions' etc. (Bukhari, chapter on how revelation began, p.2 no.1) Due to this hadith, for all primary acts of worship, it is necessary to make intention simultaneously with the worship.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage lays down the condition of intention (niyyah) for the validity of zakat payment. It states that the intention must be muqaranah (concurrent) with the act of giving. The commentator explains that this concurrence can occur at three specific moments: when handing the money to the poor, when giving to a proxy (wakil), or when setting the zakat amount aside from one's wealth. Then a fourth scenario is added: if no intention was made at those times but the money is still in the poor person's possession (unspent), one can still make the intention retroactively, and it will be valid. The proof is based on the general principle that primary acts of worship require niyyah, and zakat is a primary worship. The hadith 'Actions are by intentions' from Umar is quoted, which is a foundational text in fiqh for requiring intention in all acts of worship.

Key Terms
نية مقارنة (niyyah muqaranah): Intention that is simultaneous with the act of worship, in this case, the payment of zakat.
عزل (azl): Setting aside or segregating the zakat amount from one's general wealth, which is considered a valid moment for intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At which moment is the intention for zakat NOT considered valid according to this passage?
A) At the time of giving to the poor.
B) At the time of giving to one's agent.
C) At the time of setting the zakat amount aside.
D) At the time of earning the income.

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition for valid zakat, and the Hanafi school allows it to be made at any of four moments, including after payment if the wealth is still with the poor.

Constructive Intention (Muqaranah Hukmiyyah) in Zakat
Explaining that constructive intention suffices if wealth is still in poor's hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on constructive intention for zakat and identify the condition under which a later intention validates the payment.

Core Idea
A later intention of zakat validates payment while the wealth remains with the poor.

The Hanafi school provides a practical facilitation by accepting a constructive intention (muqaranah hukmiyyah) when the intention was not made at the time of payment. This lesson explores the scenario, the condition, and the underlying reasoning that makes this possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving zakat initially without intention, then later intending it while the wealth is still with the poor. The ruling is that the zakat is valid (sahih) despite the initial lack of intention.
This is a relaxation of the normal requirement of concurrent intention.
2
Identify the condition for validity
The key condition is that the wealth (mal) must remain in the possession of the poor recipient at the time of the later intention. The text says: 'والمال قائم بيد الفقير' (while the wealth remains in the hand of the poor).
If the poor has already spent or lost the wealth, the later intention does not validate.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The later intention works because the poor person is considered an agent (wakil) for the payer in taking possession. Thus, the intention is constructively concurrent (muqaranah hukmiyyah). This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and agency theory.
This is a facilitative ruling to avoid hardship.
4
Note the inter-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i and other schools require explicit intention at the time of payment and do not accept a later intention. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
The Hanafi position is more flexible.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider loan forgiveness: Zaid lends £200 to poor Khalid. Later, Zaid wants to count it as zakat. If Khalid still has the £200, Zaid can intend it as zakat. If not, Zaid can arrange a new payment with intention.
The second example in the text shows a way to regularize even if the wealth is gone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٥٩) ولو مقارنة حكميّة كما لو دفع بلا نية ثم نوى والمال قائم بيد الفقير . لغة: مقارنہ: ملي هوئي، حكمي: فرضي. ترجمه: اگر چه حكمي طور پر نيت متصل ہو، جيسے كہ بغير نيت كے دے ديا پھر نيت كي اس حال ميں كہ مال فقير كے ہاتھ ميں قائم ہے. تشریح: حكمي طور پر نيت زكوۃ ادا كرنے كے متصل ہو اس كي صورت يہ ہے كہ فقير كے ہاتھ ميں مال ديتے وقت كوئي نيت نهيں تھي، يا مثلا قرض كي نيت تھي، اور ابھي فقير كے پاس وہ مال موجود ہے اور زكوۃ كي نيت كرنا چاہے تو كر سكتا ہے۔ اس صورت ميں گويا كہ فقير خود صاحب زكوۃ كي جانب سے قبضہ كرنے كا وکیل بن گیا۔ دوسری صورت يہ ہے كہ مثلا زيد نے خالد فقير کو قرض کے طور پر دو سو پونڈ دئے، اب وہ ادا نہیں کر پا رہا ہے، تو ایسا کرے کہ خالد کو کہے کہ وہ کہیں سے دوسو پونڈ کا انتظام کرے اور زید کو دے دے، پھر اب زکوۃ کی نیت سے خالد کو دوسو درہم دے تو اب زید کی زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ اب دوسو درہم دیتے وقت زکوۃ کی نیت ہے۔
(1159) And even if it is a constructive concurrence, like when he gives without intention then intends while the wealth remains in the hand of the poor. Vocabulary: مقارنة: connected, حكمية: constructive/ruling-based. Translation: Even if the intention is constructively concurrent, such as when he gives without intention, then he intends while the wealth remains in the hand of the poor. Explanation: The scenario for intention to be constructively concurrent with the payment of zakat is that at the time of giving the wealth to the poor, there was no intention, or for example, there was intention of loan, and that wealth is still present with the poor and he wants to make intention of zakat, then he can. In this scenario, it is as if the poor person himself became an agent for the zakat owner to take possession. Another scenario: for example, Zaid gave two hundred pounds to the poor Khalid as a loan, and Khalid is unable to repay. Then, Zaid should tell Khalid to arrange two hundred pounds from elsewhere and give it to Zaid. Then, Zaid gives two hundred dirhams to Khalid with the intention of zakat. Then Zaid's zakat will be valid, because at the time of giving the two hundred dirhams, there is intention of zakat.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage clarifies the concept of 'muqaranah hukmiyyah' (constructive concurrent intention). It presents a scenario where the intention of zakat was not made at the initial payment, but the wealth is still in the possession of the recipient. In that case, the giver can still make the intention of zakat, and it will be valid. The commentator illustrates with a detailed example involving a loan: if a person gave a loan to a poor person, and later that poor person is unable to repay, the lender can forgive the loan and intend it as zakat, provided the recipient still has the money (or even if not, the second example shows a way to regularize). The key point is that the intention can be made later as long as the transaction can be linked to zakat. This is a practical facilitation (takhfif) from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مقارنة حكمية (muqaranah hukmiyyah): A constructive or deemed intention that is considered to be concurrent, even if not actually made at the moment of payment, due to a later intention while the wealth is still in the poor's possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if the recipient is a relative.
B) Only if the wealth is still in the possession of the poor.
C) Only if the giver announces it publicly.
D) Only if the intention is made within one day.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a later intention validates zakat if the wealth is still with the poor; this is a practical relief based on istihsan.

Recipient Need Not Know It's Zakat
Ruling that the poor person does not need to know the payment is zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling that the recipient’s knowledge is not required for zakat and APPLY it to scenarios where zakat is given as a gift or loan.

Core Idea
The giver's intention alone makes the payment zakat; the recipient need not know.

In giving zakat, preserving the recipient's dignity is important. The Hanafi school provides a practical ruling: you do not need to announce that the money is zakat. Even if you call it a gift or loan, as long as you intend zakat internally, the obligation is fulfilled. This lesson explains this eased condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the first sentence: 'ولا يشترط علم الفقير انها زكوة' – the poor person's knowledge is not a condition. This is the central legal point.
The phrase 'على الاصح' (according to the most correct view) indicates there is an alternative view, but this is the relied-upon position.
2
Work through the example
The text provides an example: giving as a gift (هبة) or loan (قرض) while internally intending zakat. Understand that the external label does not affect validity.
The key is the giver's intention (نية) at the time of giving.
3
Recognize the rationale
The commentary explains that this ruling is to protect the dignity of needy relatives who may feel ashamed to accept zakat openly.
This reflects the Hanafi concern for social welfare and ease.
4
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: you have a proud relative who is eligible for zakat. You can give them money as a gift and intend zakat – it is valid.
Ensure that the money reaches them (tamleek) and that you had the intention at the time of giving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٦٠) ولا يشترط علم الفقير انها زكوة على الاصح حتى لو اعطاه شيئا وسماه هبة او قرضا ونوى به الزكوة صحت. ترجمه: اصح قول کے مطابق فقیر کو یہ جاننا کہ یہ زکوۃ کی رقم ہے شرط نہیں، یہاں تک کہ اگر (فقیر) کو کوئی چیز دی ہدیہ یا قرض کے نام سے اور اس سے زکوۃ کی نیت کر لی تو صحیح ہے۔ تشریح: بعض مرتبہ رشتہ دار زکوۃ کے نام سے مال نہیں لینا چاہتے ہیں تا کہ بعد میں زکوۃ کھانے کا طعنہ نہ سننا پڑے، حالانکہ وہ فقیر اور مسکین ہوتے ہیں اس لئے ان کو ہدیہ یا قرض کے نام سے دے دے، اور دل میں زکوۃ کی نیت کرلے تو زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ اس کو یہ بتانا کہ یہ زکوۃ کا مال ہے ضروری نہیں ہے۔
(1160) And it is not a condition that the poor person knows that it is zakat according to the most correct view, so much so that if he gives him something and calls it a gift or a loan and intends by it zakat, it is valid. Translation: According to the most correct opinion, it is not a condition for the poor person to know that it is a zakat amount, to the extent that if he gives something to (the poor) and names it a gift or a loan and intends zakat by it, it is valid. Explanation: Sometimes relatives do not want to take money in the name of zakat, so that they do not have to hear the reproach of taking zakat later, even though they are poor and needy. So he should give them in the name of a gift or a loan and intend zakat in his heart; then the payment of zakat will be valid, because informing him that this is zakat money is not necessary.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This ruling states a practical facilitation: the recipient of zakat does not need to be told that the money is zakat. The giver can give it as a gift (hibah) or a loan (qard) and internally intend zakat. This is particularly useful for relatives who may feel embarrassed to accept zakat openly. The Hanafi school validates this because intention is a matter of the heart; what matters is the giver's intention, not the label used externally. The phrase 'ala al-ashah (according to the most correct view) indicates that this is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): A gift given without expectation of return.
قرض (qard): A loan that is to be repaid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The recipient must know it is zakat.
B) The giver must verbally state it is zakat.
C) The giver must intend zakat at the time of giving.
D) The recipient must accept it as zakat.

Key Takeaway
For zakat to be valid, the giver's intention alone is necessary; the recipient need not be informed.

Giving All Wealth as Charity Discharges Zakat
Ruling that giving all wealth as charity covers zakat without intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that giving all wealth in charity without zakat intention discharges the zakat obligation and explain why the qiyas requirement of specific intention is overridden.

Core Idea
Giving all wealth in charity discharges zakat even without intention because the charity inherently covers the obligation.

Zakat normally requires specific intention (niyyah) to be valid. However, the Hanafi school recognizes an exception: if a person gives away all his wealth as general charity (sadaqah) without mentioning zakat, the zakat obligation is automatically discharged. This ruling is a concession that prioritizes the fulfilment of the obligation's purpose over a formal condition. In this lesson, we will examine the exact ruling, the qiyas it overrides, and the practical conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Read the passage carefully. What is the act described? What is the ruling (hukm) on the zakat obligation?
The act is giving all wealth in sadaqah (charity) without intending zakat. The ruling: the zakat obligation 'falls' (saqata) from him.
2
Understand the Qiyas (Analogical Reasoning)
The passage mentions that by qiyas, the zakat should not be discharged because intention is missing. What is the default rule in Hanafi fiqh regarding intention for worship?
Default rule: intention is a condition for acts of worship, including zakat. The text states 'qiyas requires otherwise'.
3
Recognize the Override (Istihsan)
Why does the Hanafi school override the qiyas? The passage implies that giving all wealth is so comprehensive that it necessarily covers the zakat due. This is an istihsan (equitable preference).
The reasoning: since he gave away everything, the specific amount of zakat is subsumed within that charity. The purpose of zakat (helping the needy) is achieved.
4
Note the Conditions
What are the key conditions for this ruling to apply? The text specifies 'all his wealth' (bismil maalihi). What if he gives only part?
The condition is that the charity must encompass the entire wealth. If only a portion is given, the qiyas stands and intention is required.
5
Apply to Practice
Consider a scenario: someone donates his entire savings (all he owns) to a valid charity without mentioning zakat. According to this ruling, the zakat is discharged. Think about the implications for modern charitable giving.
This is a rukhsah (concession) – not the norm, but a valid dispensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٦١) ولو تصدّق بجميع ماله ولم ينو الزكوة سقط عنه . ترجمه: اگر کسی نے اپنا تمام مال صدقہ کر دیا اور زکوۃ کی نیت نہ کی تو زکوۃ کی فرضیت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ تشریح: تمام مال کو صدقہ کی نیت سے دیدیا لیکن اس میں زکوۃ کی نیت نہیں کی تو جتنا مال زکوۃ میں دینا تھا اس کی ادائیگی ہوگئی اور فرض ساقط ہو گیا۔ قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کی نیت نہیں کی ہے اس لئے زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہونی چاہئے لیکن تمام مال صدقہ کرنے کی وجہ سے اسکے تحت میں زکوۃ بھی ادا ہو جائے گی۔
(1161) And if he gives in sadaqah all his wealth and does not intend zakat, the zakat obligation is remitted. Translation: If someone gave all his wealth in charity and did not intend zakat, then the obligation of zakat will be remitted. Explanation: He gave all his wealth with the intention of sadaqah but did not intend zakat within it, then whatever amount he was required to give as zakat, that payment has been made and the obligation has been remitted. Qiyas requires that since he did not intend zakat, zakat should not be valid, but because he gave all his wealth in charity, zakat is also covered within that.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario: a person gives away all his wealth as general charity (sadaqah) without specifically intending zakat. According to the Hanafi school, this action discharges the zakat obligation. The commentator notes that by qiyas (analogy), this should not be sufficient because intention for zakat is lacking. However, the ruling goes against qiyas on the basis that if one gives away all his wealth, it inevitably covers the zakat due, even if not intended. This is a concession (rukhsah) that treats the overall charitable act as fulfilling the zakat obligation. The apparent reasoning is that the purpose of zakat (helping the poor) is achieved, and the requirement of specific intention is waived in this extreme case.

Key Terms
سقط عنه (saqata 'anhu): The obligation (zakat) falls from him, meaning it is discharged and no longer required.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used here to contrast with the actual ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if someone gives all their wealth in charity (sadaqah) without any intention of zakat?
A) The zakat obligation remains and must be paid separately.
B) The zakat obligation is remitted because the charity covers it.
C) It is valid only if the charity is given to relatives.
D) It is invalid because intention is required for any worship.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that giving all wealth in charity discharges the zakat obligation, overriding the usual requirement of specific intention, due to the comprehensive nature of the act.

Intention in Zakat: Virtual Conjunction and Recipient's Knowledge
Rulings on intention being concurrent or subsequent in zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intention can be made after giving zakat as long as the property remains with the recipient, and state that the recipient need not know it is zakat.

Core Idea
Zakat intention can be delayed if the property remains; the recipient need not know it's zakat.

Intention (niyyah) is essential for the validity of zakat, but the Hanafi school provides practical leniency. This lesson examines two key rulings: first, that intention can be made even after the act of giving, as long as the property is still with the recipient (virtual conjunction); second, that the recipient does not need to be informed that the payment is zakat. These rulings are rooted in the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' and aim to facilitate fulfillment of the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is paying zakat. The ruling is that intention must be concurrent, but a virtual conjunction (muqaranah hukmiyyah) is accepted if intention is made while the property is still with the recipient.
The text also addresses the condition of the recipient's knowledge.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' (Actions are by intentions). This is a general principle for all acts of worship.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes that intention is required for the validity of any act. For zakat, the intention must be present at the time of giving, but the Hanafis allow virtual conjunction based on istihsan (juristic preference) to ease fulfillment.
The Hanafi position relies on the principle that the recipient becomes an agent for the payer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'is) require actual conjunction of intention and also require the recipient to know the payment is zakat. The Hanafi school does not require such knowledge.
The Hanafi view is 'ala al-ashah (the most sound).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that virtual conjunction suffices and recipient knowledge is not a condition. This is supported by the need to avoid embarrassment and facilitate giving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

To the poor person or his agent, or to set aside what is obligatory (1159) even if it is a virtual conjunction, as if he gave without intention then intended while the property remains in the hand of the poor person. (1160) It is not a condition that the poor person knows it is zakat according to the most correct view, such that if he gave him something and called it a gift or a loan and intended zakat by it, it is valid.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings on intention (niyyah) in zakat. The text first states that zakat may be given to the poor person, his agent, or set aside as an obligation. Ruling (1159) allows for a virtual conjunction of intention: if one gives without intention and later intends while the property is still with the recipient, the zakat is valid because the recipient becomes like an agent for the payer. The Urdu commentary gives an example: A gives a loan to B (poor), then later tells B to arrange repayment and then gives a different amount with zakat intention – that counts. Ruling (1160) clarifies that the recipient need not know it is zakat; even if given as a gift or loan, the payer's inner intention suffices. The proof is the hadith 'Actions are by intentions,' which requires intention for all primary acts of worship. The passage concludes that at these four times, intention alone suffices because they are times of zakat payment.

Key Terms
مقارنة حكمية (muqaranah hukmiyyah): Virtual conjunction: intention is considered concurrent even if made after the act, provided the property is still with the recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the recipient is informed later
B) When the property is still in the recipient's possession and the payer intends zakat
C) Only if the property is consumed
D) When the payer has no prior intention

Key Takeaway
Intention in zakat can be made after giving as long as the property remains with the recipient, and the recipient need not be aware it is zakat.

Donating All Wealth as Sadaqah Without Zakat Intention
Ruling that giving all wealth as charity fulfills zakat obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that giving all wealth as sadaqah fulfills zakat even without intention, and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Zakat is lifted when all wealth is given as charity — intention is waived because the entire wealth exceeds the due amount.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling: if a person gives away all his wealth as voluntary charity (sadaqah) without intending zakat, the zakat obligation is still discharged. The commentary explains that while analogy (qiyas) would require intention, juristic preference (istihsan) overrides it because the entire wealth is given, subsuming the zakat portion. Understanding this exception clarifies the role of intention in zakat and the scope of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving all wealth as sadaqah without zakat intention. The ruling is that the zakat obligation falls (saqata).
The Arabic term 'saqata' indicates complete removal of liability.
2
Locate the implicit proof
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that would require intention.
Qiyas would say zakat is not fulfilled, but istihsan gives the opposite ruling.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The effective cause is that the entire wealth is given, so the zakat due is a subset of the charity. Thus, the charity automatically covers it.
This is a khafi (hidden) qiyas turned by istihsan.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may require specific intention for zakat even when all wealth is given. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that the obligation is a debt to Allah that can be fulfilled by any payment covering the due.
This shows the Hanafi emphasis on the substantive fulfillment over the form.
5
Apply the ruling to partial giving
If only part of wealth is given as sadaqah without intention, the zakat is not fulfilled because the charity does not necessarily cover the zakat portion.
The exception applies strictly when the entire wealth is given.

Source Text

And if he gives in charity all his wealth and does not intend zakat, the obligation of zakat falls from him.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of giving all wealth as voluntary charity (sadaqah) without specific intention for zakat. The ruling states that if a person gives away all his wealth as sadaqah without intending zakat, the zakat obligation is still discharged from him. The Urdu commentary explains that if one gives all wealth as charity, even without zakat intention, the portion that was due as zakat is considered paid and the obligation is lifted. The commentary notes that by analogy (qiyas), one would think zakat is not fulfilled because intention is missing, but the ruling here overrides that: because the entire wealth is given, the zakat portion is included in the general charity. This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas.

Key Terms
سقط عنه فرضها (saqata 'anhu farduha): The obligation falls from him, meaning it is considered fulfilled and no longer owed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that giving all wealth as charity fulfills zakat even without specific intention, because the zakat portion is subsumed under the general charity.

Zakat on Debts: The Hanafi Tripartite Classification
Classification of debts for zakat into three types with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a debt as strong, medium, or weak and apply the corresponding zakat ruling with its conditions.

Core Idea
Debts differ in zakat according to certainty of recovery; strong debts incur past zakat, weak debts only upon possession plus a year.

Zakat on debts owed to you is not a single rule. The Hanafi school distinguishes debts by how reliably you expect to be repaid. This lesson unpacks the famous tripartite classification — strong, medium, weak — and explains exactly when each triggers the zakat obligation, supported by the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the text and note the three categories: strong (qawi), medium (wasat), weak (daif). Each has a different definition based on the debtor's acknowledgment or denial and the presence of evidence.
The categories are based on the probability of recovery, not the debtor's financial status alone.
2
State the ruling for strong debts
For a strong debt (loan or trade price, debtor acknowledges or denies with evidence), zakat becomes wajib immediately upon possession, and past years must be covered.
This is the most severe ruling; the creditor must calculate zakat for all the years the debt was outstanding.
3
State the ruling for medium debts
For a medium debt (likely but not certain), zakat is wajib only when the received amount reaches nisab, and the one-year count begins from the date of possession.
No zakat is due for the period before possession.
4
State the ruling for weak debts
For a weak debt (doubtful recovery, like from a denier without evidence or an insolvent person with no hope), zakat is wajib only after a full year has passed from the date of possession.
Only one zakat payment; past years are ignored.
5
Locate and evaluate the evidence
The author cites three athar: Ibn Umar's distinction between reliable and doubtful debts, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz's treatment of recovered oppressed wealth as 'dhimar', and Ali's conditional ruling on weak debts. Understand how each supports the Hanafi classification.
These are qawl sahabi; their authority is zanni but accepted in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزكوة الدين على اقسام فانه قوى ووسط وضعيفٌ (١١٦٣) فالقوى وهو بدل القرض ومال التجارة اذا قبضه وكان على مقرّ ولو مُفلسا او على جاحد عليه بنية زكاه لما مضى.

ترجمه : (۱۱۶۲) قرض کی زکوۃ کی چند قسمیں ہیں، قوی ، متوسط ، ضعیف۔ تشریح : کسی کو پونڈ قرض دیا اب اس پر قبضے کی تین صورتیں ہیں [1] اگر قبضہ مضبوط ہے تو ابھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ [۲] اگر قبضہ متوسط ہے تو نصاب کے برابر [ دوسو درہم ) قبضہ کرے گا تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اور قبضہ سے پہلے ایک سال کا اعتبار ہوگا (۳) اور اگر قبضہ ضعیف ہے تو نصاب کے برابر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اس پر سال گزرے گا تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔
وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال زكوا ما كان في ايدكم و ما كان من دين في ثقة فهو بمنزلة ما في ايديكم ، و ما كان من دين ظنون فلا زكوة فيه حتى يقبضه - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب زکاۃ الدین اذا كان على معسر أو جاحد، ج رابع ، ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۷۶۲۴ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب و ما کان لا یستقر یعطیه الیوم و یا خذالی یومین فلیز کہ، ج ثانی ،ص ۱۳۸۹، نمبر (۱۰۲۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جو مال قابل اعتماد کے پاس ہو اسکی زکوۃ دو، اور جو مال ظنون یعنی جسکے پاس سے قرض وصول ہونے میں پورا شک ہو اس قرض کے وصول ہونے کے بعد زکوۃ شروع ہوگی ۔ (۲) ان عمر بن عبد العزيز كتب في مال قبـضـه بـعـض الولاة ظلما يأمر برده الى أهله و تؤخذ زكاته لما مضى من السنين ثم اعقب بعد ذالك بكتاب أن لا تؤخذ منه الا زكاة واحدة فانه كان ضمار ا ثم قال أبو عبيد : يعني الغائب الذي لا يرجى (سنن بیہقی ، باب زكاة الدین اذا کان علی معسر أو جاحد، ج رابع ، ص ۲۵۳، نمبر ۷۶۲۶ ) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ حضرت عمر ابن عبد العزیز صرف اس سال کی زکوۃ لیتے تھے جس سال ظلم سے لیا ہوا مال واپس آیا ہو، پچھلے سالوں کا نہیں ۔ کیونکہ یہ مال ضمار کی طرح ہے ۔ (۳) حضرت علی کے قول میں ہے۔ قال ابو عبيد في حديث على في الرجل يكون له الدين الظنون قال يزكيه لما مضى اذا قبضه ان كان صادقا ( سنن بیہقی ، باب زکاۃ الدین اذا کان علی معسر او جاحد، ج رابع ،ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۷۶۲۳ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب و ما كان لا يستقر يعطيه اليوم ودياً خذ الی یومین فلیز کہ، ج ثانی، ص۱۳۹۰، نمبر ۱۰۲۵۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ شک والے قرض کا آدمی سچا ہو تو پچھلے سالوں کی زکوۃ ادا کرو، اور سچا نہ ہوتو ادا نہ کرو۔
اصول: جو مال مضمار کی طرح ہو اس میں پچھلے سالوں کی زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ مال ہاتھ آنے کے بعد زکوۃ شروع ہوگی۔
And the zakat of debt is of categories: strong, medium, and weak. (1163) The strong is the substitute for loan and trade goods when he takes possession of it and it is upon one who acknowledges even if bankrupt, or upon a denier with evidence; he must pay zakat for the past.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage details the rulings on zakat for debts owed to a person. The original text categorizes debts into strong (qawi), medium (wasat), and weak (daif). The strong debt is defined as a loan or price of trade goods with a reliable debtor, whether he admits the debt (even if bankrupt) or denies it but there is evidence. Upon possession, zakat must be paid for past years. The Urdu commentary expands: for strong debts (certain recovery), zakat is wajib immediately upon possession, covering past years. For medium debts (uncertain but likely), zakat becomes wajib once the amount reaches nisab, and one year is counted from possession. For weak debts (doubtful recovery), a full year must pass after possession before zakat is due (only one zakat, not past years). The proofs are athar from Ibn Umar, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, and Ali ibn Abi Talib. Ibn Umar said: give zakat on what is in your hands and on trust debts; doubtful debts require zakat only after receipt. Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz only took one zakat on recovered oppressed wealth, treating it like 'dhimar' (lost hope). Ali said: if the debtor is truthful, pay zakat for past years upon receipt; if not, no past zakat. The principle: for property like dhimar, no past zakat; zakat begins after possession.

Key Terms
الدين القوي (al-dayn al-qawi): Strong debt: a loan or trade debt owed by a reliable debtor, whether acknowledging or denying with evidence.
الدين الظنون (al-dayn al-dhanun): Doubtful debt: where recovery is uncertain, such as from a denier without evidence or an insolvent person with no hope.
ضمار (dhimar): Lost hope: property whose recovery is not expected, like a debt from an insolvent person who has no means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the correct ruling for a 'strong debt' (al-dayn al-qawi)?
A) Zakat is due only after a full year from possession, with no zakat for past years.
B) Zakat is due immediately upon possession for all past years the debt was outstanding.
C) Zakat is due only if the debtor is not bankrupt.
D) Zakat is not due at all because debts are exempt from zakat in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on debts varies by the certainty of recovery: strong debts require past zakat; weak debts require only one year after possession.

Zakat on Debt: The Three Categories (Qawi, Wasat, Da'if)
Classifying debt zakat into three categories with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a debt as qawi, wasat, or da'if and determine when zakat becomes due according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A debt's collectability determines its zakat timing: strong debt is zakatable from the start; medium and weak debts are delayed.

The Hanafi school uniquely classifies debts into three categories based on the strength of collectability. This lesson unpacks each category and explains when zakat becomes due, with proofs from the sayings of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the debt
Determine if the debt is a loan (qard) or the price of trade goods (mal al-tijarah) – these are the two forms of strong debt (qawi). If it is the price of a non-trade item (e.g., used clothes, house), it is medium (wasat). If collection is doubtful (e.g., debtor denies without proof), it is weak (da'if).
The intention at the time of lending matters: trade goods vs. personal use.
2
Examine the debtor's reliability
For strong debt, the debtor must either acknowledge the debt (even if insolvent) or deny it but the lender has witnesses. For medium debt, the debtor's reliability is irrelevant because the item sold was not for trade. For weak debt, the debtor denies and the lender has no proof.
The strong debt is considered as if the money were in the lender's possession because he can collect it at will.
3
Apply the zakat trigger rules
Strong debt: upon receiving any amount (at least 40 dirhams), zakat is due for all past years since the debt was incurred. Medium debt: zakat is due only after receiving the full nisab (200 dirhams) and a full year has passed from the sale. Weak debt: treat as dhimar (lost property); zakat is due only after receiving the nisab and a full year passes from receipt.
The exception: for strong debt, zakat on amounts below 40 dirhams is exempt (one-fifth of nisab is exempt).
4
Understand the evidence
The primary proof is the athar of Ibn Umar (ra) that reliable debt is like cash in hand, and doubtful debt has no zakat until received. Additional athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and Ali (ra) support the treatment of doubtful debts as dhimar.
These are qawl sahabi, which is a source of law in the Hanafi school.

فرضها. (۱۱۶۲) وزكوة الدين على اقسام فانه قوى ووسط وضعيفٌ (١١٦٣) فالقوى وهو بدل القرض ومال التجارة اذا قبضه وكان على مقرّ ولو مُفلسا او على جاحد عليه بنية زكاه لما مضى. وجه: تمام مال کے صدقہ نافلہ میں فرض داخل ہو گیا اس لئے الگ سے نیت کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی ترجمه : (۱۱۶۲) قرض کی زکوۃ کی چند قسمیں ہیں، قوی ، متوسط ، ضعیف۔ تشریح : کسی کو پونڈ قرض دیا اب اس پر قبضے کی تین صورتیں ہیں [1] اگر قبضہ مضبوط ہے تو ابھی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ [۲] اگر قبضہ متوسط ہے تو نصاب کے برابر [ دوسو درہم ) قبضہ کرے گا تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اور قبضہ سے پہلے ایک سال کا اعتبار ہوگا (۳) اور اگر قبضہ ضعیف ہے تو نصاب کے برابر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اس پر سال گزرے گا تب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔

اصول: جو مال مال مضمار کی طرح ہو اس میں پچھلے سالوں کی زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ مال ہاتھ آنے کے بعد زکوۃ شروع ہوگی۔ ترجمه : (۱۱۶۳) قوی وہ قرض کا بدلہ ہے، اور مال تجارت کا بدلہ ہے جب اس پر قبضہ کرلے۔ اور قرض کے اقرار کرنے والے پر ہو چاہے مفلس ہو، یا انکار کرنے والے پر ہو اور اس پر گواہ ہو تو گزرے ہوئے کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ تشریح قوی قرض کی دو صورتیں ہیں [1] قرض کا اقرار کرتا ہو تو چاہے وہ مفلس ہو جب اس پر قبضہ ہو جائے تو پچھلے سالوں کی

قال زكوا ما كان فى ايدكم و ما كان من دين فى ثقة فهو بمنزلة ما فى ايديكم ، و ما كان من دين ظنون فلا زكوة فيه حتى يقبضه - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب زكاة الدین اذا کان علی معسر أو جاحد ، ج رابع ، ص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۷۶۲۴ مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، باب و ما كان لا يستقر يعطيه اليوم وياً خذ الی یومین فلیز که ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۸۹، نمبر ۱۰۲۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جو مال قابل اعتماد کے پاس ہو اسکی زکوۃ دو، اور جو مال ظنون یعنی جسکے پاس سے قرض وصول ہونے میں پورا شک ہواس قرض کے وصول ہونے کے بعد زکوۃ شروع ہوگی ترجمه : (۱۲۴) اور آدائیگی مؤخر ہوگی چالیس درہم قبضہ کرنے تک ۔ پس چالیس درہم میں ایک درہم ہے، اس لئے کہ نصاب کے پانچویں حصے سے کم معاف ہے، اس میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے، اور ایسے ہی اس سے زیادہ میں اس کے حساب سے۔ تشریح : اس قوی قرض پر چالیس درہم قبضہ ہو جائے تو اس میں ایک درہم واجب ہوگی ۔ اس لئے کہ اس سے کم ہو تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے، اور چالیس سے زیادہ ہو مثلا اسی درہم ہو تو اس پر دو درہم زکوۃ واجب ہے ۔ وجه : خود قارض کے پاس چالیس درہم سے کم ہوتی تو ز کا ۃ واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے قرض ملنے کے بعد چالیس درہم سے کم ہے تو زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی ترجمه : (۱۱۹۵) اور متوسط قرض ، یہ ہے کہ مال تجارت کا بدلہ نہ ہو، جیسے استعمالی کپڑے کی قیمت ، اور خدمت کے غلام کی قیمت ، اور رہنے کے گھر کی قیمت، اس میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی جب تک نصاب پر قبضہ نہ کرے۔
تشریح : جو چیز تجارت کی نہیں ہے اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے، ہاں بیچنے کے بعد اس کی قیمت تجارت کی بنے گی ، اور بکنے کے بعد سے سال پورا ہوا ہو اور نصاب تک یعنی دوسو درہم تک پہنچا ہوتو اس پر بکنے کے دن سے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ، البتہ پورے نصاب پر قبضہ کے بعد زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔
Thamarat an-Najah Volume 2, Book of Zakat. Its obligation. (1162) And zakat on debt is divided into categories: strong, medium, weak. (1163) The strong: it is the substitute of a loan and the price of trade goods when he takes possession of it, and it is upon an acknowledge (debtor) even if insolvent, or upon a denier with evidence; then he gives zakat for the past. Explanation: Complete wealth, in voluntary charity, the obligatory enters into it, so there is no need for a separate intention; the payment of zakat will be valid. Translation: (1162) Zakat on loan has several categories: strong, medium, weak. Explanation: (1) If possession is strong, then zakat becomes immediately due. (2) If possession is medium, then only after taking possession of the nisab (200 dirhams) does zakat become due, and the year is counted from before possession. (3) If possession is weak, then after taking possession of the nisab, a year passes, then zakat becomes due. Proof: (1) This is proven by the saying of the Companion: from Ibn Umar: 'Give zakat on what is in your hands, and any debt that is reliable is in the position of what is in your hands; but a debt that is doubtful has no zakat until he receives it.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Zakat al-Dayn...). This effect states: Give zakat on wealth that is with a reliable person, and for doubtful debt, i.e., where there is complete doubt about receipt, zakat begins after receipt. (2) Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote concerning wealth that some governors had seized unjustly, ordering its return to its owners and zakat taken for past years; then after that he wrote a letter that only one zakat be taken, because it was like a lost thing (dhimar). Then Abu Ubayd said: it means the absent one that is not hoped for. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This saying of a Tabi’i states that Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz would only take zakat for the year in which the unjustly seized wealth was returned, not for past years, because this wealth is like lost property. (3) In the saying of Ali: Abu Ubayd said in a hadith of Ali concerning a man who has a doubtful debt: he said he gives zakat for the past when he receives it, if he is truthful. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This effect states: For doubtful debt, if the person is truthful, he gives zakat for past years; if not truthful, he does not. Principle: Wealth that is like lost property has no zakat for past years; zakat begins after the wealth comes into hand. Translation: (1163) The strong debt is the substitute of a loan and the substitute of trade goods when he takes possession of it. And it is upon a debtor who acknowledges (the debt) even if he is insolvent, or upon a denier who has evidence, then zakat for the past is due. Explanation of strong debt: Two cases: (1) If the debtor acknowledges, even if he is insolvent, when possession is taken, zakat for past years is due. (1164) And the obligation of payment is deferred until he takes possession of forty dirhams; then there is one dirham in it, because less than one-fifth of the nisab is exempt, no zakat in it, and likewise for more, proportionally. (1165) And the medium: it is the substitute of what is not for trade, zakat is also due. Second case: The debtor denies but the lender has witnesses, then this debt is like strong, so upon taking possession of forty dirhams, zakat for past years is due. Example: In 2009 he lent five hundred dirhams, and the debtor returned in 2011; then the lender owes zakat from 2009 onwards, but he must pay after receiving the debt. Proof: (1) Because the debtor acknowledges or denies but the lender has witnesses, so this amount is as if it were with the lender, because he can take it back from the debtor whenever he wishes. And if the amount were with the lender, zakat would be due from the time the nisab was complete; similarly, zakat is due on this debt. (2) This is proven by the saying of the Companion: from Ibn Umar: 'Give zakat on what is in your hands, and any debt that is reliable is in the position of what is in your hands; but a debt that is doubtful has no zakat until he receives it.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This effect states: Give zakat on wealth that is with a reliable person, and for doubtful debt, zakat begins after receipt. Translation: (1164) And payment is deferred until he takes possession of forty dirhams; then one dirham is due, because less than one-fifth of the nisab is exempt, no zakat in it, and likewise for more, proportionally. Explanation: Upon taking possession of forty dirhams of this strong debt, one dirham is due. Because if it is less, there is no zakat; if more, e.g., eighty dirhams, then two dirhams are due. Proof: If the lender himself had less than forty dirhams, zakat would not be due; similarly, after receiving the debt, if it is less than forty, no zakat. Translation: (1165) And the medium debt is that which is not the substitute of trade goods, such as the price of used clothes, the price of a servant for service, the price of a house for dwelling—there is no zakat on these until he takes possession of the nisab. Explanation: An item that is not for trade has no zakat; however, after selling, its price becomes for trade, and if a year passes after the sale and it reaches the nisab (200 dirhams), then zakat is due from the day of sale, but only after taking possession of the full nisab.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Zakat explains the Hanafi ruling on zakat on debts (dayn). It opens by stating that zakat on debt is divided into three categories based on the strength of collectability: strong (qawi), medium (wasat), and weak (da'if). The strong debt includes the substitute of a loan (i.e., the amount lent) and the price of trade goods. For a strong debt, if the debtor acknowledges the debt (even if insolvent) or denies it but the lender has witnesses, then upon taking possession of at least forty dirhams, zakat becomes due for all past years since the debt was incurred. This is because the debt is considered as if it were in the lender's possession, as he can collect it at will. The proof is an athar from Ibn Umar (radiAllahu anhu) that reliable debt is treated like cash in hand, and an athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz regarding wealth seized unjustly. The passage then clarifies that the obligation to pay is deferred until the lender receives forty dirhams, because amounts below one-fifth of the nisab (i.e., 40 dirhams out of 200) are exempt. For medium debt, which is the substitute of something not intended for trade (e.g., used clothes, a house), no zakat is due until the recipient takes possession of the full nisab (200 dirhams) and a year passes. The weak debt (da'if) is covered briefly: zakat is due only after possession of the nisab and a full year thereafter. The passage uses two main athar as evidence, both from Sunan al-Bayhaqi. The overall principle is that zakat on debt follows the ease of collection: the more reliable the debt, the sooner zakat becomes due, and past years are counted.

Key Terms
دين قوي (dayn qawi): Strong debt: a debt that is acknowledged by the debtor or can be proven by witnesses, treated as if the money were in the lender's possession.
دين وسط (dayn wasat): Medium debt: the price of an item not originally for trade (e.g., used clothes, house); zakat only due after receiving the full nisab and the intention of trade is established after sale.
دين ضعيف (dayn da'if): Weak debt: a debt where collection is doubtful (e.g., debtor denier without proof); zakat due only after possession of nisab and a full year passes.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth subject to zakat, here 200 dirhams for silver or equivalent.
ضماءر (dhimar): Lost or unseen property that is not hoped for; applied to doubtful debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on zakat for a medium debt (dayn wasat) such as the price of a used house?
A) Zakat is due for past years upon receipt of any amount.
B) Zakat is due only after receiving the full nisab (200 dirhams) and a year has passed from the sale.
C) No zakat is ever due on such debt.
D) Zakat is due immediately upon the sale, even before receipt.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires zakat on strong debts from the time of lending, while medium and weak debts are treated differently to protect the poor and account for collectability.

Zakat on Strong Debt (Qard Qawi)
Ruling on zakat for strong debt with proof from Ibn Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for strong debt and apply the rule to calculate zakat owed upon receipt.

Core Idea
Strong debt is like cash: zakat is due on past years once you receive the nisab.

This lesson addresses a common practical question: if someone owes you money for several years and then pays you, do you owe zakat for those past years? The Hanafi school has a clear answer based on the reliability of the debt. We will examine the ruling and its proof from a companion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of debt and the ruling
First, note that the passage distinguishes between strong (qard qawi) and doubtful (dayn zannun) debts. For strong debts, zakat is deferred until receipt, but once received, past years must be accounted for.
Strong debt is acknowledged or witnessed; doubtful debt is denied or unreliable.
2
Understand the condition: receipt of nisab
Zakat is only triggered when the creditor receives at least forty dirhams (the minimum nisab for silver). Upon receiving that amount, one dirham (2.5%) is due for each year the debt was outstanding.
The text says 'ويتراخى وجوب الاداء الى ان يقبض اربعين درهما'.
3
Apply the calculation method
If the received amount is forty dirhams, one dirham is wajib. For any amount above forty, the same 2.5% rate applies proportionally. The 'one-fifth of nisab' exemption refers to amounts less than five dirhams? Actually, the text says 'لان ما دون الخمس من النصاب عفو' – less than one-fifth of the nisab (i.e., less than 8 dirhams? Wait: nisab is 200 dirhams, one-fifth is 40? That doesn't fit. Re-reading: The passage says: 'ما دون الخمس من النصاب عفو' meaning 'what is less than five dirhams of the nisab is exempt'. Actually, the nisab for silver is 200 dirhams, but here they talk about receiving 40 dirhams. The phrasing is ambiguous but the intended meaning is that the nisab for zakat on debt is based on the amount received: if you receive at least 40 dirhams (which is one-fifth of 200? No, 200/5=40, so 'one-fifth of the nisab' refers to the nisab for the debt itself, which is set at 40 dirhams. So any amount below 40 dirhams is exempt; 40 dirhams triggers zakat of 1 dirham (2.5%).
This is consistent with the Hanafi position that zakat is not due on less than 40 dirhams of silver.
4
Analyze the proof from Ibn Umar
The companion said: 'Pay zakat on what is in your hands, and whatever debt is reliable is like what is in your hands.' This analogizes strong debt to cash in hand, meaning zakat is required annually even if unpaid, but the Hanafi position defers the act of paying zakat until receipt for practical reasons.
The evidence is a qawl sahabi, which is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
5
Contrast with doubtful debt
Ibn Umar also said: 'Whatever debt is doubtful, no zakat on it until he receives it.' This shows that doubtful debts are not subject to deferred zakat for past years; only the year of receipt counts.
This distinction is crucial for fatwa: the mufti must ascertain the reliability of the debt.

ويتراخى وجوب الاداء الى ان يقبض اربعين درهما ففيها در هم لان ما دون الخمس من النصاب عفو لا زكوة فيه وكذا فيما زاد بحسابه . عن ابن عمر قال زكوا ما كان فى ايدكم و ما كان من دين فى ثقة فهو بمنزلة ما فى ايديكم ، و ما كان من دين ظنون فلا زكوة فيه حتى يقبضه
The obligation to pay is deferred until he receives forty dirhams, then in them is one dirham, because what is less than one-fifth of the nisab is exempt, no zakat on it, and similarly for what exceeds it proportionally. From Ibn Umar, he said: Pay zakat on what is in your hands, and whatever debt is reliable is like what is in your hands, and whatever debt is doubtful then no zakat on it until he receives it.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on zakat for strong debt (qard qawi). It states that zakat on a strong debt (where the debtor admits or there are witnesses) is deferred until the creditor actually receives forty dirhams (the minimum nisab). Upon receiving forty dirhams, one dirham (2.5%) is due for each year that the debt was owed, because the amount below one-fifth of the nisab is exempt. The proof is an athar from Ibn Umar, which distinguishes between reliable (thiqa) and doubtful (zannun) debts: reliable debts are treated like cash in hand, requiring zakat annually, while doubtful debts only require zakat after receipt. The Hanafi position is that strong debts trigger zakat on past years once received, provided the nisab is met.

Key Terms
قرض قوي (qard qawi): A strong debt: a loan that is acknowledged by the debtor or supported by witnesses, making it easily collectible.
دين ظنون (dayn zannun): A doubtful debt: one where the debtor denies or is unreliable, making collection uncertain.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat (for silver, 200 dirhams or its equivalent; but for debt receipt, the threshold is 40 dirhams per this passage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is zakat due on a strong debt of 100 dirhams owed for two years?
A) Zakat is due only in the year of receipt for that year.
B) Zakat is due for the past two years upon receipt of 40 dirhams or more.
C) Zakat is never due on debts.
D) Zakat is due annually regardless of receipt.

Key Takeaway
Strong debt is treated like cash: zakat for past years becomes wajib upon receipt of the nisab.

Zakat on Medium Debt: When and How Much?
Ruling on medium debt from non-trade assets requiring zakat upon receipt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for medium debt (qard wasat), explain when zakat becomes wajib, and calculate the portion of the year due upon receipt.

Core Idea
Zakat on medium debt is due only upon receipt of nisab, counting the year from the sale.

This passage addresses a specific type of debt known as medium debt (qard wasat) — the price received from selling personal-use items like clothes or a house. Unlike trade goods, these are not held for commerce, so their zakat treatment differs. The Hanafi school clarifies that zakat is not required annually on the unpaid debt; instead, it becomes obligatory only when you actually receive the nisab amount, and you only pay for the portion of the lunar year that has elapsed since the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of debt
Medium debt (qard wasat) is the price of non-trade items such as personal clothing, a domestic servant, or a residence. Recognize that this category excludes trade goods.
2
State the trigger for zakat
Zakat is not obligatory until the creditor actually receives a nisab (minimum amount, e.g., 200 dirhams). No zakat is due on the outstanding debt itself.
Contrast with trade goods where annual zakat is due even before sale.
3
Determine the year calculation
The zakat year is counted from the moment the price became binding on the buyer (sale contract date), not from the date of receipt. This is the sound riwayah.
Some narrations may differ, but the preferred view is as stated.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Example: Sold personal property for 500 dirhams. After 6 months from sale, you receive 500 dirhams. Zakat is due for 6 months on the nisab amount (200+ dirhams).
Calculate: 500 * 2.5% * (6/12) = 6.25 dirhams.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may require annual zakat on debts even if not received, considering it as owned wealth. Hanafis differ due to lack of physical control (qabd).
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and based on sound evidence from both sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوسط وهو بدل ما ليس للتجارة مثل ثمن ثياب البذلة وعبد الخدمة ودار السكنى لا تجب الزكوة فيه ما لم يقبض نصابا ويعتبر ما مضى من الحول من وقت لزومه لذمة المشترى فى صحيح الرواية
And the medium (debt) is the price of what is not for trade, like the price of clothes for wear, a servant for service, and a house for residence; zakat is not obligatory therein until he receives a nisab, and the portion of the year that has passed is counted from the time it became binding on the purchaser's liability in the correct narration.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on medium debt (qard wasat). It defines medium debt as the price obtained from selling non-commercial items such as personal clothing, a domestic servant, or a residence. Zakat is not obligatory on such debt until the creditor actually receives a full nisab (e.g., 200 dirhams). Once received, zakat is due for the portion of the year that has passed since the debt became binding on the buyer (i.e., since the sale contract). The Hanafi position, based on the sound riwayah, is that the year is counted from the moment the price became a liability on the purchaser, not from the receipt. Thus, if six months passed after the sale before payment, only six months of zakat are due upon receipt, provided the nisab is met.

Key Terms
بدل ما ليس للتجارة (badal ma laysa lil-tijarah): The price received for selling an item that was not held for trade, such as personal clothing or a house.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation, typically 200 dirhams (silver) or 85 grams of gold.
صحيح الرواية (sahih al-riwayah): The sound/correct narration (riwayah) from the Hanafi imams, indicating the preferred transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon the sale contract.
B) Only when the seller receives a nisab amount, with the year counted from the sale date.
C) Every year as the debt remains outstanding.
D) Only on the profit portion of the sale.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on medium debt is deferred until receipt of nisab, and the zakat year is counted from the sale contract date.

Zakat on Weak Debt (Qard Da'if)
Ruling on weak debt: definition, examples, and zakat timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define weak debt, list its examples, and state the Hanafi ruling on when zakat becomes obligatory on it.

Core Idea
Zakat on weak debt is due only after receipt and a full year — uncertainty delays the obligation.

You have seen the general rule that zakat is due on wealth after a year. But what about debts that are not certain to be collected? The Hanafi school distinguishes between strong and weak debts. This lesson examines the category of weak debt (qard da'if) and the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifah that zakat is not obligatory on such debts until the creditor actually receives the payment and then a full lunar year passes.

Guided Path
1
Define weak debt
Start by understanding the definition: a weak debt is compensation for something that is not considered property (mal) in itself, such as dower or blood money. Its collection is uncertain because the debtor may not be able or willing to pay.
The opposite is strong debt (qard qawi), which is for property loans or sale price.
2
Identify the examples given
The text lists: mahr (dower), wasiyyah (bequest), khul' compensation, blood money (diyah), settlement for intentional killing, kitabah (manumission contract), and sa'yah (earnings of a part-freed slave). Memorise these as the standard weak debts in Hanafi fiqh.
These are all situations where the debt is not for a tangible asset.
3
State the ruling on zakat
According to Abu Hanifah, zakat is not wajib on weak debt until two conditions are met: receipt of a nisab (minimum threshold, e.g., 200 dirhams) and the passage of a full lunar year after that receipt.
This means no annual zakat during the period the debt is outstanding.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differed: they considered some of these weak debts as strong, requiring zakat upon receipt for past years. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is that of Abu Hanifah.
The text specifies 'at Abu Hanifah' to mark his view as the basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والضعيف وهو بدل ما ليس بمال كالمهر والوصيّة وبدل الخلع والصلح عن دم العمد والديّة وبدل الكتابة والسعاية لا تجب فيه الزكوة ما لم يقبض نصابا ويحول عليه الحول بعد القبض وهذا عند ابي حنيفة
And the weak (debt) is the price of what is not wealth, like the dower, bequest, price of khul', settlement for intentional killing, blood money, price of kitabah, and sa'yah; zakat is not obligatory therein until he receives a nisab and a year passes after receipt, and this is according to Abu Hanifah.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on weak debt (qard da'if). Weak debt is the compensation for things that are not considered wealth in themselves, such as mahr (dower), wasiyyah (bequest), khul' compensation, blood money (diyah), settlement for intentional homicide, kitabah (contract of manumission), and sa'yah (earnings of a part-freed slave). According to Imam Abu Hanifah, zakat is not obligatory on such debts until the creditor actually receives a full nisab (e.g., 200 dirhams) and then a full lunar year passes after that receipt. This is because these debts are not considered property until actually in hand. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad may differ; the text specifies 'at Abu Hanifah' indicating his position is the basis. The Hanafi school follows this view.

Key Terms
قرض ضعيف (qard da'if): A weak debt: a debt that is not for property, such as dower or blood money, where collection is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman receives her mahr of 500 dirhams after two years. According to Abu Hanifah, when is zakat due?
A) Zakat is due for the two past years upon receipt.
B) Zakat is due one year after receipt.
C) Zakat is due immediately upon receipt.
D) Zakat is never due on mahr.

Key Takeaway
Weak debt delays zakat until one year after receipt because of its uncertain nature as compensation for non-property.

Zakat on Sale Proceeds of Personal-Use Items: Year Counted from Purchase
States ruling on zakat year for proceeds of non-trade items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for calculating the zakat year on proceeds from selling personal-use items and apply it to a concrete scenario.

Core Idea
The zakat year on proceeds of personal-use items begins at purchase, not at sale.

When someone sells an item that was never intended for trade, the money received becomes subject to zakat only after conditions are met. A key condition is the passage of a full lunar year. This lesson clarifies exactly when that year begins according to the Hanafi school, ensuring correct zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject Items
Recognize the three categories of personal-use items mentioned: clothes for wear, a servant for service, and a dwelling house. These are not trade goods initially.
These are examples; the ruling extends to any similar personal-use item.
2
Determine the Triggering Event
Zakat becomes relevant upon sale when the price is received. However, the ruling specifies that the zakat year is not counted from this event alone.
3
Apply the Year Calculation Rule
The year is counted from the original purchase date of the item, not from the date of sale. The text states: 'from the time it becomes binding upon the buyer’s liability' – i.e., purchase.
The Arabic phrase 'min waqt luzumihi fi dhimmat al-mushtari' refers to the purchase contract.
4
Consider Nisab Requirement
Zakat is only due if the sale price reaches the nisab threshold and a full year has passed since purchase.
Nisab is the minimum amount of wealth subject to zakat.
5
Recognize the Authority
This is the correct (sahih) narration within the Hanafi school, as indicated by the text. It is the mufta bihi position.
No intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned in this excerpt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر كثمن ثياب البذلة وعبد الخدمة ودار السكنى لا تجب الزكوة فيه ما لم يقبض نصابا لما مضى من الحول من وقت لزومه لذمة المشترى فى صحيح الرواية. ترجمه : (۱۱۲۶) اور سال کا جو حصہ گزر گیا ہے اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا مشتری کے ذمے لازم ہونے کے وقت سے ہی روایت یہ ہے۔ تشریح : جس وقت مشتری نے استعمالی کپڑے وغیرہ کوخریدا ہے اس وقت سے سال شمار ہوگا صحیح روایت یہی ہے، کیونکہ اسی وقت سے یہ مال مال تجارت بن گیا ہے۔
And it is considered: From the price of clothes for wear, a servant for service, and a house for dwelling, zakat is not obligatory therein until he takes possession of a nisab, for what has passed of the year from the time it becomes binding upon the buyer's liability in the correct narration. Translation (1126): And consideration will be given to whatever portion of the year has passed from the time it became binding upon the buyer's liability, this is the narration. Explanation: From the time the buyer bought the clothes for wear, etc., the year will be counted from that time; the correct narration is this, because from that time this wealth became trade goods.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding zakat on the proceeds of selling personal-use items that originally were not for trade. The text states that when someone sells items like everyday clothes, a domestic servant, or a residence house, these were not trade goods initially. Upon sale, the payment received becomes trade capital. The zakat year for this amount begins from the time of purchase, not from the time of sale, according to the sahih riwaya (the correct transmission). The reasoning is that from the moment of purchase, the intention was to use the item, but when sold, it becomes trade. However, Hanafi methodology counts the year from the original acquisition because that is when it could have been trade if intended. The ruling clarifies that zakat is only due if the sale price reaches nisab and a full year passes from the original purchase date. The commentary in Urdu elaborates that the accurate narration is to count from the purchase, as the wealth becomes trade money from that point.

Key Terms
ثیاب البذلة (thiyab al-badhla): Clothes meant for everyday wear, not for trade.
عبد الخدمة (abd al-khidmah): A slave kept for domestic service, not for sale.
دار السكنى (dar al-sukna): A house intended for residence, not for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) After a full year from the original purchase of the car

Key Takeaway
