Zakat on Weak Debts: Imam Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat due on weak debts upon receipt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on zakat for weak debts and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of their disagreement.

Core Idea
A weak debt is not property until received; Sahibayn oblige zakat proportionally upon receipt; Imam Abu Hanifa requires a new year.

In Hanafi fiqh, debts are classified into three categories: strong, medium, and weak. Weak debts, such as mahr or blood money, are considered substitutes for non-property rights. This leads to a dispute within the school on when zakat becomes due on such debts. Let's explore the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Define weak debt and list examples
Identify the seven examples of weak debts given in the text: mahr, bequest, khul' compensation, reconciliation for intentional killing, blood money, kitaba compensation, and sa'aya compensation.
These are substitutes for personal rights, not property.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and rationale
Imam holds that weak debts are not property until possession, so zakat is only due after receiving nisab and completing a new year from the date of receipt.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and rationale
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that zakat is due proportionally upon any receipt of the debt, regardless of amount, and the year is counted from when the debt originated (i.e., when the borrower took possession).
This is analogous to strong debts.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam's view, zakat on weak debts is deferred until sufficient amount and new year; under Sahibayn, zakat is immediate proportionally, even for amounts below nisab.
This affects when and how much zakat is paid.
5
Note the later tarjih
Though the text does not give tarjih, later Hanafi practice often relies on the Sahibayn's view for ease and practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والضعيف وهو بدل ما ليس بمال كالمهر والوصيّة وبدل الخلع والصلح عن دم العمد والديّة وبدل الكتابة والسعاية لا تجب فيه الزكوة ما لم يقبض نصابا ويحول عليه الحول بعد القبض وهذا عند الامام. ترجمه : (۱۱۶۷) ضعیف قرض اس چیز کا بدلہ ہے جو مال نہیں ، جیسے مہر ، وصیت ، بدل خلع کی رقم قتل عمد کے بدلے صلح کی رقم ، یا دیت، یا بدل کتابت ، یا بدل سعایت کی رقم، ان تمام صورتوں میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی جب تک کہ ایک نصاب پر قبضہ نہ کرلے اور قبضہ کے بعد سال نہ گذر جائے ، یہ امام صاحب کا مسلک ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں سات قسم کی چیزیں ہیں جو کسی مال کے بدلے نہیں ہیں، جان کے بدلے میں ہیں، یار قم کا وعدہ ہے اس لئے جب تک مالک کے ہاتھ میں نہ آجائے اس کا مال ہی نہیں ہے، اس لئے اس کے ہاتھ میں آجائے ، اور اس وقت سے ایک سال گزرے، اور نصاب کی مقدار ہوتب زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ واوجبا عن المقبوض من الديون الثلاثة بحسابه مطلقا . (۱۱۶۸) اور صاحبین نے تینوں قرضوں میں مطلقاً اس کے حساب سے زکوۃ واجب کی ہے۔ تشریح : صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ قرض چاہے قوی ہو ، یا اوسط ہو، یا ضعیف ہو، جتنا جتنا قبضہ ہوتا جائے گا اس کی زکوۃ واجب ہوتی جائے گی ، چاہے چالیس درہم سے کم پر قبضہ ہو یا زیادہ پر ، اور جس وقت سے مقروض کے ہاتھ میں مال گیا اسی وقت سے سال گزرنا کافی ہے، قارض کے ہاتھ میں مال آنے کے بعد ضعیف قرض میں سال گزرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
And the weak (debt) is that which is a substitute for what is not property, like mahr, bequest, khul' compensation, reconciliation for intentional killing, blood money, kitaba compensation, and sa'aya compensation — zakat is not obligatory therein until he takes possession of a nisab and a year passes after possession. And this is according to al-Imam. Translation (1167): Weak debt is the substitute for something that is not property, like mahr, bequest, khul' compensation, reconciliation for intentional killing, diyya, kitaba compensation, and sa'aya compensation. In all these cases, zakat is not obligatory until one takes possession of a nisab and a year passes after possession. This is the view of Imam Sahib. Explanation: Here there are seven types of things that are not substitutes for property; they are substitutes for life or a promise of payment, so as long as it does not come into the owner's hand, it is not his property. So when it comes into his hand and a year passes from that time, and it reaches nisab, then zakat becomes obligatory. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) made obligatory upon what is received of the three types of debts proportionally in absolute terms. (1168) And the two Sahibayn have made zakat obligatory on all three debts absolutely proportionally. Explanation: Sahibayn say that whether the debt is strong, medium, or weak, as much as is received, its zakat will become obligatory proportionally, whether possession is of less than forty dirhams or more, and from the time the money went into the hands of the borrower, passing of a year is sufficient; after the money comes into the hands of the lender, a year passing is not necessary.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for weak debts (qard da'if). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on weak debts until a nisab amount is actually received (qabd) and a full year passes after that receipt. The reasoning is that these debts are not property per se; they are substitutes for personal rights (like mahr for marriage, bequest, etc.). As long as the creditor has not taken possession, it is not considered owned wealth capable of growth. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) argue that zakat should be paid proportionally upon receipt of any portion of the debt, regardless of amount, and the year is counted from when the money came into the hands of the borrower (i.e., from the origin of the debt). This means that if someone lends money, the zakat year for that debt starts when the borrower received it, not when the creditor collects it. The text provides both views without explicit tarjih, though in later Hanafi practice, the view of Sahibayn is often relied upon for practicality.

Key Terms
قرض ضعیف (qard da'if): A weak debt that is a substitute for a non-property right (e.g., mahr, bequest, blood money).
مهر (mahr): Dower paid to the wife upon marriage; it is a substitute for the marital right (bud').
بدل الخلع (badl al-khul'): Compensation paid by the wife for khul' divorce; substitute for marital right.
صلح عن دم العمد (sulh 'an dam al-amd): Settlement money paid by the killer to avoid qisas; substitute for the right to retaliation.
دية (diyya): Blood money paid for unintentional killing; substitute for life.
بدل کتابت (badl al-kitaba): Payment by a slave under manumission contract (mukatab) to the master; substitute for freedom.
بدل سعایت (badl al-sa'aya): Payment by a partly freed slave (mudabbar) to the co-owner; substitute for remaining servitude.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does zakat become due on a weak debt like mahr (dower)?
A) Immediately upon the marriage contract
B) When the wife receives any amount of mahr
C) Only after she receives a full nisab and a new year passes after receipt
D) Zakat is never due on mahr

Key Takeaway
Weak debts (qard da'if) require nisab and a new year from receipt for zakat under Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn oblige zakat proportionally upon any receipt, counting the year from the debt's origin.

No Zakat for Past Years on Mal al-Dimar
Ruling on zakat for past years when mal al-dimar is recovered

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for past years when mal al-dimar is recovered and explain the proofs (dalil) supporting this ruling.

Core Idea
Past years' zakat is not due on recovered uncollectible wealth; only the current year after possession matters.

Zakat is generally due on wealth that is in one's possession and capable of growth. But what about assets that were lost or unrecoverable for years? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on hadith and practice. This lesson examines the ruling on mal al-dimar and why past years' zakat is waived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State precisely what the passage says about zakat for past years when mal al-dimar is recovered. Look for the explicit statement.
The ruling is unconditional: no zakat for past years.
2
Understand the Reasoning
Explain why past zakat is not required. Identify the conditions for zakat (possession, growth) and why mal al-dimar fails them.
The key condition is actual control and growth potential.
3
Examine the Proofs
Analyze the two main proofs: the athar of Ibn Umar (distinguishing trustworthy vs. doubtful debts) and the practice of Umar ibn Abdul Aziz (taking only one year's zakat on recovered unjustly seized wealth).
These demonstrate the distinction between accessible and inaccessible wealth.
4
Contrast with Other Views
Note that this ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Consider how other madhabs might differ, especially if they require zakat for past years when recovery was theoretically possible.
The Hanafi position is more lenient due to the strict interpretation of possession.

Source Text

( سنن بیہقی ، باب زكاة الدین اذا کان علی معسر أو جاحد ، ج رابع ، ص ۲۵۳، نمبر ۷۶۲۶ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت عمر ابن عبد العزیز صرف اس سال کی زکوۃ لیتے تھے جس سال ظلم سے لیا ہوا مال واپس آیا ہو، پچھلے سالوں کا نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ مال ضمار کی طرح ہے۔۔ مال ضمار پوشیدہ مال ، جس مال پر اعتماد نہ ہو۔ ترجمه : (۱۱۷۰) جیسے بھاگا ہوا غلام ، اور وہ گم شدہ وغصب کیا ہوا مال جس کے گواہ نہ ہوں، اور وہ مال جو سمندر میں گر گیا، یا میدان میں یا بڑے مکان میں دفن کیا اور اس کی جگہ بھول گیا، یا تاوان میں لیا گیا تھا، یا غیر معروف آدمی کے پاس امانت رکھ دیا گیا ہو، یا ایسا قرض جس پر گواہ نہ ہو۔
And when the wealth of dimar is taken possession of, zakat for past years is not obligatory. And it is like a runaway slave, lost property, usurped property without evidence, and wealth for which zakat is not obligatory. Translation (1169): And when mal al-dimar is taken possession of, zakat for past years is not wajib. Explanation: Such wealth that is out of possession and its recovery is difficult; when it is taken possession of, there is no zakat for past years. After the wealth comes into hand, a full year passes and it reaches nisab, then zakat becomes wajib. Reasons: (1) When the wealth is not in hand and its recovery is impossible, it cannot grow, which is a condition for zakat, so past years' zakat is not wajib. (2) This is proven in this athar: from Ibn Umar, he said: 'Give zakat on what is in your hands, and what is a debt from a trustworthy person is like what is in your hands, and what is a doubtful debt, there is no zakat on it until he takes possession.' (Sunan Bayhaqi, Bab Zakat al-Din...). This athar states that zakat is given on wealth that is with trustworthy people, and for doubtful debt, where there is doubt in recovery, zakat begins after possession. (3) Umar ibn Abdul Aziz wrote concerning wealth that some governors had seized unjustly, ordering it to be returned to its owners and zakat to be taken for past years; then he followed with a letter that only one zakat should be taken because it was dimar. Then Abu Ubayd said: Meaning the absent one that is not hoped for. (Sunan Bayhaqi...) This athar shows that Umar ibn Abdul Aziz only took zakat for the year in which the oppressively seized wealth was returned, not for past years, because it is like mal al-dimar. Mal al-dimar is hidden wealth, on which there is no reliance. Translation (1170): Like a runaway slave, and lost property, and usurped property without evidence, and wealth that fell into the sea, or in a field, or buried in a large house and its location forgotten, or taken as tribute, or placed as an amana with an unknown person, or a debt without witnesses.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage deals with mal al-dimar (lost/hopeless assets), which are assets that are out of reach and unlikely to be recovered. The ruling states that when such assets are eventually recovered, zakat for the past years during which they were inaccessible is not required. Only zakat for the current year (after recovery and a full year in hand) becomes due if the nisab is met. The text provides three proofs: (1) rational reasoning: since the asset was not in hand and could not be grown, the condition for zakat (growth potential) was absent; (2) athar of Ibn Umar: differentiate between trustworthy debt (zakat due) and doubtful debt (no zakat until possession); (3) practice of Umar ibn Abdul Aziz: he ordered zakat only for the year of recovery, not past years. The text also lists examples of mal al-dimar: a runaway slave, lost property, usurped property without witnesses, property lost at sea or buried and forgotten, property taken as tribute, property placed as amana with an unknown person, and a debt without witnesses. These all share the characteristic that they are unlikely to be recovered.

Key Terms
مال الضمار (mal al-dimar): Wealth that is out of reach and unlikely to be recovered, such as lost property, runaway slave, etc.
دين ظنون (dayn zanun): A debt whose collection is doubtful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on zakat for past years when mal al-dimar (like a runaway slave) is recovered?
A) Zakat for all past years must be paid
B) Zakat for only the last year must be paid
C) No zakat for past years is due
D) It depends on the owner's intention

Key Takeaway
Upon recovering mal al-dimar, zakat for past years is not wajib; only zakat for the current year after possession and the passage of a full year becomes due.

Ruling on Missing Wealth (Mal Dhimar) and Zakat
Lists nine cases of mal dhimar and states no past zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for mal dhimar and identify the nine cases where past zakat is not due.

Core Idea
Wealth beyond reach incurs no zakat until it returns to your possession.

Zakat is due on wealth that is in your possession and growing. But what if your wealth is lost, buried, confiscated, or disputed? The Hanafi school addresses this with the concept of mal dhimar. This lesson walks through the nine cases of mal dhimar and the ruling that no zakat is due for past years.

Guided Path
1
Define mal dhimar
Understand that mal dhimar refers to wealth that is lost, inaccessible, or unattainable with no hope of recovery in the foreseeable future.
The term 'dhimar' implies being hidden or missing.
2
List the nine cases from the text
Identify each case mentioned: runaway slave, lost slave, usurped slave without witness, wealth lost at sea, wealth buried and forgotten, wealth confiscated, deposit with unknown person, debt without evidence, and any wealth missing without hope of recovery.
The source lists six explicitly; the commentary adds three more common examples.
3
Extract the ruling
From the text and commentary, note that the Hanafi ruling is: no zakat is due on mal dhimar for past years. Zakat becomes obligatory only from the year the wealth is recovered.
The ruling is based on lack of access (tamakkun) and lack of growth (nama').
4
Understand the rationale
Recognize that zakat is a right on wealth that is both possessed and productive. Mal dhimar fails both conditions: it is not at hand and does not grow.
This is a Hanafi-specific usul principle: al-nama' wa al-tamakkun.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Compare with the Shafi'i position: they obligate zakat for past years upon recovery because ownership remains. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The difference turns on the condition of 'tamakkun' for zakat obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساقط في البحر ومدفون فى مفازة او دار عظيمة وقد نسى مكانه وماخوذ مصادرة ومودع عند من لا يعرفه ودين لا بيّنة عليه
Fallen into the sea, buried in a desert or a large house and its location is forgotten, taken by confiscation, deposited with someone unknown, and a debt without evidence.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage lists cases of 'mal dhimar' (missing or lost wealth). The author presents nine examples: a runaway slave, a lost slave, a slave usurped without witness, wealth lost at sea, wealth buried in a desert or large house and forgotten, wealth confiscated by a ruler with no hope of return, a deposit with an unknown person, and a debt denied by the debtor without evidence. The ruling is that no zakat is due on such wealth for past years because growth is absent and recovery was impossible. Zakat becomes due only after the wealth is recovered, starting from that year.

Key Terms
مال ضمار (mal dhimar): Wealth that is lost, inaccessible, or unattainable, with no hope of recovery in the foreseeable future.
تمكن (tamakkun): Having physical or legal access and control over wealth, enabling its use and growth.
نماء (nama'): Growth or potential for increase; zakat is tied to wealth that yields profit or offspring.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zakat is due for all past years since the wealth was acquired.
B) Zakat is due only for the current year (the year of recovery).
C) Zakat is never due on mal dhimar.
D) Zakat is due only if the wealth was hidden intentionally.

Key Takeaway
Mal dhimar exempts past zakat; only the year of recovery counts.

Zakat on Debt Discharged with Intention
Ruling that discharging a debt with zakat intention after payment is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on discharging a debt with zakat intention after payment and explain why the intention must coincide with the act of giving.

Core Idea
Zakat intention must be made at the time of giving; after-the-fact forgiveness of a loan does not suffice.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a person lends money to a poor person, and later decides to count that loan as zakat. The Hanafi school rules that this does not fulfill the zakat obligation, because the intention (niyyah) was not present when the wealth left the owner's possession. The proof is the famous hadith 'Actions are by intentions.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is discharging a debt (ibra') with zakat intention after the loan was already given. The ruling is that it is not sufficient (la yujzi') and zakat is not fulfilled.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyah' (Sahih al-Bukhari).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith requires intention for actions. Here the action of giving was the loan (without zakat intention), and the later intention cannot retroactively change the character of the earlier transfer.
4
Apply the ruling
If someone wants to pay zakat by forgiving a debt, they must intend zakat at the time of forgiving while the money is still owed, not after.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُجزئ عن الزكوة دين ابرى عنه فقير بنيتها
It is not sufficient for zakat to discharge a debt from a poor person with the intention (of zakat).
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This is a ruling about discharging a debt with the intention of zakat after the fact. The scenario: a person gives money as a loan to a poor person; the money is spent. Later, the lender decides to forgive the debt intending it as zakat. This does not fulfill zakat. The reason is that intention must accompany the act of giving, or at least be present while the wealth is still in the poor person's hand. The proof is the hadith: 'Actions are judged by intentions' from Sahih al-Bukhari, which requires that for acts of worship, intention coincide with the action.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibra'): Discharging or forgiving a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it valid to discharge a debt from a poor person with the intention of zakat if the intention is made after the loan was given?
A) Yes, if the poor person is eligible.
B) Yes, as long as the intention is sincere.
C) No, because intention must be present at the time of the act.
D) No, because debts cannot be discharged with zakat.

Key Takeaway
For zakat, intention must accompany the act of giving; a later intention to count a previous loan as zakat is invalid.

Substituting Goods for Gold/Silver Zakat by Value
Permissibility of giving goods equivalent to zakat value for gold/silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substituting goods for zakat on gold/silver and cite the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Giving goods equivalent to gold/silver zakat value is valid in the Hanafi school.

When a person owes zakat on gold or silver, the Hanafi school allows them to give goods (urud), measured items (makil), or weighed items (mawzun) provided their total value equals the required zakat amount. This ruling is based on a hadith where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) instructed Mu'adh ibn Jabal to collect from each adult a dinar or its equivalent in cloth. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving goods (urud, makil, mawzun) for the zakat of gold/silver. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
The Arabic phrase 'wa-sahha daf'u' indicates validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof is the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet (saw) ordered taking a dinar or its equivalent in cloth.
Reference: Sunan Abi Dawud, Book of Jizyah, no. 3038.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly permits taking an equivalent value from a different category (cloth instead of dinar), indicating that substitution by value is allowed.
The word 'adlahu (its equivalent) is the key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i does not allow giving value; he requires the zakat to be given from the same species (gold/silver).
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the clear text of the hadith and also on istihsan, making this the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح دفع عرض ومكيل وموزون عن زكوة النقدين بالقيمة
It is valid to give goods, dry goods (by measure), and (goods by) weight for the zakat of gold and silver by their value.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This ruling states that it is permissible to give commodities (urud), items sold by measure (makil), or items sold by weight (mawzun) as zakat for gold and silver, provided their total value equals the required amount. For example, if 5 dirhams are due on 200 dirhams, one may give wheat worth 5 dirhams instead of the dirhams. Proof is from a hadith in Abu Dawud where the Prophet ordered Mu'adh to take from each adult a dinar or its equivalent in cloth. Another hadith about Abu Bakr's instruction on zakat camels also supports giving value. The key principle: giving the value is permissible.

Key Terms
عرض (urud): Any commodity or goods, not cash or measure/weight items (here, general goods like utensils).
مكيل (makil): Items sold by measure (e.g., wheat, barley).
موزون (mawzun): Items sold by weight (e.g., salt, iron).
نقدين (naqdayn): Gold and silver (dinar and dirham).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is permissible.
B) No, only dirhams can be given.
C) Yes, but only if the poor person agrees.
D) No, because wheat is not from the same category.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits paying zakat on gold/silver with goods of equivalent value, based on the hadith of Mu'adh.

Weight Standard in Zakat Payment of Gold/Silver
Ruling statement with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that zakat obligation and payment for gold and silver are based on weight, not value, and state the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, zakat on gold and silver is measured by weight for both obligation and payment; market value is irrelevant.

This lesson examines a core Hanafi principle in zakat: that the nisab and payment for gold and silver are determined by weight alone. While many assume market value plays a role, the established position from the Mujtahid Imams is strict adherence to weight, based on the explicit wording of the hadith. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in calculating zakat on jewellery, coins, and utensils.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying zakat on gold/silver. The ruling establishes that weight is the measure both for the obligation (when nisab is reached) and for the payment (when discharging zakat from the same species).
The ruling is that weight, not value, is decisive.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no zakat on less than five awqiyah...' (Bukhari and Muslim). This hadith explicitly uses a weight measure (five awqiyah) for the nisab.
The hadith is sahih but ahad; its transmission is certain (qat'i al-thubut) but its indication (dalala) is zanni.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'five awqiyah' (خمس اواق) directly indicates a weight threshold. The Hanafi school understands this as the defining criterion; no other measure (like value) is mentioned.
Weight is the apparent meaning, and no evidence overrides it.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
Since the dalil is clear and not overridden by istihsan or other proofs, weight remains the only consideration. Thus, zakat becomes wajib only when the weight of gold/silver reaches the nisab, and payment must also be by weight.
This principle is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a person owns silver weighing 150 dirhams but worth 300 dirhams, no zakat is due because the weight is below 200 dirhams. Conversely, if the weight is 220 dirhams but the value is only 100 dirhams, zakat is wajib because weight condition is met.
This protects against market fluctuations and ensures objective measurement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان أدی من عين النقدين فالمعتبر وزنهما اداءً كما اعتبر وجوبا
And if he pays from the same species of the two monies, then their weight is considered in payment just as it is considered in obligation.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage establishes two rules: (1) Zakat becomes obligatory on gold/silver only when their weight reaches the nisab (200 dirhams of silver or 20 mithqals of gold). Market value is irrelevant; even if a silver utensil is worth 200 dirhams but weighs only 150, no zakat is due. (2) When paying zakat from the same species, the payment must be by weight of the metal given, not its value. For example, if 5 dirhams weight of silver is due, one cannot give an item weighting 3 dirhams even if its market value is 5 dirhams. The evidence is the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no zakat on less than five awsuq... less than five awqiyah...' which establishes weight thresholds.

Key Terms
خمس اواق (khams awaq): Five uqiyah, equivalent to 200 silver dirhams by weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person owns a silver utensil weighing 150 dirhams but worth 250 dirhams. Is zakat due on it?
A) Yes, because its value exceeds 200 dirhams.
B) No, because its weight is less than 200 dirhams.
C) Yes, because silver items are exempt from weight consideration.
D) No, because utensils are not zakatable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the nisab and payment of zakat on gold and silver are strictly by weight, not value, based on the hadith of five awqiyah.

Substituting Animals in Zakat with Equivalent Value
Hadith proof for substitution with compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substituting a different category of camel in zakat and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
You may give the value or an equivalent substitute for the prescribed zakat animal, with compensation.

This lesson examines a key hadith that forms the basis for the Hanafi position on giving value (qimah) in zakat. While other schools insist on the exact specified animal, the Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of the Companions, permits substitution with an equivalent plus compensation. Understanding this principle not only clarifies a common misconception but also shows how usul al-fiqh is applied to derive broader rules from specific texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the problem
What is the zakat obligation? A person owes a specific type of camel (jadha'ah) but does not possess it. He has another type (hiqqah).
2
Note the solution in the hadith
The zakat collector accepts the hiqqah along with two sheep or twenty dirhams as compensation.
3
Identify the principle extracted
The commentary states that this proves the permissibility of giving value instead of the exact item.
4
Compare with other madhahib
The Shafi'i school restricts to the exact prescribed animal; the Hanafi school generalizes from the hadith.
5
Apply to modern context
This ruling extends to giving cash value in zakat for other categories (e.g., gold, silver, trade goods).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتُضم قيمة الصدقة التي امر الله رسوله عالم . من بلغت عنده من الابل صدقة الجذعة و ليست عنده جذعة و عنده حقة فانها تقبل منه الحقة و يجعل معها شاتين ان استيسر تا له ، أو عشرين درهما . و من بلغت عنده صدقة الحقة و ليست عنده الحقة و عنده الجذعة فانها تقبل منه الجذعة ، و يعطيه المصدق عشرين درهما أو شاتين
And the value of the sadaqah which Allah commanded His Messenger is considered. Whoever owes a jadha'ah (camel) and does not have it but has a hiqqah, that hiqqah is accepted from him along with two sheep if available, or twenty dirhams. And whoever owes a hiqqah and does not have it but has a jadha'ah, that jadha'ah is accepted from him, and the collector gives him twenty dirhams or two sheep.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage provides the textual proof for the permissibility of substituting value in zakat on livestock. The hadith (from Bukhari and Abu Dawud) describes the case of a person who owes a specific type of camel (jadha'ah) but only possesses a different type (hiqqah). The zakat collector accepts the substitute along with compensation (two sheep or twenty dirhams). Conversely, if a person owes a hiqqah but has a jadha'ah, the collector gives the person compensation. This proves the general principle that one may give the value (or equivalent) of the required zakat item. The commentary extracts the principle: 'کوئی چیز واجب ہو اس کی قیمت لگا کر کوئی دوسری چیز دینا جائز ہے' meaning it is permissible to give the value instead of the exact item.

Key Terms
جذعة (jadha'ah): A young female camel in her fourth year entering her fifth.
حقة (hiqqah): A female camel in her third year entering her fourth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, if a person owes a jadha'ah but only has a hiqqah, what must he do?
A) He must buy a jadha'ah to fulfill zakat.
B) He gives the hiqqah alone without anything extra.
C) He gives the hiqqah along with two sheep or twenty dirhams.
D) He must wait until he acquires a jadha'ah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits substitution of the prescribed zakat animal with an equivalent plus compensation, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Weight Considered in Zakat Payment for Gold and Silver
States ruling that weight is considered in zakat payment for gold and silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that weight is the basis for zakat on gold and silver, apply it to obligation and payment scenarios, and distinguish it from value-based approaches.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold and silver is based on weight, not value — both for obligation and payment.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling in Hanafi zakat law: the obligation and payment of zakat on gold and silver are determined by weight, not market value. This principle, derived from the hadith specifying nisab in 'uqiyas', has practical consequences for how zakat is calculated and discharged. We will explore the evidence, the reasoning, and the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
The passage states that weight is considered in both obligation and payment for gold and silver (al-naqdain). Identify the act (zakat) and the ruling (weight is the criterion).
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
The main evidence is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no zakat on less than five uqiyas of silver.' Note that 'uqiya' is a weight measure.
Hadith in Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith uses a weight term (uqiya) to define nisab, implying that weight is the determinant for both obligation and payment. Consider how this fixes the criterion.
Weight is explicit; value is not mentioned.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school may consider value for certain items (e.g., jewelry), but Hanafi strictly requires weight even for non-coin forms. Understand the practical difference.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply to the Text's Examples
Work through the two examples: (1) a silver vessel weighing 150 dirhams valued at 200 dirhams – no zakat; (2) a debtor owes 5 dirhams but has a vessel worth 5 dirhams weighing 3 dirhams – cannot pay with it.
Emphasize that weight, not value, decides in both cases.

And if he pays from the actual gold and silver, then their weight is considered in payment just as it is considered in obligation. Principle: It is permissible to give another thing by valuing something obligatory. Lexicon: 'arad: goods like utensils etc. 'mawzun': thing weighed by kilo etc., like gold and silver. 'an-naqdain': two, meaning dirham and dinar. Translation: (1173) And if he wants to pay specifically from the gold and silver, then weight will be considered in both, just as weight is considered in zakat obligation. Explanation: There are two issues. [1] Zakat becomes obligatory on dirham and dinar when they reach by weight two hundred dirhams or twenty mithqals of gold. For example, a silver vessel weighs one hundred fifty dirhams but its value is two hundred dirhams, zakat is not obligatory because it is not two hundred dirhams by weight. [2] In payment also, weight is considered, not value. For example, a person owes five dirhams of zakat and has a vessel worth five dirhams but weighing three dirhams, it is not permissible to give it for the five dirhams of zakat because its weight is not five dirhams. Proof: (1) The evidence is in this hadith: I heard Abu Sa‘id al-Khudri said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: There is no zakat on less than five dhud of camels, less than five uqiyas of silver, and less than five awsuq of dates or grain. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that when it is five uqiyas by weight, zakat is obligatory, showing that weight is considered in both obligation and payment, not value. (2) Another hadith states: When you have two hundred dirhams by weight and a year passes, then five dirhams are due, and nothing on gold until...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Thamaratun Najah on zakat for gold and silver. The ruling states that both the obligation and payment of zakat for gold and silver are based on their weight, not their market value. The author explains two practical applications: (1) For obligation, items like a silver vessel must reach the nisab by weight (200 dirhams) even if its value is higher; (2) For payment, a debtor cannot substitute a lighter item of equal value—weight must match. The proof relies on the famous hadith from Abu Sa‘id al-Khudri specifying 'five uqiyas' (200 dirhams) as the nisab, implying weight is the criterion. A second hadith from ‘Ali reinforces that on 200 dirhams, five dirhams are due. The principle is that zakat is on the substance (weight) not on value.

Key Terms
النقدين (an-naqdain): The two: gold (dinar) and silver (dirham). Refers to the two precious metals used as currency.
عرض ('arad): Goods or merchandise, such as utensils, clothes, etc., as opposed to gold/silver or grains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because value is equal
B) No, because weight is less
C) Yes, if the vessel is silver
D) No, because zakat must be paid in coins only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi zakat law, weight is the sole criterion for both obligation and payment of zakat on gold and silver, not market value.

Decrease of Nisab During the Year Does Not Harm
States the Hanafi ruling on nisab continuity for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nisab decrease during the zakat year and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Zakat is due if nisab is complete at both ends of the year; a temporary dip does not break the obligation.

This lesson clarifies a practical ease in zakat: if your wealth dips below nisab mid-year but recovers by year-end, the obligation remains. Hanafi fiqh prioritizes the beginning and end of the lunar year to avoid hardship and complicated calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The text states that a decrease of nisab during the year does not harm. This means that zakat remains wajib if nisab is present at the start and end of the lunar year.
2
Understand the condition
The condition for the ruling is that nisab must be complete at both the beginning and end of the year. A mid-year drop does not matter.
3
Work through the example
The author gives an example: 200 dirhams in Shawwal, drops to 100, then returns to 200 by next Shawwal. Zakat is due.
4
Grasp the rationale
The reason is that requiring nisab throughout would cause hardship (haraj) and complicate calculation. The fiqh principle of ease applies.
This is based on istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٧٥) ونقصان النصاب في الحول لا يضر ان یکون لک عشرون دينارا فاذا كانت لك عشرون دينارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلك (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ، ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۳)
ترجمه : (۱۱۷۵) اور نصاب کا نقصان سال کے اندر مضر نہیں ، اگر سال کے اول و آخر پورا ہو تشریح : مثلا شوال میں دو سو درہم تھے، اور درمیان میں ایک سو ہو گیا، پھر شوال میں دوسو درہم ہو گئے تو اس پر زکوۃ ادا کرنا واجب ہے، کیونکہ زکوۃ کے لئے اول آخر میں نصاب ہونا کافی ہے۔
وجه : درمیان میں بھی نصاب پورا ر ہے اس کی رعایت کرنے میں حرج ہے اور حساب کرنے میں مشکلات ہیں اس لئے اول اور
(1175) And a decrease of nisab during the year does not harm, if you have twenty dinars... Translation: (1175) And a decrease of nisab during the year is not harmful if it is complete at the beginning and end. Explanation: For example, in Shawwal he had two hundred dirhams, then in between it became one hundred, then in Shawwal it became two hundred dirhams again, then zakat payment is obligatory because for zakat it is sufficient to have nisab at the beginning and end. Proof: Because maintaining nisab throughout is difficult and calculating it is problematic, so only the beginning and end are considered.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This ruling from Thamaratun Najah addresses a practical issue in zakat: if a person's wealth drops below nisab during the lunar year but is regained by year-end, the obligation of zakat remains. The author provides an example: someone has 200 dirhams in Shawwal, then it drops to 100, then by the next Shawwal returns to 200; zakat is due. The rationale is that requiring constant nisab throughout the year would cause hardship and complicate calculation. The proof cited (though incomplete in the OCR) is based on ease and istihsan. This is the Hanafi position: only the beginning and end of the year matter for nisab continuity.

Key Terms
نقصان النصاب (nuqsan an-nisab): A temporary decrease in the value or amount of zakatable wealth below the nisab during the lunar year.
الحول (al-hawal): The lunar year as the period for zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Zakat is not due because the nisab was broken
C) Zakat is due only if the drop was less than half
D) Zakat is not due because the wealth was below nisab for more than half the year

Key Takeaway
Zakat remains wajib if nisab is present at both the start and end of the lunar year, regardless of mid-year fluctuations.

Combining Trade Goods with Gold and Silver for Zakat Nisab
Ruling and proofs on combining trade goods value with cash for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining trade goods with gold and silver for zakat nisab and explain the proofs (dalil) used to derive it.

Core Idea
Trade goods are valued, not weighed, and their value is added to gold/silver to complete the zakat nisab.

This passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi zakat law: when a person has trade goods (like inventory for sale) and also possesses gold or silver cash, the value of the goods is added to the cash to determine if the nisab threshold is reached. The ruling is justified through istihsan and supported by multiple hadith that show value substitution in zakat. We will explore the ruling, its practical application, and the proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage to find the exact ruling: trade goods are combined with gold and silver by value, not by weight.
2
Examine the example
The author gives an example: trade goods worth 100 dirhams plus 100 dirhams cash make 200 dirhams total, triggering zakat.
Nisab for silver is 200 dirhams.
3
Analyze the first proof
The hadith of Abu Bakr shows that when the exact zakat animal is missing, its value can be substituted with sheep or dirhams.
This establishes the principle of value substitution in zakat.
4
Analyze the second proof
The hadith of Mu'adh allows taking a dinar or its equivalent in cloth, again supporting value equivalence.
5
Analyze the third proof
The statement of Makhul (a Tabi'i) explicitly says gold and silver are combined for zakat, including the value of a sword.
This is a qawl sahabi / tabi'i supporting the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
۲۶۸
كتاب الزكوة
الـعروض الى الثمنين والذهب الى الفضة قيمة . (۱۱۷۵) ونقصان النصاب في الحول لا يضر ان یکون لک عشرون دينارا فاذا كانت لك عشرون دينارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلك (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ، ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۵۷۳)
ترجمه : (۱۱۷۴) اور سامان کی قیمت منین یعنی سونا اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملائی جائے گی ۔ تشریح : سامان کو اگر سونا اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملانا ہو تو وزن کے اعتبار سے نہیں ملا سکتا، اس لئے اس کی قیمت لگا کر ہی ملائے گا ، مثلا ایک آدمی کے پاس سامان تجارت ہے، اس کی قیمت ایک سو درہم ہے، اور ایک سو درہم نقد ہے، تو سامان تجارت کی قیمت کو نقد کے ساتھ ملا کر دوسو درہم ہو گئے اس لئے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔
صلى الله
وجه: (1) ان ابا بكر كتب له فريضة الصدقة التي امر الله رسوله ا . من بلغت عنده من الابل صدقة الجذعة و ليست عنده جذعة و عنده حقة فانها تقبل منه الحقة و يجعل معها شاتين ان استيسر تا له ، أو عشرين درهما . و من بلغت عنده صدقة الحقة و ليست عنده الحقة وعنده الجذعة فانها تقبل منه الجذعة ، و يعطيه المصدق عشرين درهما أو شاتين (بخاری شریف ، باب من بلغت عنده صدقته بنت مخاض ولیست عنده ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۱۴۵۳ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب زکوۃ السائمۃ ص ۲۲۵ نمبر ۱۵۶۷ء) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مالک پر جذعہ واجب ہو اور وہ اس کے پاس نہ ہو تو حقہ دے دے اور نہیں درہم بھی دے دے۔ اور حقہ واجب تھا اور اس کے پاس جذعہ ہے تو جذعہ دے دے اور مصدق سے ہیں درہم لے لے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ میں سامان کی قیمت دے دے تب بھی جائز ہے۔ (۲) عن ابى وائل عن معاذ ان النبي الله لما وجهه الى اليمن امره ان ياخذ من كل حالم يعني محتلما دينارا او عدله من المعافرى ثياب تكون باليمن - ابوداود شریف ، باب اخذا الجزية ، ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۳۰۳۸) اس حدیث میں دینار کے بدلے کپڑا لینے کے لئے کہا گیا ۔(۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ سونے کو چاندی کے ساتھ ملا کر زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ قلت لمكحول : یا ابا عبد الله ان لي سيفا فيه خمسون و مائة درهم فهل على فيه زكاة ؟ قال اضف اليه ما كان لك من ذهب و فضة فاذا بلغ مانتی درهم ذهب وفضة فعليك فيه الزكاة . (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب ۸، في الرجل تكون عنده مائة درهم وعشرة دنا نیر ، ج ثانی ،ص ۳۵۸، نمبر ۹۸۸۵) یہاں سونے کو چاندی کے ساتھ ملا کر زکوۃ دینے کے لئے کہا گیا ہے۔
Trade goods are [valued] in terms of silver and gold by value. (1175) Deficiency of nisab during the year does not harm: if you have twenty dinars and a year passes, then half a dinar is due; for increase, proportionate. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Zakat al-Saima, p. 233, no. 1573) Translation: (1174) And the value of goods is combined with silver and gold. Explanation: If goods are to be combined with gold and silver, they cannot be combined by weight; rather, their value must be assessed. For example, a person has trade goods worth one hundred dirhams, and one hundred dirhams cash; then the value of the trade goods is added to the cash, making two hundred dirhams, so zakat becomes obligatory. Proof: (1) Abu Bakr wrote the ordinance of charity that Allah commanded His Messenger: whoever among camels reaches the age of jadha'a but does not have it, and has a hiqqa, then the hiqqa is accepted from him, and he gives two sheep if they are available, or twenty dirhams. And whoever reaches the zakat of hiqqa and does not have hiqqa but has jadha'a, then jadha'a is accepted from him, and the zakat collector gives him twenty dirhams or two sheep. (Bukhari, Bab man balaghat indahu sadaqatuhu bint makhadin wa laysat indahu, p. 195, no. 1453; Abu Dawud, Bab zakat al-sa'imah, p. 225, no. 1567) This hadith indicates that when jadha'a is obligatory and the owner does not have it, he may give hiqqa plus twenty dirhams. And when hiqqa was obligatory and he has jadha'a, he gives jadha'a and takes twenty dirhams from the collector, showing that paying the value in zakat is permissible. (2) From Abu Wa'il from Mu'adh that the Prophet, when he sent him to Yemen, ordered him to take from every adult (meaning a mature person) a dinar or its equivalent from the Yemeni garments called ma'afir. (Abu Dawud, Bab akhdh al-jizyah, p. 445, no. 3038) This hadith commands taking cloth in place of a dinar. (3) In the saying of a Tabi'i: gold and silver are combined for zakat. I said to Makhul: 'O Abu Abdillah, I have a sword worth one hundred and fifty dirhams, is there zakat on it?' He said: 'Add to it whatever gold and silver you have; if it reaches two hundred dirhams of gold and silver, then zakat is due.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab 8, fi al-rajul takunu indahu mi'atu dirham wa 'asharat dananir, vol. 2, p. 358, no. 9885) Here gold and silver are combined for zakat.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on combining trade goods with gold and silver for the purpose of completing the zakat nisab. The author states the basic rule: trade goods ('urud) are valued in terms of the two precious metals (gold and silver) – meaning their market value is considered, not their weight. This is because trade goods are diverse and cannot be weighed directly against gold/silver. The ruling is numbered (1175) in the text, though the Urdu translation labels it (1174), possibly a numbering discrepancy. The commentary provides a clear example: if a person has trade goods worth 100 dirhams and also has 100 dirhams cash, the values are added together; if the total reaches 200 dirhams (the nisab for silver), zakat becomes obligatory. The proof section adduces three evidences. First, a hadith from Abu Bakr's letter on zakat of camels: when an animal of a higher age is due but not available, the owner may give a lower age plus compensation (two sheep or twenty dirhams), proving that value can substitute in zakat. Second, a hadith from Mu'adh that the Prophet allowed collecting a dinar or its equivalent in cloth, again showing value substitution. Third, a statement of the Tabi'i Makhul: he advised combining gold and silver to reach the nisab, including the value of a sword. Together, these proofs establish the Hanafi position that trade goods are added by value, not weight, and that combining gold and silver (the two nisab currencies) is valid for completing nisab.

Key Terms
العروض (al-'urud): Trade goods: items purchased for resale, excluding gold and silver (cash).
الثمنين (al-thamanayn): The two price measures: gold and silver (i.e., currency).
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how are trade goods combined with gold and silver for zakat?
A) By weight, because gold and silver are weighed.
B) By value, because trade goods cannot be weighed.
C) They are not combined at all.
D) Only if both are in the same physical form.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, trade goods are valued and added to gold/silver to complete the zakat nisab, based on the principle of value substitution from prophetic precedent.

Nisab Deficiency Mid-Year: Only Start and End Matter
Ruling that nisab need only be present at start and end of zakat year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that zakat is due if nisab is present at both the beginning and end of the lunar year, and differentiate it from the scenario where nisab is only attained at year-end.

Core Idea
Zakat is due if nisab exists at start and end; mid-year dips are ignored.

A common practical question is whether a person must pay zakat if their wealth falls below the nisab during the year and then recovers. The Hanafi school, based on ease and istihsan, holds that only the state at the beginning and end of the lunar year matters. This lesson explains that rule and a related scenario involving new trade goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving zakat (wajib). The condition that triggers obligation is possession of nisab at the start and end of the hawl.
The ruling is clear: if nisab exists at both boundaries, zakat is due regardless of mid-year fluctuations.
2
Understand the reasoning (istihsan)
The proof is based on hardship: requiring continuous nisab throughout the year would cause difficulty and complex calculations. The law eases this by only considering start and end.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) of istihsan, not a textual proof.
3
Apply to the example
Example from text: Had 200 dirhams in Shawwal, dropped to 100 mid-year, returned to 200 in next Shawwal. Zakat is wajib because start and end are complete.
If the dip had continued to the end, no zakat.
4
Distinguish the second scenario
For new trade goods purchased with no other wealth, if their value only reaches nisab at the end of the year, the hawl starts from that point, so zakat is due in the following year, not the current one.
This is because the hawl begins only when full nisab is owned.

Translation: (1175) And the deficiency of nisab during the year does not harm, if the year's beginning and end are complete. Explanation: For example, in Shawwal he had two hundred dirhams, then mid-year it became one hundred, then in Shawwal it became two hundred again; then zakat is obligatory, because for zakat it is sufficient to have nisab at the beginning and end. Proof: Because observing the nisab throughout the middle is burdensome and calculating it is difficult; therefore, having it complete at the beginning and end suffices.

Explanation: He bought trade goods whose value is not yet two hundred dirhams, and he has no other trade goods to combine to complete the nisab; therefore the zakat year has not started. At the end of the year its value reaches two hundred dirhams; now he becomes owner of the nisab, and the zakat year starts from that time; zakat will be obligatory next year. Proof: Because for the commencement of the zakat year, complete nisab at the start is necessary.

(2) Another hadith states that two hundred dirhams or twenty dinars trigger zakat. Commentary
This passage contains three distinct rulings, presented sequentially. The first ruling (numbered 1175 in translation) addresses a practical concern: if a person's wealth dips below the nisab during the zakat year but returns to nisab by year-end, their zakat obligation remains intact. The author argues by way of istihsan: requiring continuous nisab throughout the year would impose hardship and complex calculations. Therefore, only the beginning and end of the year matter. This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) based on ease. The second ruling (1176) clarifies a related scenario: if a person acquires trade goods that initially do not reach nisab, and the value only reaches nisab at the end of the year, zakat is not due for that year. The reason is that the year starts only when full nisab is possessed; the nisab at the end does not retroactively start the year. The third ruling (1177) defines the nisab thresholds for gold and silver: 20 mithqal for gold (i.e., 20 dinars, since one dinar equals one mithqal) and 200 dirhams for silver, where each dirham weighs 0.7 mithqal (so total 140 mithqal of silver). The proof cites two hadith: one from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri establishing nisab for silver at five uqiyas (200 dirhams), and another from Ali specifying 200 dirhams or 20 dinars. The passage thus establishes foundational zakat rules with practical examples and authentic Prophetic evidence.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that obligates zakat; for silver 200 dirhams, for gold 20 mithqal.
حول (hawl): The lunar year that must pass for zakat to become due; the start of the year is when full nisab is possessed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Only start and end nisab matter for existing wealth; new assets start their own hawl when nisab is first attained.

The Nisab of Gold and Silver
Definition of nisab for gold and silver with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi nisab for gold (20 mithqal) and silver (200 dirhams of 0.7 mithqal each) and explain the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Gold nisab = 20 mithqal; silver nisab = 200 dirhams of specified weight.

Zakat is only obligatory on wealth that reaches a minimum threshold known as nisab. This lesson defines the nisab for gold and silver according to the Hanafi school, based on explicit Prophetic hadith. Understanding these amounts is essential for correctly calculating zakat.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the nisab values
Gold: 20 mithqal (20 dinars, each dinar = 1 mithqal). Silver: 200 dirhams, where each dirham weighs 0.7 mithqal (total 140 mithqal).
Modern grams: gold ~85g, silver ~595g (using 1 mithqal = 4.25g).
2
Understand the weight relationship
One dirham = 0.7 mithqal, so 200 dirhams = 140 mithqal of silver. One dinar = 1 mithqal of gold.
This is the standard Hanafi measurement.
3
Identify the hadith evidence
The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri states: no zakat on less than five uqiyas (200 dirhams). The hadith from Ali specifies 200 dirhams or 20 dinars as triggering zakat.
These hadith are the primary textual proofs for the nisab thresholds.
4
Apply the rule
If someone has 15 mithqal of gold, no zakat. If they have 30 mithqal, zakat is due on the excess (and the nisab is covered).
Zakat is on the entire amount once nisab is reached.

Source Text

D) 100 mithqal

Key Takeaway
The nisab for gold is 20 mithqal and for silver is 200 dirhams (140 mithqal), established by authentic hadith.

Zakat on Trade Goods: Nisab at Start of Year Required
Ruling that missing nisab at beginning prevents zakat obligation for that year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that nisab must be present at both the beginning and end of the lunar year for zakat on trade goods to be obligatory, and apply it to determine when the zakat year begins.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods requires nisab at both the start and end of the year.

Zakat on trade goods ('arḍ tijāra) is a significant obligation for Muslim merchants. One common confusion is whether the value of goods must reach the nisab at any point during the year or precisely at the start and end. This passage from the Hanafi matn clarifies that the zakat year does not even begin unless the nisab is complete at the outset. Let us walk through the reasoning so you can confidently determine when zakat becomes due on your own trade assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is owning trade goods ('arḍ tijāra). The ruling is that zakat is not obligatory (lā tajibu zakātuhu) for that particular year. This is a negative ruling – no obligation arises.
The ruling here is absence of obligation, not prohibition.
2
Identify the condition that triggers the obligation
The zakat year is defined by the lunar calendar. For obligation to arise, the owner must possess a nisab (minimum threshold) at the very beginning of the year. In this scenario, the owner had no other wealth and the goods initially did not reach nisab, so the year never started.
Hanafi school: nisab is assessed at the beginning and end of the year, not continuously.
3
Examine the consequence of missing the condition
Because the nisab was absent at the start, the entire year is invalid for zakat. Even though the value later reaches nisab, no zakat is due for that year. Instead, a new year begins from the moment nisab is achieved.
This differs from some other schools which may calculate zakat on the increase during the year.
4
Apply the rule to determine timing
If at the end of the year the value reaches nisab, but it was not at the start, then the owner must start counting a fresh year from that day. Zakat will be due after a full lunar year from that point, provided nisab is maintained at both ends of that new year.
This ensures the year is complete with nisab present at its boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تملك عرضا بنية التجارة وهو لا يساوى نصابا وليس له غيره ثم بلغت قيمته نصابا في آخر الحول لا تجب زكوته لذلك الحول
If one owns a commodity with the intention of trade, and it is not equal to the nisab, and he has no other [wealth], then its value reaches nisab at the end of the year, its zakat is not obligatory for that year.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school on zakat for trade goods. The key condition for zakat obligation is that the nisab must be complete at the beginning and end of the lunar year. If at the beginning of the year the trade goods do not reach the nisab, the zakat year does not start. Even if the value later rises to nisab before the year ends, no zakat is due for that year because the year was not initiated with a complete nisab. Instead, the year begins from the moment nisab is reached, and zakat will be due after a full year from that point.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.
عرض تجارة ('arḍ tijāra): A commodity owned with the intention of trade for profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zakat is obligatory for that year
B) Zakat is not obligatory for that year
C) Zakat is obligatory only on the increase
D) Zakat is obligatory if the owner intended trade

Key Takeaway
Zakat on trade goods requires the nisab to be present at both the beginning and the end of the lunar year; otherwise, no zakat is due for that year and a new year starts when nisab is first achieved.

Nisab of Gold and Silver in Zakat: Fixed Weights from Hadith
Definition of nisab amounts for gold and silver with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab amounts for gold (20 mithqal) and silver (200 dirhams) and explain the hadith evidence that establishes them.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold and silver is due upon reaching fixed weight thresholds: 20 mithqal gold and 200 dirhams silver.

This lesson defines the nisab thresholds for zakat on gold and silver as specified by the Hanafi school through authentic hadith. You will learn the exact weights, their historical basis, and the 2.5% rate that applies once nisab is reached and a lunar year passes.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the nisab amounts
From the text, gold nisab is 20 mithqal (or 20 dinars) and silver nisab is 200 dirhams (each dirham weighing 7/10 mithqal).
One mithqal ≈ 4.374g (Hanafi).
2
Understand the weight conversion
The dirham is defined as 0.7 mithqal, so 200 dirhams = 140 mithqal (≈ 612.36g silver).
This standard was set by Caliph Umar.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (RA) establishes that no zakat is due on less than five uqiyas (200 dirhams). The hadith of Ali (RA) specifies the rate: 2.5% (half a dinar on 20 dinars, 5 dirhams on 200 dirhams).
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qat'i dalala).
4
Apply the rate
Once nisab is reached and a lunar year passes, zakat of 2.5% is due on the excess as well, calculated proportionally.
The phrase 'fama zad fa bihisab dhalik' in the hadith indicates this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصاب الذهب عشرون مثقالا ونصاب الفضة مائتا درهم من الدراهم التي كل عشرة منها وزن سبعة مثاقيل سمعت ابا سعيد الخدرى قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليس فيما دون خمس ذود صدقة من الابل، وليس فيما دون خمس اواق صدقة، وليس فيما دون خمسة اوسق صدقة عن علي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ببعض اول الحديث قال فاذا كانت لك مائتا درهم و حال عليه الحول ففيها خمسة دراهم وليس عليك شيء يعني في الذهب حتى يكون لك عشرون دينارا فاذا كانت لك عشرون دينارا و حال عليه الحول ففيها نصف دينار فما زاد فبحساب ذلك
The nisab of gold is twenty mithqal, and the nisab of silver is two hundred dirhams from those dirhams of which every ten has the weight of seven mithqal. I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no charity (zakat) for less than five camels, and there is no charity for less than five uqiyas (200 dirhams), and there is no charity for less than five wasqs.' And from Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding part of the beginning of the hadith: 'When you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes over them, then five dirhams are due; and nothing is due from you regarding gold until you have twenty dinars; when you have twenty dinars and a year passes over them, then half a dinar is due; and for any excess, calculate accordingly.'
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage defines the nisab thresholds for zakat on gold and silver as per the Hanafi school. The nisab for gold is twenty mithqal (equivalent to twenty dinars, since one dinar equals one mithqal). For silver, it is two hundred dirhams, but the dirhams referred to are those weighing seven mithqal per ten dirhams—the standard weight established by Caliph Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). The passage provides hadith evidence: the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri establishes that zakat is not due on less than five uqiyas (two hundred dirhams) of silver, and the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) specifies the exact rates: for two hundred dirhams, five dirhams (2.5%), and for twenty dinars, half a dinar (also 2.5%). This confirms that zakat is 2.5% on both gold and silver once they reach nisab and a full lunar year passes.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqāl): A unit of weight used for gold; one mithqal equals the weight of one dinar (approximately 4.374 grams in the Hanafi school).
درهم (dirham): A unit of weight for silver; the standard dirham used for nisab weighs 0.7 mithqal (approx. 3.06g).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 20 mithqal
C) 5 mithqal
D) 200 mithqal

Key Takeaway
The nisab for gold is 20 mithqal and for silver 200 dirhams, each with a 2.5% zakat rate after a lunar year.

Calculating Zakat on Gold and Silver
Practical calculation guide for zakat on gold and silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate zakat on gold and silver using Hanafi nisab values and the proportional rule for amounts below full nisab.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold/silver is 2.5% (1/40) of the nisab or fraction thereof if owned amount reaches one-fifth of nisab.

Zakat on gold and silver is a wajib obligation when your holdings reach the nisab threshold. This lesson unpacks the practical calculation method used in the South Asian tradition, defining precise weights for the dinar and dirham, and showing how to compute zakat for full and fractional nisab amounts. Pay careful attention to the rate: the text says '40%' but arithmetic reveals it means 1/40 (2.5%).

Guided Path
1
Memorize the nisab weights
Identify the weights given for one dinar (gold coin) and one dirham (silver coin), then compute the full nisab for gold (20 dinars) and silver (200 dirhams) in grams and tola.
Gold: 1 dinar = 4.374g; nisab = 87.48g. Silver: 1 dirham = 3.0618g; nisab = 612.36g.
2
Apply the one-fifth rule
If your holding is less than the full nisab but equal to or more than one-fifth of the nisab (4 dinars gold or 40 dirhams silver), zakat is due proportionally. If below one-fifth, no zakat.
Source text: 'Whatever exceeds the nisab and reaches one-fifth of it, then according to its calculation, its zakat will be due.'
3
Calculate zakat at the correct rate
The zakat rate is 1/40 of the owned amount (dividing by 40 gives zakat). The text writes '40%' but the arithmetic consistently uses division by 40 (e.g., 20 dinars ÷ 40 = 0.5 dinar).
Do not multiply by 0.4; the intended rate is 2.5% (1/40).
4
Convert to currency (optional)
If you need to pay in cash, determine the current market value of the gold/silver weight due as zakat and exchange into currency (rupees, dollars, etc.).
The source mentions converting to rupees, pounds, or dollars.

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah is a practical guide for calculating zakat on gold and silver. It begins by stating the weight of one dinar (a gold coin) as 4.374 grams, and the gold nisab as 20 dinars (87.48 grams). The author then calculates zakat as 40% (likely meaning 1/40, or 2.5%, but the text explicitly says 40%). The text provides equivalent weights in tola, a traditional South Asian unit. For silver, one dirham is defined as 3.0618 grams, and the silver nisab is 200 dirhams (612.36 grams). Zakat on silver is also stated as 40% of the nisab. The passage includes examples: for the full gold nisab, zakat is half a dinar (0.5) or 0.1875 tola; for silver nisab, zakat is 5 dirhams. It also calculates zakat for fractional holdings: e.g., 4 dinars (less than nisab) still gets zakat at 40%? Actually, the text says for 4 dinars, zakat is 0.1 dinar, implying that if the holding reaches 1/5 of nisab (4 dinars is 1/5 of 20), zakat is due proportionally. This is clarified in the note and the translation of a hadith (or text) at the end: 'Whatever exceeds the nisab and reaches one-fifth of it, then according to its calculation, its zakat will be due.' So the passage teaches that zakat on gold and silver is calculated at the rate of 1/40 (though written as 40%) of the total, but if the owned amount is less than the full nisab but at least one-fifth of it, zakat is due proportionally. The text also mentions that one can convert the gold/silver to currency for valuation.

Key Terms
دینار (dinar): A gold coin; its weight in this text is 4.374 grams (0.375 tola).
درہم (dirham): A silver coin; its weight in this text is 3.0618 grams (0.2625 tola).
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.
زکوۃ (zakah): Obligatory charity; here calculated at 40% (but arithmetically 1/40 or 2.5%).
تولہ (tola): A traditional weight; 1 tola = 11.6638 grams, used in the South Asian context.
مثقال (mithqal): A weight of gold; 1 mithqal = 4.374 grams; used for gold nisab.

Weights for Gold Zakat: Dinar, Mithqal, and Calculation
Defining the weight of dinar and dirham and calculating zakat on gold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the weight of one Islamic dinar in grams and tola, calculate the nisab for gold, and compute zakat due on any quantity of gold.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold is wajib at 2.5% on a nisab of 20 dinars (87.48g).

This lesson establishes the authoritative Hanafi weights for the gold dinar and dirham, which are essential for correctly calculating zakat. You will learn the exact weight of one dinar, the nisab threshold, and how to apply the 2.5% rate to any amount of gold. This is a foundational reference for every Muslim who owns gold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the weight of one dinar
The passage states that one dinar equals one mithqal, which is 0.375 tola or 4.374 grams. Memorize this equivalent.
These are the standard Hanafi weights; other schools may use slightly different values.
2
Determine the nisab for gold
The nisab is 20 dinars. Using the weight of one dinar, calculate: 20 dinars = 20 mithqal = 7.5 tola = 87.48 grams.
The nisab is a condition (shart) for the obligation of zakat.
3
Recall the zakat rate
Zakat on gold is one-fortieth (1/40) or 2.5%. This is derived from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The rate is fixed and does not change with market value.
4
Calculate zakat on full nisab
For 20 dinars, zakat = 20 × 1/40 = 0.5 dinar. In weight: 7.5 tola × 1/40 = 0.1875 tola; 87.48g × 1/40 = 2.187g.
The passage provides these exact figures.
5
Calculate zakat on lesser amounts
For gold below nisab, the calculation method is the same but zakat is not wajib unless the nisab is reached. The passage gives an example: 4 dinars → zakat = 4 × 1/40 = 0.1 dinar = 0.0375 tola = 0.4374g.
This is for illustration; practical zakat is only due when nisab is met and a full year passes.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ۲ دینار کا وزن کتنا ہو گا اس کو دیکھیں کتنادر هم اس کا وزن کتنا ہوتا ہے ایک دینار کا وزن ایک مثقال ہوتا ہے ایک دینار کا وزن 0.375 تولہ سونا ہوتا ہے ایک دینار کا وزن 4.374 گرام سونا ہوتا ہے 20 دینار کا وزن 20 مثقال سونا ہوتا ہے 20 دینار کا وزن 7.5 تولہ سونا ہوتا ہے 20 دینار کا وزن 87.48 گرام سونا ہوتا ہے سونے کی زکوۃ کتنی نکلے گی کتنے دینار میں کتنی فی صد کتنی زکوۃ نکلے گی 20 دینار سونے میں زکوۃ 40 فیصد 0.5۔آدھا دینار سونا نکلے گا 7.5 تولہ سونے میں زکوۃ 40 فیصد 0.1875 تولہ سونا نکلے گا 87.48 گرام سونے میں زکوۃ 40 فیصد 2.187 گرام سونا نکلے گا کتنے دینار میں کتنی فی صد کتنی زکوۃ نکلے گی 4 دینار سونے میں زکوۃ 40 فیصد 0.1 دینا ر سونا نکلے گا۔ 1.5 تولہ سونے میں زکوۃ 40 فیصد 0.0375 تولہ سونا نکلے گا 17.496 گرام سونے میں زکوۃ 40 فیصد 0.4374 گرام سونا نکلے گا ۔ اب اس کی قیمت لگانا چاہیں تو روپیہ یا پونڈ ، یا ڈالر سے اس کی قیمت لگالیں۔ نوٹ : او پر حساب میں 0.1 دینارز کوۃ ہے، اس کا مطلب ہے کہ ایک دینار کے دسویں حصے میں سے ایک حصہ زکوۃ ہوگی ۔ ۔ ہمیشہ اوپر کوہ کہ حصہ ہوگی۔ ۔ زکوۃ 40 فیصد ہوتی ہے اس لئے ہمیشہ 40 سے تقسیم دیں تو زکوۃ کی رقم نکل جائے گی۔
Fruit of Salvation Volume 2. How much is the weight of a dinar? Look. How many dirhams? How much is its weight? One dinar weighs one mithqal. One dinar weighs 0.375 tola of gold. One dinar weighs 4.374 grams of gold. 20 dinars weigh 20 mithqals of gold. 20 dinars weigh 7.5 tolas of gold. 20 dinars weigh 87.48 grams of gold. How much zakat on gold will be given? In how many dinars? What percentage? How much zakat? In 20 dinars of gold, zakat at 1/40 (2.5%): half a dinar of gold will be given. In 7.5 tolas of gold, zakat at 1/40: 0.1875 tola of gold will be given. In 87.48 grams of gold, zakat at 1/40: 2.187 grams of gold will be given. In how many dinars? What percentage? How much zakat? In 4 dinars of gold, zakat at 1/40: 0.1 dinar of gold will be given. In 1.5 tolas of gold, zakat at 1/40: 0.0375 tola of gold will be given. In 17.496 grams of gold, zakat at 1/40: 0.4374 grams of gold will be given. Now if you want to value it, value it in rupees or pounds or dollars. Note: In the above calculation, 0.1 dinar is zakat. It means that one part out of ten parts of a dinar is zakat. Always the upper part is the portion. Zakat is 1/40, so always divide by 40 to get the zakat amount.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage provides the standard weights for the gold nisab in classical and modern units. It establishes that one Islamic dinar equals one mithqal, which is approximately 0.375 tola or 4.374 grams. The nisab for gold is 20 dinars (7.5 tolas). Zakat is one-fortieth (2.5%) of the gold when it reaches the nisab. The passage also shows how to calculate zakat on lesser amounts proportionally. It guides the reader to value the gold in local currency if needed. This serves as a practical reference for fulfilling the zakat obligation correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
دینار (dinar): A gold coin used as a unit of weight and currency; its weight is one mithqal.
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight equal to one dinar.
زکوۃ (zakah): The obligatory charity due on wealth that reaches the nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the weight of one Islamic dinar in grams according to this passage?
A) 4.374 grams
B) 4.5 grams
C) 3.75 grams
D) 5 grams

Key Takeaway
The nisab for gold zakat is 20 dinars (7.5 tola or 87.48g) and the rate is 2.5% (1/40), all based on weight, not market value.
